# Relativistic ISP Roadmap V3: Toward Interacting Dynamics, Continuum QFT, and Non-Abelian Gauge Theory

Author: Felix Robles Elvira

Date: 2026-05-13

Updated: 2026-05-18 after V3 Papers 1-10: the roadmap now separates
Gamma-only stochastic data, operational instruments, enriched Wilson/no-Wilson
QFT matching, restricted foliation independence, the Paper-8 QFT
reconstruction/no-go gate, and the Paper-9 finite non-Abelian gauge benchmark.
Paper 10 adds a Peter-Weyl finite-battery `SU(2)` projective gauge layer.
Full signed metric, full QFT reconstruction, and continuum Yang-Mills remain
enriched or open targets rather than Gamma-only consequences.

Updated: 2026-05-23 after the Paper 8--12 and Paper 20 source audits:
Papers 8--10 now explicitly separate finite/projective records from continuum
QFT or continuum Yang-Mills construction. Paper 11 exports RG residual and
trajectory ledgers, not the Paper-20 `SEL2` coefficient-time source. Paper 12
exports renormalized Wilson-loop readout control, not the `SEL2`
block-plaquette tree-rate source. Paper 20 therefore parks
`P20-SEL2-TREE-RATE-GATE` as the active remaining source obstruction.

Updated: 2026-05-23 after the Paper-20 endpoint pass: Paper 20 is frozen as
a completed reduction and obstruction ledger. V3 Paper 21 is now the dedicated
`SEL2` tree-rate source-or-falsification paper. The global synthesis role is
postponed so it is not mixed with the active source campaign.

Updated: 2026-05-24 after the Paper-21 source audit and the Paper-22 Work-I--III
closure: Paper 21 is frozen as a finite source-table reduction and obstruction
ledger, not a synthesis paper. Paper 22 has closed common inverse/admissibility,
`CMPSRC+`, the licensed pass graph, and finite-depth reduced-tail closure on the
strict row-complete envelope branch. The active obstruction returns to
`P20-SEL2-TREE-RATE-GATE` and the associated surface prefactor comparison.
Paper 22 Section 15 freezes this gate as a scalar worksheet: `TREE-TIME` is
the selector-time trichotomy, while `ESC-MASS` is exposed as a near-maximal
same-record anti-concentration problem rather than a small positive
escape-mass problem. Section 16 then makes the escape side executable by
introducing the cofinal escape-ceiling functional
`\mathcal E_{\rho}^{cof,SEL2}`; `ESC-MASS` is now exactly the strict
inequality `\mathcal E_{\rho}^{cof,SEL2}>\Theta_{esc}`.

Updated: 2026-05-25 after the Paper-22 A/B/C branch audit: Paper 22 is now
frozen as a completed continuation/source-audit ledger. It falsifies the
strict \(F_4\) escape branch, reduces Branch A to fixed or adaptive prefactor
source gates, parks Branch B behind a new positive full-support surface theorem,
and parks Branch C behind a new signed/selector exact-anchor package. Paper 23
is therefore not a synthesis paper. It is the adaptive Branch-A source campaign:
prove or falsify the large-\(N\), high-\(\alpha\), same-record package
`XIPLOG+AREA+RPCOV/RPF`.

Updated: 2026-05-25 after Paper 23 Section 57: Paper 23 is frozen as the
adaptive Branch-A reduction and current-corpus falsification ledger. The next
paper is not another bookkeeping audit. Paper 24 is the full-object RPF
dual-certificate campaign: either print a same-law certificate for the full
normalized minimal-edge Hamiltonian, or print a same-law witness showing that
the closed Paper-23 scalar body cannot certify the required range.

Updated: 2026-05-25 after Paper 24: Paper 24 is completed as a negative
certificate-body theorem.  The full-object finite-dual certificate format is
sound and would close adaptive Branch A, but the closed Paper-23 body
\({\mathcal M}_{56}\) remains too large in the nontrivial live RPF case:
residual full-mixed directions give same-law witnesses against closing
universal certificates.  The next positive proof must add new actual-law
scalar information, source a Peter-Weyl tail, prove bridge damping, prove
screened conditional influence/Dobrushin, or return to Branch B/C.

Updated: 2026-05-25 after Paper 25: Paper 25 is completed as the Branch-A
actual-law source and truth-status audit.  It is not a summary.  It proves
the exact positive closure chain for five Branch-A routes: direct cofinal
Dobrushin rows, screened conditional shells, Peter-Weyl step contraction,
Peter-Weyl tail/projection control, and actual-law bridge damping.  It also
proves that the current Papers 20--24 supply none of those five sources, do
not supply the lower-floor theorem needed to falsify adaptive Branch A, and
do not decide the actual truth value of any of the five options.  The next
positive proof, if it stays in Branch A, must be genuinely new actual-law
numerical, screening, spectral, tail, or bridge information.

Updated: 2026-05-25 after Paper 26: Paper 26 is completed as the actual-law
finite-template data extraction, atom-value source, residual-source ledger,
`SEL2` RN-ratio bypass audit, minimal-edge RN-ratio attempt, RN-MIXAMP value
campaign, and evaluation campaign.  It is not a summary.  It freezes the
finite worksheet
\({\mathcal W}_{26}^{N,j}({\mathfrak T},L)\), proves that a populated
complete worksheet would decide all five Paper-25 Branch-A gates by finite
scalar arithmetic, prints the minimal live-edge conditional density
formally, imports the Paper-23 formal residual atom identity, unwinds the
exact residual density
\(H_{RPF}^{N,j}=\log Z+\log p-\sum_p\log K_p^{CE}\), isolates the weaker
four-point RN-ratio bypass, then proves that on the minimal live edge this
ratio is exactly the true mixed `CleanRPF`/bridge amplitude table.  It proves
`P26-ACTLAW-DATA-GAP`, `P26-ACTATOM-DATA-GAP`,
`P26-RPF-RESID-SOURCE-GAP`, `P26-SEL2-RN-RATIO-GAP`, and
`P26-SEL2-RN-RATIO-ATTEMPT-GAP`, and
`P26-RN-MIXAMP-VALUE-GAP`: Papers 20--25 do not populate the needed
conditional probabilities, primitive residual density values, mixed RN
ratios, actual residual atom values or oscillation bounds, Peter-Weyl tails,
or bridge amplitudes cofinally on the actual adaptive `SEL2` law.  The
sharp endpoint exported by Paper 26 is the RN-MIXAMP trichotomy:
prove smallness, prove a same-law lower floor, or leave adaptive Branch A.

Updated: 2026-05-25 after Paper 27: Paper 27 executes the promised
RN-MIXAMP continuation rather than adding another worksheet.  It freezes the
weighted mixed RN row norm, tries signed cancellation, tries conditional
spectral contraction, tries direct row smallness, and then tries the
same-law lower-floor exit.  The result is a completed current-corpus
nonclosure theorem:
`P27-RN-MIXAMP-SIGN-GAP`, `P27-RN-MIXAMP-SPEC-GAP`,
`P27-RN-MIXAMP-SMALL-GAP`, and `P27-RN-MIXAMP-FLOOR-GAP`.
Adaptive Branch A is therefore still undecided, but it cannot be advanced by
more finite labels alone.  A positive continuation must supply new same-law
signed amplitude control, conditional spectral contraction plus tail,
direct RN-MIXAMP values/domination, bridge damping plus tail, the lower
floor \(\overline\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}\ge M_*\), or exit to Branch B/C.

Updated: 2026-05-25 after Paper 28: Paper 28 executes the spectral
contraction plus tail route for RN-MIXAMP.  It defines the actual same-law
conditional transfer operator, isolates the finite low-mode Peter-Weyl block,
audits the same-law tail, and compares the combined quantity with the
Paper-25 contraction margin.  The operator exists and is finite at fixed
cutoff, but the current corpus supplies only the trivial Markov/oscillation
non-expansion \(\Theta\le1\), while the margin requires a strict
\(\Theta+\kappa<\theta_{\mathrm{crit}}<1\).  It also supplies no same-law
finite-band, Peter-Weyl decay, or cofinal tail table.  The completed verdicts
are `P28-RN-MIXAMP-LOWGAP-GAP`,
`P28-RN-MIXAMP-KTAIL-GAP`, and
`P28-RN-MIXAMP-SPECTAIL-GAP`.

Updated: 2026-05-25 after Paper 29: Paper 29 executes the low-mode value
extraction attempt and then attacks the primitive residual value theorem
itself.  It freezes the smallest useful endpoint battery
\(\{F_N,F_N^*,\mathrm{Ad}_N\}\), with \(SU(4)\) as a specialization rather
than the default adaptive target, writes the finite low-mode entries as
same-law conditional integrals against \(H_{RPF}^{N,j}\), and proves the key
non-recovery theorem: Paper-26 four-point RN-MIXAMP ratios do not determine
the spectral transition matrix because endpoint-additive one-site terms
cancel from mixed ratios but change conditional weights.  It then defines
`P29-PRIMRES-VAL` and proves that direct density sourcing, residual
coefficient row identity, and actual same-law polymer-value sourcing are not
supplied by the current corpus.  The completed gaps are
`P29-RN-MIXAMP-LOWENTRY-GAP`,
`P29-RN-MIXAMP-LOWGAP-GAP`,
`P29-RN-MIXAMP-DOEBLIN-GAP`, and
`P29-RN-MIXAMP-SPECTRAL-VALUE-GAP`, plus
`P29-PRIMRES-DIRECT-GAP`, `P29-PRIMRES-ROWID-GAP`,
`P29-PRIMRES-POLYVAL-GAP`, and the sharper Part-II verdict
`P29-PRIMRES-ROWID-FULL-GAP`.  Part II also proves
`P29-PRIMRES-ATOM-ID`, showing that primitive residual atoms are exactly the
nonconstant literal RPF residual atoms, and exports
`P29-PRIMRES-DEFECT-EXPORTED`, the exact defect-polymer target left after
retained rows are charged.  Part III maximizes the retained value-licensed
class, proves that a defect polymer-value theorem would source primitive
residual values and reopen the spectral route, and records the current-corpus
gaps `P29-PRIMRES-DEFECT-POLYVAL-GAP` and
`P29-PRIMRES-DEFECT-FLOOR-GAP`.  Part IV executes the defect Dobrushin test:
`P29-PRIMRES-DEFECT-DOB(q,a)` would source the defect-polymer theorem, but
the current corpus does not print the defect conditional influence matrix;
failure of Dobrushin is not itself a lower floor, and the stronger witness is
also unsourced.  The new gaps are `P29-PRIMRES-DEFECT-DOB-GAP` and
`P29-PRIMRES-DEFECT-DOBWIT-GAP`.  A final completion certificate records
`P29-SPECTRAL-VALUE-EXTRACTION-CLOSED`: more finite labels do not move the
spectral route unless they carry same-law residual values, direct low-mode
entries, a Doeblin floor, or a same-law Peter-Weyl tail table.

Updated: 2026-05-25 after Paper 30: Paper 30 is completed as the actual-law
signed/bridge amplitude-or-floor campaign.  It is not a summary paper.  It
proves the exact closure implications for same-law signed bridge values,
narrowed-body finite dual certificates, bridge damping plus tail, full-object
signed range control, and the lower-floor exit, then proves that Papers
20--29 supply none of those sources in a closing or falsifying range.  The
signed/bridge channel is therefore settled at the current-corpus level.
Paper 30 then opens and executes the first analytic unblock attempt: it
proves parent-law pushforward domination `P30-PARENT-PUSH-DOM`, proves exact
finite-volume DLR localization `P30-FV-DLR-EXACT`, proves the needed
log-oscillation pushforward lemma `P30-PARENT-LOGOSC-DOM`, and reduces actual
bridge damping to the strict exponent test
$$
{1\over2}C_{min}^{br}\tau_{br}^{cof}-\chi_{tilt}^{cof}>g_{br}
$$
plus the common tail budget.  The new current-corpus gaps are
`P30-TREE-HK-BRIDGEDAMP-GAP` and `P30-TREE-HK-SIGNED-GAP`.  Future progress
requires this heat-kernel/tree-gauge exponent, new same-law signed/bridge
values, a new narrowed certificate, a lower floor, a return to the Paper-29
defect value/influence route, or an exit from adaptive Branch A.  Part III
then freezes the bridge-exponent worksheet itself: the exponent is reduced
to a positive bridge time slope, a Casimir floor with fixed heat-kernel
normalization, a sharp finite bridge-entropy table, and a residual tilt
bound.  It proves the normalizer-oscillation bookkeeping and the four-account
closure theorem, and records the active front as
`P30-BRIDGE-TIME-SLOPE-GAP`, `P30-TILT-RPF-GAP`, and
`P30-BRIDGE-ENTROPY-TABLE-GAP`.  The first two are genuine same-law
analytic value problems; the last is a finite table problem.  A final finite
pass closes `P30-CASIMIR-NORM(1)` and proves the coarse over-refined bridge
entropy certificate
$$
g_{br}\le g_{br}^{99},\qquad \log g_{br}^{99}\le157.02.
$$
This finite certificate is valid but not a plausible closing estimate by
itself.  The time-slope audit then proves a unit-compatibility obstruction:
with carrier-size length, the total `SEL2` sheet heat time is cofinally
bounded, so unbounded bridge lengths force
\(\tau_{br}^{cof}(\ell_{car})=0\).  Positive heat-kernel damping therefore
requires a time-compatible bridge length and a matching entropy theorem
`P30-BRIDGE-TIMEENT(g_time)`, plus residual tilt control.  This provisional
front is refined below to the primitive local-bridge tilt source.  The
Casimir-time salvage audit then closes the
remaining fixed-\(N\) loophole: for every fixed declared \(SU(N_0)\), including
the \(N_0=4096\) row, the carrier-size Casimir-time slope is still zero if
bridge lengths are unbounded.  A carrier-step rescue requires a joint
\(N(j)\)-with-cutoff branch with \(\liminf_j N(j)/H_j>0\), which is a
different large-\(N\) diagnostic and not a fixed-gauge-group continuum
Yang-Mills theorem.  The residual tilt localization audit then removes the
local, endpoint-additive, normalizer, and HKSD interior tangent pieces from
the mixed tilt account.  The remaining primitive source is the real 4D
doubly centered residual RN term:
`P30-TILT-LOCAL-BRIDGE(chi_0)`.  The fixed-\(N\) heat-kernel bridge route is
therefore reduced to
`P30-BRIDGE-TIMEENT(g_time) + P30-TILT-LOCAL-BRIDGE(chi_0)` with
\({1\over2}C_0-\chi_0>g_{time}\), or else to a direct signed/bridge value
theorem, lower floor, or exit from adaptive Branch A.
The final positive-theorem search in Paper 30 then names the smallest
fixed-\(N\) bridge theorem that would actually unblock the route:
`P30-MIXED-RN-SCREEN(g_time,chi_0)` in a closing range.  This theorem combines
time-compatible true-bridge entropy with screened doubly centered control of
the real 4D residual RN mixed term.  Paper 30 proves that this theorem would
source the Paper-23 bridge route, but also proves the no-free-locality
verdict: endpoint/local removals, HKSD tangent cancellation, finite carriers,
canonical labels, and RP/Cov bookkeeping do not imply it.  The residual-tail
countermodels from Paper 23 remain the obstruction.  Future positive progress
therefore requires new same-law value information, not more finite labels.
Paper 30 then executes the screening campaign internally rather than
deferring it.  The bounded AF-area heat-time window refines the fixed-\(N\)
positive theorem from a slope statement to the literal window partition-sum
source `P30-MIXED-RN-WINDOW(D)` plus the common Paper-23 tail.  It proves the
closure implication, then proves the current-corpus gaps
`P30-BRIDGE-TIMEWIN-GAP` and `P30-RN-MIXED-TILTWIN-GAP`: carrier entropy is
in the wrong unit, and local/HKSD ledgers do not bound the actual residual
mixed RN tilt.
Finally, Paper 30 executes the signed-involution push: it defines admissible
true-bridge involutions, proves that an orbit-defect value theorem or an
HK-symmetric cancellation plus residual-defect bound would close the signed
route, and proves the current-corpus gaps
`P30-BRIDGE-INV-RESDEF-GAP` and
`P30-BRIDGE-INV-DEFECT-FLOOR-GAP`.  Recorded orientation, duality,
reflection, conjugation, quotient, RP, and covariance symmetries reduce labels
but do not supply a negative pairing or a residual-defect value theorem.
The final Paper-30 pass makes the needed residual-defect estimate sharp:
`P30-BRIDGE-INV-XRATIO(C,Omega,kappa)` closes the signed route exactly when
`2C+Omega^2/4<M_sgn(kappa)`.  It then proves the three positive sourcing
routes that would supply this bound -- maximal-defect KP, involution-defect
Dobrushin/activity, or projected low-mode plus tail -- and the opposite
lower-floor witness route.  The current-corpus gaps are now
`P30-BRIDGE-INV-DEFECT-DOB-GAP`,
`P30-BRIDGE-INV-LOWTAIL-GAP`, and
`P30-BRIDGE-INV-DEFECT-WIT-GAP`.  This is the honest endpoint of Paper 30:
the obstruction is no longer "which label table is missing"; it is same-law
value information about the actual residual defect.
Paper 30 then performs the requested prove/falsify pass on the three
positive residual-defect source routes.  It proves each route is
conditionally sufficient, proves none is supplied by Papers 20--30, and
falsifies each as a current-corpus derivation by same-record residual-tail
completions preserving the closed ledgers.  It does not globally falsify any
route as a possible future theorem about the actual adaptive law.  The
completed verdict is: maximal-defect KP, involution-defect
Dobrushin/activity, and projected low-mode plus tail are all closed at the
current-corpus level; progress now requires new same-law value information or
a lower-floor witness.
Paper 30 then keeps the continuation inside Branch A and gives the precise
way to overcome the three current-corpus failures: add actual-law anchors.
`P30-BRANCHA-KP-ANCHOR`, `P30-BRANCHA-DOB-ANCHOR`, and
`P30-BRANCHA-LOWTAIL-ANCHOR` respectively print the same-law connected
defect activities, defect conditional influence/activity data, or projected
low-mode plus Peter-Weyl complement data.  Each anchor makes the old
residual-tail countercompletions inadmissible and closes `P23-RPF-TRANS0`
when its displayed Paper-30 margin holds.  Thus Branch A is not abandoned:
it is reduced to one of three concrete actual-law value-extraction tasks.
The final audit then corrects any possible overreading: those anchor values
are not proven and not falsified in Paper 30.  What is falsified is their
decidability from the current closed corpus.  Same-record completions
preserving all printed ledgers can make the anchor quantities pass or fail,
so a positive or negative truth verdict requires new same-law quantitative
information about the actual adaptive residual law.
Paper 30 then finds the first such same-law quantitative extractor rather
than merely naming its absence: finite-DLR range/log-ratio envelopes for the
actual parent law.  These give an exact finite same-law boundary log-ratio
quantity \(\Delta_{xy}^{DLR,N,j}\), the Dobrushin upper envelope
\(\sum_y e^{ad(x,y)}\tanh(\Delta_{xy}^{DLR,N,j}/4)\), a Möbius activity
envelope for the KP route, and exact projected Peter-Weyl low-mode/tail
quantities for the signed bridge defect.  This is genuine same-law
quantitative information, but the crude range version does not close:
heat-kernel ranges diverge in the small-time limit, Dobrushin
\(\tanh\)-bounds saturate near one, and range control alone gives no
Peter-Weyl tail decay.  The next positive theorem must sharpen this
extractor through cancellation/cluster improvement, a genuinely small
boundary log-ratio row, or same-law coefficient decay.
Paper 30 then executes the requested radical search pass.  It explores six
far-field same-law routes: score/covariance response, connected
Möbius/cumulant cancellation, Peter-Weyl heat-flow smoothing plus residual
tail, finite Schwinger-Dyson/Ward signed bridge identities, transport or
entropic contraction, and the lower-floor exit.  For each route Paper 30
proves the finite identity or closure implication that is genuinely
available, then proves the current-corpus non-sourcing verdict.  The pass
does not close Branch A from Papers 20--30, but it narrows the next real
positive theorem to `P30-CONN-MOBIUS`, `P30-SCORE-COV-ROW`, or
`P30-HK-RESID-PWTAIL`, with the signed alternatives `P30-WARD-BRIDGE` and
`P30-RADICAL-FLOOR`.
Paper 30 then pushes one step further in a Feynman/path-integral direction:
it rewrites the same finite parent DLR law as an exact Peter-Weyl
representation-history sum.  This gives the same-law spin-foam DLR formula,
a flux-selection rule for projected bridge coefficients, and a foam-tail
upper bound for the omitted Peter-Weyl complement.  The new constructive
target is `P30-SPINFOAM-TAIL(r_L)`, preferably sourced by a high-charge area
lower bound, residual insertion coefficient decay, signed/intertwiner
cancellation, and a denominator lower bound.  This does not close Branch A
yet, but it replaces the abstract tail gap by an explicit same-law
path-history estimate.
Paper 30 then sharpens the Feynman-style idea into a nonabelian switching
program.  The exact analogue of Ising random-current switching is not a free
inference, because nonabelian histories carry recoupling coefficients,
complex phases, and actual RPF/Jacobian residual insertions.  What is proved
is a rigorous corridor-switching framework: legal local recouplings preserve
the same-law history space, the heat-kernel part of the switching defect is
explicit, and a sign-reversing nearly amplitude-neutral switch bounds the
signed high-charge tail by a mismatch term plus an unpaired-sector debit.
The next live structural source is
`P30-NONABELIAN-SWITCHING(delta,u)`, more primitively
`P30-SWITCH-RESID-QI + P30-SWITCH-NEUTRAL + P30-SWITCH-UNPAIRED`, with
`P30-SWITCH-AREA` as the proposed way to pay the unpaired sector.
Paper 30 then performs the minimal-corridor amplitude-ratio test.  The exact
termwise ratio factors as \(R_{HK}R_F R_{RPF}\), and termwise neutrality is
not generic: heat-kernel Casimir/dimension factors, recoupling coefficients,
and the actual residual insertion do not cancel term by term.  This does not
kill switching; it forces the correct nonabelian replacement, block
switching.  The new concrete source is `P30-BLOCK-SWITCH(theta,u)`, a finite
matrix anticommutation/commutator theorem on each minimal recoupling block:
print \(\Sigma_{\Gamma_1}\), \(U_{\Gamma_1}\),
\(D_{\Gamma_1}^{HK}\), and \(\mathcal R_{\Gamma_1}\), then bound the trace
norm of \(D^{HK}\mathcal R\Sigma+U^*D^{HK}\mathcal R\Sigma U\).
The universal \(F\otimes F^*\) block table is then printed:
$$
U_N=
\begin{pmatrix}
1/N&\sqrt{N^2-1}/N\\
\sqrt{N^2-1}/N&-1/N
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
D^{HK}=\operatorname{diag}(1,(N^2-1)e^{-t_p\lambda_{HK}N}).
$$
The optimistic switch-odd signed insertion still leaks by
\(|h_0-h_A|\sqrt{N^2-1}/N\) if the residual is scalar, so pure oddness does
not close the route.  The sharp subgate is now
`P30-BLOCK-EVEN-SMALL(theta)`: bound the \(U_N\)-even part of
\(D_{\Gamma_1}^{HK}\mathcal R_{\Gamma_1}\Sigma_{\Gamma_1}\).
Paper 30 then algebraizes this subgate completely.  For
\(A=D^{HK}\mathcal R\Sigma=\begin{pmatrix}p&q\\r&s\end{pmatrix}\), the
block-even projection is
$$
\Pi_+^U(A)
=
{1\over2}(\delta_1 I+\delta_2U_N),
\qquad
\delta_1=p+s,\quad
\delta_2=b_N(q+r)+a_N(p-s).
$$
Thus the block-switching obstruction is exactly the same-law value problem
for the two scalar defects \(\delta_1,\delta_2\).  Paper 30 proves a
current-corpus no-go for deriving their smallness from universal data,
finite labels, or scalar magnitude envelopes alone.  The live fork is now
`P30-HKCOMP-BLOCK-ODD(theta)` or
`P30-BLOCK-EVEN-FLOOR-WIT(M_*)`.
Paper 30 finally prints the exact finite-DLR/Peter-Weyl formulas for
\(p,q,r,s\), rewrites \(\delta_1,\delta_2\) as expectations of two explicit
defect insertions \(\Phi_1,\Phi_2\), and targets the finite compact-Lie Ward
identity at those two insertions.  This yields the exact chain
`P30-DEFECT-WARD(theta) => P30-HKCOMP-BLOCK-ODD(theta)`, while proving that
the current corpus still does not source the required residual/Jacobian
score smallness.  The live same-law value sources are now
`P30-DEFECT-WARD(theta)`, `P30-RESID-SCORE-TAIL`, or
`P30-BLOCK-EVEN-FLOOR-WIT(M_*)`.
Paper 30 then isolates the residual score
\(S_{\ell,a}^{RPF}=-X_{\ell,a}V_{RPF}+X_{\ell,a}\log J_{tree}\), pairs it
with the two defect-Ward primitives, and defines a same-law Peter-Weyl
low-mode-plus-tail source
`P30-RESID-SCORE-TAIL(L,Theta_L,r_L)`.  This proves the conditional chain
`P30-RESID-SCORE-TAIL => P30-DEFECT-WARD(Theta_L+r_L)`, while recording that
Papers 20--30 still do not print the finite low-mode score table,
residual-score coefficient decay, score-orthogonality, or the alternative
score-floor witness.
Paper 30 then keeps the score-orthogonality campaign inside the same paper:
it defines the finite heat-kernel Stein operator on the actual compact chart,
solves the Poisson equation for the two defect insertions, and proves the
exact identity
`heat-reference defect + residual-score pairing = actual defect`.  This
isolates `P30-HKREF-DEFECT-NEUTRAL`, `P30-DEFECT-SCORE-ORTHO`, and the
supporting `P30-STEIN-PW-ORTHO` route, with
`P30-STEIN-SCORE-FLOOR-WIT(M_*)` as the negative closure if
non-transversality becomes sign-coherent.
Paper 30 then attacks the heat-reference neutrality subgate directly.  The
two-channel heat-reference mean matrix \(M_{\Gamma_1}^{HK}\) is reduced to
two traces, \(m_1=\operatorname{Tr}M\) and \(m_2=\operatorname{Tr}(U_NM)\).
The natural recoupling involution \(U_N\) fails to preserve the heat
diagonal unless \(h_0=h_A\), while the phase involution preserves the heat
diagonal but does not kill the diagonal trace defects.  In the optimistic
switch-odd probe the heat-reference debit is exactly
\(|h_0-h_A|\sqrt{N^2-1}/N\).  Thus universal heat-reference neutrality is
not closed; it requires a printed heat-reference table, a nonlocal
parent-graph cancellation, a margin test absorbing the debit, or a floor
witness.
Paper 30 then attacks the margin-absorption option.  The optimistic heat
debit can fit only if the live heat time lies in the adjoint-balance window
around
\(\log(N^2-1)/(\lambda_{HK}N)\), with width
\(O(\mathfrak M_{HK}/N)\), where
\(\mathfrak M_{HK}=M_{\mathrm{sgn}}(\kappa)-u-\epsilon_s\).  This isolates
`P30-HK-BALANCE-COMPAT(Delta)`: a cofinal selector preserving the same
adaptive `SEL2` scalar law and all previous finite-table closures while
satisfying the balance window.  The current corpus neither proves nor
forbids that compatibility.
Paper 30 then resolves this balance-compatibility subgate sharply.  For a
fixed \(SU(N_0)\) target, the AF microscopic heat time satisfies
\(t_i\to0\), so the optimistic adjoint imbalance tends to \(N_0^2-2\);
fixed-rank balance therefore fails on the AF tail.  For the already declared
large-rank Branch-A family, however, a rank-diagonal selector choosing
\(N_i\) so that
\(\log(N_i^2-1)/(\lambda_{HK}N_i)\) tracks \(t_i\) gives
$$
\left|1-(N_i^2-1)e^{-t_i\lambda_{HK}N_i}\right|
=O(\log N_i/N_i).
$$
This preserves the `SEL2` block-time ledger and `TREE-TIME` on the large-rank
fundamental row.  Thus the live obstruction moves from balance compatibility
to the genuinely same-law residual budget
\(M_{\mathrm{sgn}}(\kappa)-u-\epsilon_s>0\).
Paper 30 then expands that residual budget into three primitive same-law
entries: the minimal-edge Peter-Weyl tail \(\kappa\), the unblocked-sector
mass \(u\), and the Stein residual-score debit \(\epsilon_s\).  It imports
the Paper-23/Paper-28/Paper-29 verdict that \(\kappa\) is not sourced by
finite labels or heat-kernel reference rows; records that \(u\) is zero only
after a complete switching-block cover, otherwise an actual-law mass bound;
and splits \(\epsilon_s\) into a finite Stein low-mode table plus a
same-law score tail.  The exact conditional positive package is
$$
\mathrm{P23\text{-}RPF\text{-}MIN\text{-}KTAIL}(\kappa)
+
\mathrm{P30\text{-}UNBLOCKED\text{-}SMALL}(u)
+
\mathrm{P30\text{-}DEFECT\text{-}SCORE\text{-}ORTHO}(\epsilon_s)
+
\{M_{\mathrm{sgn}}(\kappa)-u-\epsilon_s>0\}.
$$
The current corpus proves none of the three numerical entries in a closing
range.  The negative branch is the corresponding floor witness
\(\overline\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}\ge M_*\).
Paper 30 then attacks the \(u\)-entry directly.  It defines the
`U_N`-blockable high-charge bridge rows, classifies the unblocked complement
into tail-paid, previously licensed, finite-cover, signed-switch, and
actual-value failure modes, and proves that the finite-cover route closes
\(u=0\) only through
$$
\mathrm{P30\text{-}CORRIDOR\text{-}COMPLETE}
+
\mathrm{P30\text{-}SWITCH\text{-}SIGNED\text{-}COMPLETE}(\delta,0).
$$
If exact cover fails, the switch-area route gives the explicit conditional
bound
$$
u\le \exp(g_{sw}+\epsilon_{res}+d_Z-A_0),
$$
so the residual budget closes only if
\(M_{\mathrm{sgn}}(\kappa)-\epsilon_s-\exp(g_{sw}+\epsilon_{res}+d_Z-A_0)>0\).
The current corpus does not yet prove either exact cover or a useful
switch-area bound, but \(u\) is no longer a vague leftover: its next source is
`P30-CORRIDOR-COMPLETE`, `P30-SWITCH-SIGNED-COMPLETE`, or
`P30-SWITCH-AREA`.
Paper 30 then closes the corridor-completeness source in the full-block
sense.  The minimal \(2\times2\) singlet/adjoint \(U_N\) table is only a
diagnostic; the actual high-charge tail must be covered by the full finite
invariant tensor block attached to the selected corridor cell.  Using the
same-law representation-history expansion, every retained true-bridge history
has an endpoint-mixed flux component, hence a canonical first corridor cell.
The full local invariant tensor space supplies a finite unitary recoupling
matrix, so the structural flags `NOCELL`, `NON2CH`, and `DEN0` are removed.
Thus `P30-CORRIDOR-COMPLETE` is closed in the full-block sense, and the live
\(u\)-gate is now exactly signed switching/residual control:
`P30-SWITCH-SIGNED-COMPLETE`, or else the fallback
`P30-SWITCH-AREA`.
Paper 30 then attacks signed switching on the full blocks.  It defines the
full-block weighted signed matrix \(A_\Gamma^{full}=D_\Gamma^{HK}\mathcal
R_\Gamma\Sigma_\Gamma\), the defect
$$
\mathcal E_\Gamma^{full}
=
A_\Gamma^{full}+U_\Gamma^*A_\Gamma^{full}U_\Gamma,
$$
and proves that its trace norm bounds the signed block contribution.  The
defect splits exactly into three same-law debits: signed parity
`P30-FULL-SIGPAR`, heat recoupling commutation `P30-FULL-HKCOMM`, and
residual quasi-invariance `P30-FULL-RPFQI`.  A full-block Ward/Stein lift
`P30-FULLDEF-WARD` is also printed.  The current corpus does not prove these
debits in a closing range.  The live positive target after corridor closure
is therefore full-block signed amplitude control, with `P30-FULL-HKCOMM` as
the most structural next subgate and `P30-SWITCH-AREA` or a floor witness as
fallbacks.
Paper 30 then attacks `P30-FULL-HKCOMM`.  It proves the exact heat
commutation criterion: \(U_\Gamma^*D_\Gamma U_\Gamma=D_\Gamma\) iff the
heat weights are constant on every connected component of the full-block
recoupling mixing graph.  The rank-diagonal adjoint balance is shown not to
extend universally: at the adjoint-balance time the two-index symmetric and
antisymmetric channel weights tend to \(1/2\), and any scalar heat time has
an asymptotic three-channel balance gap at least \(1/3\) for the
singlet/adjoint/two-index test.  Thus full heat commutation is not a
structural consequence of the balance selector.  The replacement live source
is `P30-FULL-HKBAL-SUPPORT(delta_HK,u_HK)`: nonbalanced full-block channels
must be absent, annihilated by the actual signed/residual factor, or paid by
an explicit same-law debit.
Paper 30 then makes this replacement source finite and testable.  It defines
the heat-bad component classifier on the full recoupling graph, records the
low-channel table showing that singlet/adjoint/two-index components are
cofinally heat-bad below the \(1/3\) obstruction threshold, and names the
exact same-law heat-bad debit
`P30-HKBAD-MASS(delta,mu)`.  The result is a sharp reduction:
`P30-HKBAD-MASS(delta,mu)` plus the good-sector size bound sources
`P30-FULL-HKCOMM(delta B_RSigma+mu)`, while the current corpus cannot derive
that mass bound from representation data alone.  The next live theorem is
therefore actual same-law value information on the heat-bad projection:
support zero, signed cancellation, residual quasi-invariance, direct
absolute smallness, or a sign-coherent floor witness.
Paper 30 then audits the cleanest of these options, support-zero.  It defines
`P30-HKBAD-ACTZERO(delta)` and proves that it would imply
`P30-HKBAD-MASS(delta,0)`, hence the heat-commutator debit with only the
good-sector cost.  It also proves that this support-zero statement is not a
consequence of representation labels or heat balance alone: two-index
channels are present by ordinary tensor-product support, so their absence
must come from actual signed/residual annihilation.  The next positive
subroute is therefore signed cancellation on the heat-bad projection.
Paper 30 then audits that signed-cancellation route.  The key correction is
that bare switch-oddness of the signed insertion \(\Sigma\) is not enough on
a heat-bad component: a two-channel block with unequal heat weights can have
\(U^*\Sigma U=-\Sigma\) while \(D\Sigma+U^*D\Sigma U\ne0\).  The valid
positive theorem is the weighted statement
`P30-HKBAD-WODD(delta,theta)`, a direct bound on
\(P_{bad}^{HK}(DR\Sigma+U^*DR\Sigma U)\).  This would pay the heat-bad
sector directly, but the current corpus does not prove it in a closing
range.  The remaining heat-bad front is residual/Jacobian quasi-invariance,
direct absolute smallness, or a sign-coherent floor witness.
Paper 30 then audits those remaining heat-bad options.  It defines
`P30-HKBAD-RPFQI(delta,eta_R)` and proves that this projected residual
quasi-invariance pays exactly the residual term in the projected three-term
identity, but also proves by the same unequal-heat two-channel example that
RPFQI alone is not a standalone escape.  It defines the direct absolute
smallness theorem `P30-HKBAD-ABS(delta,mu)` and the negative
`P30-HKBAD-FLOOR(M_*)` witness.  Neither upper smallness nor lower floor is
sourced by the current corpus.  The heat-bad branch is therefore fully
reduced to the single actual same-law matrix
\(P_{bad}^{HK}(DR\Sigma+U^*DR\Sigma U)\); further finite-label refinement is
bookkeeping unless it brings new quantitative value information for that
matrix.
Paper 30 then changes viewpoint.  Instead of asking for entries of
\(P_{bad}^{HK}(DR\Sigma+U^*DR\Sigma U)\), it uses trace duality to rewrite
the heat-bad trace-norm debit as a supremum of first responses of same-law
source pressures \(\Psi_Q(s)\) over deterministic heat-bad dual tests
\(Q\).  The identity is exact:
`P30-HKBAD-ABS(delta,mu)` is equivalent to a uniform bound on
\(\sup_Q \partial_s\Psi_Q(0)\).  A new calculus lemma proves that source
near-evenness `P30-HKBAD-SRC-NEUT(a,rho)` plus source curvature
`P30-HKBAD-SRC-CURV(a,chi)` implies the debit
\(\rho/a+\chi a/2\).  These source theorems are not sourced by the current
corpus, but the obstruction has been reframed as finite same-law response
control rather than direct conditional-row evaluation.

Updated: 2026-05-26 after the Paper-31 closure pass: Paper 31 is now finished
as the same-law source-response calculus.  It is not a summary.  It turns the
repeated "missing same-law value" obstruction into a finite derivative
calculus, exports that calculus to the active obstructions, and closes the
menu: source-response gives exact reformulations and conditional reductions,
not free confinement.  The next paper must choose a primitive same-law
analytic input directly.

Updated: 2026-05-26 after Paper 32: Paper 32 attacks the narrowest primitive
input first, the heat-bad source neutrality/curvature route.  It makes the
Feynman-style change of viewpoint from matrix-entry recovery to switch
pressure: every heat-bad source splits into switch-odd and switch-even parts,
and the switch-odd part has exactly even pressure under a same-law switch
symmetry.  The positive target is therefore no longer the whole heat-bad
matrix, but the two primitive same-law estimates
`P32-HKBAD-EVENDEF(epsilon)` and `P32-HKBAD-SRC-CURV(a,chi)`, with debit
\(\epsilon+\chi a/2\).  Paper 32 proves this reduction, audits Poincare,
Ward-Stein, Peter-Weyl, and floor routes, and records that the current corpus
does not source the needed even-defect, susceptibility, or floor constants.
Its second pass sharpens the actual primitive target: if the switch is only
quasi-invariant, the switch Radon-Nikodym oscillation contributes
\(\omega/(2a)\), so the optimized debit is
\(\epsilon+\sqrt{\omega\chi}\).  The next concrete finite same-law inputs are
therefore `P32-HKBAD-SWQI(omega)`, `P32-HKBAD-PRODTHIN(tau)` or the weaker
`P32-HKBAD-EVENRESP(epsilon)`, and only then curvature optimization.
The third pass attacks those inputs directly.  It proves that `SWQI` is
exactly a switch oscillation of the actual finite DLR Hamiltonian, with
envelope \(\Omega_{SW}^{DLR}\); it proves that `PRODTHIN` is equivalent,
up to explicit heat-mismatch singular-value constants, to smallness of the
stubborn heat-bad product term; and it isolates the response-only fallback
and product-floor alternative.  These are concrete finite same-law
quantities, but the current corpus still does not prove them in closing or
falsifying range.
The fourth pass exposes the switch-oscillation trap: on heat-bad components
with a positive heat switch floor, residual/Jacobian switch neutrality is the
wrong sign for `SWQI`; the positive theorem would have to be
`P32-HKBAD-SWCOUNTER(omega)`, an actual residual/Jacobian counter-tilt that
cancels the heat mismatch.  It also splits product thinness into
nondegenerate heat-term control plus null-sector mass, and identifies
`P32-HKBAD-EVEN-WARD(kappa)` as the response-only Ward route.
The fifth pass turns counter-tilt into an exact anti-heat residual atom
equation: modulo constants and licensed endpoint/Jacobian pieces,
`P32-HKBAD-SWCOUNTER(omega)` is equivalent to a switched residual atom sum
approximating minus the heat switch mismatch.  It then exposes the positive
compatibility theorem `P32-HKBAD-CT-PROD-COMP(omega,tau)`: the same residual
atom family must cancel heat in the switch RN oscillation while leaving small
heat-bad product mass.  This compatibility is not sourced by the current
corpus.
The sixth pass compresses compatibility into a finite quotient-distance
problem.  It defines the heat-bad residual atom quotient
\(\overline{\mathcal V}_{HB}^{N,j}\), the heat target class
\(\mathfrak k_{HB}^{N,j}\), the product seminorm \(\|\cdot\|_{prod}\), and
the anti-heat product distance \(d_{prod}^{N,j}(\omega)\).  The positive
route is now `P32-HKBAD-HIDDEN-ANTIHEAT(omega,tau)`,
\(d_{prod}^{N,j}(\omega)\le\tau\); the negative route is product visibility
plus sign coherence, `P32-HKBAD-VISHEAT + P32-HKBAD-VISPROD-FLOOR`.
The seventh pass turns this into a fixed-row primal/dual certificate
worksheet.  At cutoff \(L\), one must print the atom space, licensed
subspace, quotient map, heat target vector, and product operators
\(A_\Gamma^{N,j,L}\).  The positive certificate is
`P32-HKBAD-QDIST-UP(omega,tau,L,delta)`; the negative certificate is
`P32-HKBAD-QDIST-DUAL-FLOOR(M,L,delta)`.  Fixed-row compatibility is now
certificate-decidable to any rational tolerance, and the only remaining
non-row issue is the already separated Peter-Weyl tail.
The eighth pass attacks the rowprint theorem.  It proves that the structural
pieces \(E,C,Q,k\) are already sourced by Papers 23, 26, 29, 30, and 31; the
unsourced item is the heat-bad product-entry data for \(A_\Gamma^{N,j,L}\).
It then narrows the best positive target from full product-entry population
to `P32-HKBAD-QRESP(L,epsilon_data)`, source responses only against the
finite polar tests that the quotient-distance certificate actually uses.
The ninth pass attacks `QRESP` itself.  It defines the certificate polar
family \({\mathcal P}_{HB}^{N,j,L}\), polar source observables
\(V_\Lambda\), and polar pressures \(\Psi_\Lambda\).  It proves the exact
first-response identity and reduces positive closure to polar switch-oddness
plus polar curvature, or a polar Ward/Stein route.  If those fail, the same
polar family supplies the sharp floor route
`P32-HKBAD-QPOLAR-FLOOR`.  The current corpus does not prove any of these
polar primitive inputs in closing range.
The tenth pass explores those three polar routes.  Route I is valid with
debit
\(\omega_S/(2a)+\eta/2+\chi a/2\), or
\(\eta/2+R\sqrt{\omega_S}/2\) under the universal oscillation curvature
bound.  Route II is valid if an admissible actual-law Ward/Stein package is
printed for the polar observables.  Route III is valid if a polar slope is
sign-coherent and exceeds \(B_A^{rem}\).  The current corpus proves none of
the three in closing range; the next worksheet is to instantiate
\({\mathcal P}_{HB}^{N,j,L}\) and print the switch-defect, curvature/Ward,
and floor tables.
The eleventh pass instantiates the smallest nontrivial worksheet: the
Paper-30 singlet-adjoint crossing block.  The structural matrices
\(U_N\) and \(D_{\Gamma_1}^{HK}\) are already printed, and the three polar
routes all reduce to the actual \(2\times2\) same-law product
\(B_{\Gamma_1}^{N,j}=R_{\Gamma_1}^{N,j}\Sigma_{\Gamma_1}^{N,j}\).  Route I
needs weighted switch-oddness of
\(\Pi_+^{U_N}(D_{\Gamma_1}^{HK}B_{\Gamma_1}^{N,j})\), Route II needs a
minimal Ward/Stein package for the same polar functionals, and Route III
needs a sign-coherent floor functional.  Thus the smallest live theorem is
`P32-HKBAD-MINPOL-BTABLE`, `P32-HKBAD-MINPOL-WARD`, or
`P32-HKBAD-MINPOL-FLOOR`; more finite labels still do not move the branch.
The twelfth pass prints the full two-channel algebra.  Writing
\(B_{\Gamma_1}^{N,j}=(\beta_{\alpha\beta})\), the polar even defect compresses
exactly to
\(\Pi_+^{U_N}(D_{\Gamma_1}^{HK}B_{\Gamma_1}^{N,j})=(mI_2+tU_N)/2\), with
\(m=h_0\beta_{00}+h_A\beta_{AA}\) and
\(t=a_N(h_0\beta_{00}-h_A\beta_{AA})+
b_N(h_0\beta_{0A}+h_A\beta_{A0})\).  The trace norm is
\(\max\{|m|,|t|\}\) in the real normal case.  Gauge/Haar Ward identities
alone cannot source \(m,t\), since scalar intertwiner coefficients such as
\(B=cI_2\) obey the same structural covariance while changing both scalars.
The smallest live theorem is now `P32-HKBAD-MINPOL-MTABLE`: source, center,
or floor the two scalar responses \(m,t\).
The thirteenth pass attacks that theorem directly.  It defines the same-law
two-scalar pressure \(\Psi_{MT}^{N,j}(s,u)\), whose first derivatives are
exactly the missing values of \(m\) and \(t\).  It proves that a genuine
same-law centering involution with log-RN defect \(\omega\) and oddness error
\(\eta\) would source the needed smallness, but then proves that the known
crossing switch fixes \(m,t\) rather than negating them, selector relabeling
is tautological unless it changes the numerical block product, and
gauge/Haar Ward identities do not determine scalar intertwiner coefficients.
It also prints the exact floor candidates
\(\lambda_\pm=(m\pm t)/2\).  Thus the \(m,t\) route is fully settled at
current-corpus level: positive closure needs new same-law scalar smallness or
a new non-gauge Stein/centering theorem; negative closure needs a
sign-coherent floor for \(m,t,\lambda_+,\lambda_-\).
The fourteenth pass stays in Paper 32 and attacks the next primitive input:
same-law Peter-Weyl regularity/tail.  It defines a common tail theorem
`P32-SLAW-PWTAIL` covering the Paper-28 RN-MIXAMP tail, Paper-29 residual
low-mode lift, Paper-30 residual-score tail, and Paper-32 quotient/polar
tail lift.  It proves the positive sufficient theorem: cofinal Sobolev
regularity `P32-SLAW-PW-SOB(q,A)` or uniform analytic regularity implies a
Peter-Weyl tail, and residual multiplier tameness `P32-SLAW-MULT(q,B)` would
transfer clean heat-kernel damping to the actual residual observables.  It
also proves the limitation: heat-kernel smoothness of the reference factor
alone does not control conditional ratios, residual Hamiltonians, Jacobians,
selectors, logarithms, or residual-score derivatives.  The current corpus
prints neither Sobolev/analytic regularity, multiplier tameness, projection
commutator control, normalizer lower bounds, nor a high-mode sign-coherent
floor.  Thus this route is reduced to `P32-SLAW-PW-SOB`,
`P32-SLAW-MULT`, or `P32-SLAW-PWTAIL-FLOOR`.
The fifteenth pass investigates the six exact gates behind that transfer.
It proves the conditional transfer theorem
`P32-SLAW-PW-XFER`: Sobolev regularity, multiplier tameness, normalizer
lower bound, projection commutator decay, and residual-score Sobolev
regularity together transfer clean heat tails to actual tails.  It then
audits each gate.  `P32-SLAW-PW-SOB` needs cofinal derivative bounds;
`P32-SLAW-MULT` needs Sobolev multiplier bounds for residual/Jacobian/
selector/ratio/log factors; `P32-SLAW-ZNORM` needs an anchored log lower
bound, not just fixed-row positivity; `P32-SLAW-COMM` needs multiplier tail
control; `P32-SLAW-SCORE-SOB` needs one higher derivative on residual
logarithmic factors; and `P32-SLAW-PWTAIL-FLOOR-PKG` needs a retained
sign-coherent high-mode witness.  None is sourced by the current corpus.
The sixteenth pass attacks nonlinear source-Dobrushin locally rather than as
a global mixing theorem.  It defines the live observable family
\({\mathcal O}_{live}^{N,j}\), the finite boundary source family
\({\mathcal B}_{bd}^{N,j}\), mixed source pressures, the linear influence
row, the nonlinear boundary-segment row, and `P32-SRC-DOB-LOCAL(q,a)`.  It
proves that `LOCAL(q<1)` gives a Neumann bound \(1/(1-q)\) for cumulative
live responses; proves the curvature upgrade
`P32-SRC-DOB-LIN(q0,a) + P32-SRC-DOB-CURV(K,a) -> P32-SRC-DOB-LOCAL(q0+K/2,a)`;
audits the finite-DLR log-ratio envelope; and records the floor alternative
`P32-SRC-DOB-FLOOR(M_*)`.  The current corpus supplies neither a strict local
row, nor the curvature upgrade, nor a closing DLR envelope, nor a floor
witness.
The seventeenth pass attacks mixed RN-MIXAMP Ward/curvature control.  It
imports the Paper-27 weighted mixed row, defines the residual-tilted mixed
source pressure \(\Psi_{xy}^{N,j}(s,t,z)\), proves the endpoint-additive
cancellation, prints the exact same-law finite Ward integration-by-parts
identity, and isolates the positive packages
`P32-RNMIXAMP-WARD-SPAN + P32-RNMIXAMP-WARDDEF` and
`P32-RNMIXAMP-WARD0 + P32-RNMIXAMP-TILTCURV`.  It proves the conditional
closure implications, identifies tilt curvature as a connected third source
cumulant, audits why gauge/Haar Ward identities alone do not source the
needed span, score-defect, or curvature bounds, and prints the negative
alternative `P32-RNMIXAMP-WARD-FLOOR`.  None of these mixed RN-MIXAMP inputs
is supplied by the current corpus.
The eighteenth pass attacks the last untried Paper-31 primitive: connected
source-cumulant decay for the retained defect/Mobius activity family.  It
defines the defect source family \({\mathcal A}_{def}^{N,j}\), connected
source cumulants \(\kappa_\Gamma^{N,j}\), and the KP-weighted norm
\({\mathfrak K}_{def}^{N,j}(a)\).  It proves that
`P32-CONN-SRC-KP(q,a)` would source the defect-polymer theorem and reopen
primitive residual value extraction; records conditional exports to RN-MIXAMP
tilt curvature, local source-Dobrushin curvature, and Peter-Weyl score
cumulants through finite projection constants \(C_{RN},C_{DOB},C_{PW}\); and
audits why moment-cumulant identities, clean KP, and the already named defect
Dobrushin route do not source the needed decay in the current corpus.  It
prints the floor alternative `P32-CONN-SRC-FLOOR`.  Paper 32 has therefore
exhausted the Paper-31 primitive menu inside one paper: the attack surface is
reduced to a finite list of genuine same-law quantitative theorems, not more
source rewrites.
The nineteenth pass records and begins the post-menu attack plan.  It
reframes the remaining live values as a finite Ward/Stein range problem:
build the actual-law module generated by admissible \(XF\), test whether the
live target span \(M,T,\lambda_\pm,W_{xy}^{RN}\) lies in that range modulo
licensed rows, and then either bound the Ward score defect or print a
separating dual floor.  It proves the conditional closure theorem
`P32-JOINT-WS-RANGE + P32-JOINT-WS-DEFECT`, proves the fixed-row dual
separation theorem, and executes the first subtest: the pure gauge/Haar Ward
module is too small because it annihilates scalar intertwiner classes rather
than determining \(M,T,\lambda_\pm\).  The next executable target is therefore
the residual/selector Ward/Stein module
`P32-JOINT-WS-RESRANGE + P32-JOINT-WS-RESDEFECT`, or the dual floor
`P32-JOINT-WS-DUALFLOOR`.
The twentieth pass executes that residual/selector module split.  It defines
the residual/selector coordinate map \(\Phi_{\Gamma_1}^{N,j,L}\), its
Jacobian \(J_{res}^{N,j,L}\), the rank gate
`P32-JOINT-WS-RESRANGE`, and the residual score-defect gate
`P32-JOINT-WS-RESDEFECT`.  It proves selector-only directions have zero live
Jacobian, so relabeling cannot move \(M,T,\lambda_\pm\) or normalized
RN-MIXAMP values.  It proves that residual range plus residual score-defect
would close the joint route, and audits that the current corpus prints
neither \(J_{res}\), nor a quotient rank/least-singular-value bound, nor the
score-defect estimate, nor the dual floor sign-retention theorem.
The twenty-first pass executes the promised five-step residual-range
worksheet.  It instantiates the smallest \(\Gamma_1\) block, prints the
block-entry coordinates \((\beta_{00},\beta_{0A},\beta_{A0},\beta_{AA})\),
computes the scalar Jacobian for \(m,t,\lambda_+,\lambda_-\), and proves
that this scalar Jacobian has rank two for \(N>1\) and \(h_0h_A\ne0\).
Thus scalar rank is not the obstruction inside the block-entry envelope.
The full joint route is reduced to three exact items: admissibility of the
block-entry vector fields as actual residual/selector directions, the
normalized RN block-derivative table `P32-RN-BLKDER(L)`, and the scalar
residual score-defect estimate `P32-SCAL-RESDEFECT(delta)`.
The twenty-second pass attacks the finite RN derivative fork and finds a
hidden prerequisite.  The expression \(\partial W_{xy}^{RN}/\partial
\beta_{ab}\) is canonical only if the block-entry directions lift to actual
residual/selector vector fields and the RN row factors through the four
block entries.  Paper 32 defines `P32-BLKFIELD-ADM`,
`P32-RN-BETA-FACTOR`, and the kernel-separation alternative
`P32-RN-KERSEP`; proves the chain-rule formula
\(K_{RN}^{blk}=D_\theta W_{RN}R_{blk}\) under those hypotheses; and records
that the current corpus proves neither factorization nor kernel separation.
Thus `P32-RN-BLKDER(L)` is reduced, not printed.
The twenty-third pass avoids overpaying for that four-entry package on the
minimal scalar route.  It proves that the scalar heat-bad branch needs only
two admissible directions, \(m\) and \(t\), and defines the sharper gate
`P32-SCALFIELD-ADM`.  That gate is sourced either by a configuration
Jacobian theorem `P32-SCAL-CONFJAC` or by a source-response matrix theorem
`P32-SCAL-SRCMAT` with curvature/score control.  Paper 32 records that the
current corpus proves neither input, but the admissibility target is now
rank two rather than rank four.
The twenty-fourth pass settles the configuration-Jacobian fork at
current-corpus level.  Paper 32 proves that `P32-SCAL-CONFJAC` requires a
same-law pointwise lift of \(m,t\), and audits the three possible lift
mechanisms: atom-value lift, group-coordinate lift, and free-coordinate lift.
The first two are not sourced by the current corpus, while the third is not
same-law data.  The remaining positive scalar route is therefore the
source-matrix route, now reduced to a finite scalar source-rank theorem
`P32-SCAL-SRC-RANK(sigma)` plus a curvature theorem
`P32-SCAL-SRC-CURV(rho,epsilon)`, together with the residual score-defect
bound.
The twenty-fifth pass executes the source-rank worksheet.  It defines the
retained scalar source list, source columns \(C_A=(\mathcal C_A^m,\mathcal
C_A^t)^T\), the determinant minor
\(\Delta_{A,B}^{scal}\), and the quantitative determinant gate
`P32-SCAL-SRC-DET(A,B;Delta,M_C)`.  It proves the finite determinant
criterion for `P32-SCAL-SRC-RANK`, splits sources into zero, \(m\)-axis,
\(t\)-axis, and mixed channels, and audits that the current corpus prints
neither a positive determinant pair nor a sign-coherent rank-gap/floor.
Thus the source-rank problem is now an explicit finite minor problem, not a
curvature problem yet.
The twenty-sixth pass records the structural source tomography viewpoint.
It defines the two-knob structural block source \(S_{\alpha,\zeta}\), the
structural pressure \(\Phi_{str}\), the realization gate
`P32-SCAL-STRUCTSRC-ID`, the Gram gate `P32-SCAL-STRUCTSRC-GRAM`, and the
rigidity/floor exit `P32-SCAL-STRUCTSRC-RIGIDFLOOR`.  It proves that, once
the structural source is realized on the same adaptive law, Gram positivity
sources scalar rank; it also proves that clean structural knobs alone see
the heat channel rather than the actual residual/signed product
\(R_{\Gamma_1}\Sigma_{\Gamma_1}\).  The compact positive target is therefore
`P32-SCAL-STRUCTSRC-COUPLE + P32-SCAL-STRUCTSRC-GRAM`; the current corpus
prints neither coupling, Gram determinant, nor rigidity floor.

Updated: 2026-05-26 after Paper 33 first pass: Paper 33 starts the
same-law law-space bootstrap.  It treats the already printed finite
constraints as a convex set of admissible same-record laws and asks whether
positivity, gauge covariance, recoupling, heat-kernel data, Ward identities,
and moment matrices force the live scalar values \(m,t\).  The bootstrap
certificate format is sound and Barandes-aligned: positive closure is a
finite dual upper certificate, while negative closure is a sign-coherent
dual floor.  The minimal two-channel bootstrap is then settled negatively at
current-corpus level.  The scalar ray \(B=cI_2\) is feasible for every
allowed envelope value \(c\), giving
\(m=c(h_0+h_A)\) and \(t=ca_N(h_0-h_A)\).  Therefore ordinary moment
positivity and the existing structural constraints do not bound \(m,t\), do
not force a positive structural Gram determinant, and do not orient a floor.
The next theorem must add an active same-law constraint cutting or orienting
that ray: residual score smallness, structural coupling plus Gram,
non-gauge Ward/Stein, reflection-positive upper moments involving
\(R\Sigma\), RN block derivatives, or a sign-coherent scalar floor.
The second pass attacks the first candidate, residual score smallness.  It
defines the score-augmented bootstrap and proves the exact positive
implication
`P33-SCAL-SCOREENERGY(I_m,I_t) -> P32-SCAL-RESDEFECT(delta_score)` with
\(\delta_{score}=A_m(M_\beta)\sqrt{I_m}+A_t(M_\beta)\sqrt{I_t}\).  It also
proves the no-free-Ward theorem: Ward identities and score centering without
score-energy bounds merely replace the scalar ray by two-point score rays
with arbitrarily large score cost.  Thus residual-score closure now requires
a genuine same-law \(L^2\) residual/selector score estimate in the two scalar
block-entry directions.
The third pass investigates that \(L^2\) estimate itself.  It decomposes the
new scalar score into residual Hamiltonian, Jacobian, selector, and
normalizer components; proves component \(L^2\) bounds imply score energy;
prints three sourcing routes, pointwise score bounds, same-law
Sobolev/analytic score regularity, and a curvature/self-energy identity; and
audits all three as unsourced by the current corpus.  The sharpest new
positive target is the curvature package
`P33-SCAL-SCORE-CURV(K_m,L_m) + P33-SCAL-SCORE-CURV(K_t,L_t)`, which asks for
expected second score derivatives plus licensed-score energy.
The fourth pass attacks that curvature package directly.  It proves that
the score-curvature route is exactly the four-component package
`P33-RES-HESS`, `P33-JAC-HESS`, `P33-SEL-CURV`, and `P33-NORM-HESS`, plus
licensed-score energy.  Residual Hessian, Jacobian Hessian, selector
boundary curvature, and normalizer Hessian then imply
`P33-SCAL-SCOREENERGY`, hence `P32-SCAL-RESDEFECT`.  The pass also proves
that normalization only centers the conditional score; it does not bound the
normalizer variance, and finite-label refinement cannot close the route
unless it prints one of these component curvature estimates.  The cleanest
remaining positive subroute is selector local constancy plus residual
Hessian, scalar-chart Jacobian Hessian, and normalizer-Hessian domination.

Updated: 2026-05-26 after Paper 34: Paper 34 attacks the reflection-positive
moment/SOS bootstrap candidate from Paper 33.  It defines the finite
same-law RP record algebra, RP moment matrices
\(M_{ab}^{RP}=\mathbf E[(\Theta A_a)A_b]\), and finite RP/SOS upper and
floor certificates.  The framework is sound and Barandes-aligned because all
objects are finite record functions under the same adaptive law.  The
decisive all-degree test is negative at current-corpus level: every passive
RP/SOS worksheet admits the deterministic reflection-invariant scalar-ray
law \(B=cI_2\), so all ordinary and RP moment matrices are rank-one positive
outer products.  Consequently passive reflection positivity cannot bound
\(m,t\), cannot force the structural Gram gap, and cannot orient
\(\lambda_\pm\).  The only RP routes that remain are non-passive same-law
value theorems: `P34-RP-UPMOM`, `P34-RP-ODD`, `P34-RP-SCHUR`,
`P34-RP-STRUCTCOUPLE`, or `P34-RP-FLOOR-WIT`.  None is sourced by the
current corpus.  Paper 34 therefore closes the reflection-positive bootstrap
route as exact but non-sourcing unless it supplies a new actual-law value
inequality or orientation.

Updated: 2026-05-26 after Paper 35: Paper 35 proves the scalar-ray detector
theorem.  It classifies every future Branch-A scalar constraint by its trace
on the surviving scalar ray \(B=cI_2\).  Passive finite labels, ordinary
moment positivity, gauge covariance, recoupling, heat-diagonal identities,
selector relabelings, source reparametrization identities, and passive
reflection positivity are all ray-blind: every allowed \(c\) has a
deterministic same-law extension satisfying them.  A route can move Branch A
only if it is ray-cutting or ray-orienting: same-law upper value or
score-energy control, a non-gauge Ward/Stein equation \(Ac=\hbox{small}\),
structural coupling to \(R\Sigma\) plus Gram, a non-passive RP upper-moment,
oddness or Schur theorem, an RN block derivative/residual Jacobian rank
theorem, or a sign-coherent floor.  The next recommended constructive target
is the non-gauge Ward/Stein ray-cut detector
`P35-NONGAUGE-WS-RAYCUT(A,epsilon)`, with the corresponding dual floor if
the range misses the scalar direction.

Updated: 2026-05-26 after Paper 36: Paper 36 attacks the Paper-35 Rank-1
detector.  It proves that the formal block-entry Ward-Stein algebra works:
the live scalar readouts \(m,t\) are exact formal derivatives and the scalar
ray has coefficients \(A_m=h_0+h_A\) and \(A_t=a_N(h_0-h_A)\).  It then
separates this formal fact from the actual same-law theorem needed for
Branch A.  The positive route is now exactly
`P36-ACT-SCALFIELD-ADM + P36-ACT-RAYCOEFF(A_0) +
P36-WS-SCOREDEF(epsilon)` in a closing range.  Pure gauge/Haar,
selector-only, endpoint-additive, normalizer-only, and heat-only directions
are ray-blind for this detector.  If the actual Ward-Stein range misses the
scalar direction, finite separation gives only a dual candidate; closing
requires the sign-coherent floor theorem `P36-WS-DUALSIGN(M_*)`.  Paper 36
therefore reduces the non-gauge Ward-Stein route to actual scalar-field
admissibility and residual-score control, or a dual floor.

Updated: 2026-05-26 after Paper 37: Paper 37 executes the actual
scalar-field admissibility gate left by Paper 36.  It defines the actual
scalar map
\(s_{act}(\theta)=(m_{\Gamma_1}^{pt}(\theta),
t_{\Gamma_1}^{pt}(\theta))\), prints the actual Jacobian target
\(G_{act}^{scal}=D_\theta s_{act}\), and proves that actual scalar-field
admissibility is exactly
`P37-SCAL-POINTLIFT + P37-SCAL-JACRANK(sigma) +
P37-SCAL-SCOREENV(C_S)`.  It then audits all ways to build the controlled
right inverse: atom-value pointwise lift, group-coordinate lift, free scalar
coordinates, and source-response substitute.  The first two are not sourced
by the current corpus, free coordinates violate same-law discipline, and
source response is valid but belongs to the separate source-rank/curvature
route rather than to actual configuration-vector admissibility.  If rank two
passes, Paper 37 defines the lifted fields \(Y_m,Y_t\) and sends the problem
back to the Paper-36 score-defect theorem.  If rank fails, it yields only a
kernel separator candidate; closure requires the sign-coherent value theorem
`P37-SCAL-KERFLOOR(M_*)`.  Thus the actual admissibility route is settled at
current-corpus level: no formal-coordinate shortcut remains.  Paper 37 then
keeps the next pivot inside the same paper and attacks the structural
source-response route.  It defines the two-knob structural source, the
coupling gate `P37-STRUCTSRC-COUPLE`, the Gram gate
`P37-STRUCTSRC-GRAM`, the curvature gate `P37-STRUCTSRC-CURV`, and the
rigidity/floor exit `P37-STRUCTSRC-RIGIDFLOOR`.  It proves that coupling plus
Gram plus curvature is a valid same-law replacement for configuration vector
fields, while clean heat/channel sources are ray-blind because they do not
couple to the actual residual/signed product \(R\Sigma\).  The current corpus
prints none of coupling, Gram, curvature, or rigidity floor.  Thus Paper 37
reduces the scalar route to actual pointwise lift and Jacobian, structural
coupling and Gram with curvature, residual score control, or sign-coherent
floor.

Purpose: define the next strategic roadmap after the V2 finite-to-continuum viability program. The V3 goal is to push as far as possible toward three north-star targets:

1. full Lorentz-covariant interacting ISP;
2. full continuum QFT reconstruction or a precise no-go theorem;
3. non-Abelian gauge theory.

This roadmap is intentionally ambitious but not promotional. It distinguishes what V3 can realistically prove from what remains a longer program.

## Executive Status

V2 gives the beginnings of a continuum-directed relativistic ISP framework:

- a free stochastic-curvature theorem;
- a log-smeared finite-slab lift in the free one-particle benchmark;
- a projective hypersurface-kernel framework for changing regulators;
- a no-go theorem preventing Gamma-only Markovized QFT reconstruction;
- a conditional free-QFT promotion/matching arc for the massive `1+1D`
  Dirac/CAR benchmark;
- a Route-B sampled Lorentz-covariant free-QFT completion with finite boost
  approximants and spacetime local-net matching;
- a metric-data gate showing that the present Born-squared `Gamma` rule can
  retain diagonal/signless metric invariants but cannot reconstruct a full
  signed spatial metric without enriched representation data;
- a roadmap for interacting inverse control, operational reconstruction,
  continuum gauge benchmarks, QFT reconstruction tests, and metric-data gates.

V3 should not restart the program. It should use the V2 spine to attack the
three hard goals directly, with one added lesson from Paper 10: before claiming
QFT reconstruction, V3 must define the minimal enriched ISP data package that
is allowed to carry phases, orientations, CAR/Clifford structure, instruments,
and metric coefficients.

The honest expectation is:

- **controlled Lorentz-covariant interacting ISP:** plausible as a restricted V3 target;
- **full continuum QFT:** likely too large for one roadmap cycle, but V3 can produce a reconstruction theorem for a known class or a sharp no-go theorem;
- **non-Abelian gauge theory:** plausible at finite/projective benchmark level in V3; full continuum non-Abelian Yang-Mills-like ISP is a longer target.

The best V3 success would be a theorem chain showing that projective stochastic kernels, localized comparison maps, exchange defects, operational local nets, and gauge constraints can survive in at least one genuinely interacting and one genuinely non-Abelian controlled continuum-directed benchmark.

The V2 free-QFT result should be treated as a benchmark export, not as a
license to claim full QFT. Its strongest current form is:

```text
enriched ISP + lift/polarization/CAR data
-> sampled massive 1+1D Lorentz-covariant free Dirac/CAR QFT matching.
```

It is not:

```text
Gamma alone -> QFT, metric, stress-energy, or interactions.
```

## V3 North-Star Claim

The V3 north-star claim should be:

> Relativistic ISP can be promoted from a free/projective finite-kernel architecture to a controlled interacting projective kernel theory, with non-Abelian gauge-sector benchmarks and a precise reconstruction interface to continuum QFT.

This is weaker than claiming full QFT has been reconstructed. It is stronger than adding more finite examples.

After V2 Paper 10, the phrase "reconstruction interface" must mean a declared
enriched interface. Bare endpoint `Gamma` remains primary for stochastic ISP,
but it is not by itself a carrier of all QFT phases, local observables,
orientation signs, or full metric coefficients.

## Prerequisites From V2

V3 should assume the following V2 deliverables are either proved or explicitly carried as hypotheses:

1. **Free stochastic curvature.** A normalized exchange defect has the correct tangential hypersurface-deformation limit in the free one-particle benchmark.
2. **Projective kernel dynamics.** Regulated hypersurface kernels, projective states, cylinder effects, comparison maps, and exchange defects have exact or asymptotic naturality statements.
3. **Interacting inverse-control hypotheses.** V2 Paper 3 proves fixed-order linked-cluster cancellation for the connected logarithmic defect `L_R=log J_R`, but the finite-slab convergence upgrade must still control `L_R`, or an equivalent relative-cumulant object, in an anchored/local topology so primitive refinement errors can be propagated through `Gamma_0^{-1}`, `J_R`, `J_R^{-1}`, and `E_{R,S}` with explicit bounds. If the finite-slab linked-cluster theorem remains conditional, V3 must carry it as a named hypothesis rather than hiding it inside finite-range Hamiltonian locality.
4. **Operational reconstruction layer.** Raw comparison maps and operational effect algebras must be kept distinct.
5. **Gauge center resolution.** Physical gauge sectors require boundary-center or representation-center bookkeeping.
6. **Gamma-only no-go and Barandes discipline.** V2 Paper 6 blocks any route that reconstructs QFT from endpoint stochastic shadows alone or composes undeclared subprocesses as if the whole process were Markov divisible.
7. **Free-QFT promotion and matching.** V2 Papers 7-8 provide the conditional lift/polarization/CAR/local-net data needed to match the free massive `1+1D` benchmark on sampled equal-time sectors.
8. **Lorentz-covariant free-QFT completion.** V2 Paper 9 supplies a Route-B sampled-sector theorem-framework for finite boost approximants, asymptotic polarization/vacuum invariance, spacetime local nets, microcausality, and tested tangential-action compatibility.
9. **Metric-data gate.** V2 Paper 10 is a Gamma-level obstruction/gate. Under
   the present Born-squared rule it exports diagonal/signless metric remnants
   and an all-order sign-ambiguity no-go for full signed metric reconstruction
   from bare `Gamma`. It does not export gravity, stress-energy, or dynamical
   geometry.
10. **Enrichment ledger.** V3 must track which claims are Gamma-level,
    instrument-level, and enriched-representation-level. A theorem that uses
    Hilbert lifts, phases, CAR data, Clifford/principal-symbol data,
    polarizations, or operational instruments must say so. After Paper 10 this
    is not bookkeeping; it is a theorem-level obstruction boundary.

If any of these V2 pieces remain unproved, V3 papers should either prove them first or state them as named hypotheses.

## 2026-05-22 Boundary Remediation Log

This roadmap now records the response to the external whole-project critique
of the Yang-Mills/confinement arc. The critique is not accepted as authority,
but its mathematical boundary warnings are correct enough to require an
explicit remediation pass.

The remediation targets are:

1. **No hidden confinement assumption.** Papers 14--20 must distinguish
   conditional reductions from unconditional `4D SU(N)` confinement
   theorems. A source gate is circular if it silently assumes the continuum
   Yang-Mills measure, Wilson-loop area law, or positive string tension it is
   supposed to prove.
2. **Split whole-process towers.** A frozen record tower may supply common
   finite restrictions, readout maps, and debit bookkeeping. It may not by
   itself supply area-law behavior, positive source constants, or a continuum
   scaling limit unless those are proved or separately named as hypotheses.
3. **Finite Lorentz covariance is not exact Lorentz covariance.** On a finite
   state space, an invertible stochastic map whose inverse is stochastic is a
   permutation. Therefore V3 may claim only sampled, asymptotic, projective,
   or continuum-limit Lorentz covariance unless a genuine continuum
   construction is supplied.
4. **Operational locality is not Haag-Kastler AQFT.** Finite effect-space
   no-signaling and boundary-flux locality must not be advertised as full
   Einstein causality, spectrum condition, time-slice, additivity,
   quasilocal `C^*` completion, or type-III local structure.
5. **Schur-Hadamard phases need a lift class.** Entrywise rephasing preserves
   `Gamma=|Theta|^2` but not unitarity in general. Entropy and gauge claims
   must specify whether the lift is arbitrary, unistochastic/unitary,
   circuit-realizable, or physical-gauge equivalent.
6. **Gate names need standard translations.** Internal gate labels remain
   useful, but every major gate must have a one-line translation into
   standard lattice gauge theory, constructive QFT, AQFT, or ISP record-law
   language, together with its status: proved, conditional, imported, open,
   or falsified.

Immediate edits:

- Paper 19's `P19-TOWER` is to be read as a structural same-record tower,
  not as an area-law or continuum-confinement assumption.
- Paper 20 is the actual source-estimate paper. It must prove or falsify
  `R_H^opt<R_H^crit` and `L_AFM^sharp<Sig_AFM` on one frozen selector; it
  may not import those inequalities from Paper 19 or bury them in a tower
  axiom.
- Abstracts and conclusion/status sections in Papers 18--20 must continue to
  say that actual `4D SU(N)` confinement is not unconditionally proved unless
  the Paper-20 source estimates are proved without assuming the area law.

## Boundary Between V2 And V3

V2 now closes the free benchmark as far as is currently honest:

```text
free stochastic curvature
-> projective finite kernels
-> operational reconstruction discipline
-> Gamma-only no-go
-> free-QFT promotion/matching
-> sampled Lorentz-covariant free-QFT completion
-> Gamma-level metric-data obstruction and enriched metric-data gate.
```

V3 should therefore focus on what V2 still cannot do:

1. define the minimal enriched ISP data package needed for QFT-level
   reconstruction without pretending it is present in bare `Gamma`;
2. primitive smooth-lapse kernels beyond log-smearing;
3. interacting inverse-control and exchange-defect convergence;
4. operational local nets under projective refinement;
5. reconstruction/no-go theorems beyond the already supplied free benchmark;
6. finite and projective non-Abelian gauge benchmarks;
7. interacting Lorentz covariance and foliation independence.

This boundary keeps the roadmap Barandes-aligned. Whole-process kernels remain
primary. Divisions, local nets, detectors, Hilbert lifts, and field algebras are
declared structures, not secretly inferred from unrecorded Markov slices.

## Global Boundary Audit And Gate Translation Ledger

Every V3 theorem should be labeled by the strongest status it honestly has:

| Status | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| `proved` | Derived inside the paper from earlier proved or explicitly imported hypotheses. |
| `conditional` | A valid implication whose hypotheses include open source estimates. |
| `imported` | Brought from another paper as a named theorem or hypothesis. |
| `open source estimate` | A concrete inequality or existence statement still requiring proof or falsification. |
| `falsified branch` | A route shown not to close under the declared hypotheses or constants. |

The following translations are mandatory reader-facing shorthand for the
Yang-Mills/confinement arc:

| Internal gate | Standard-language translation | Status boundary |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `P19-TOWER` | One structural projective family of finite Wilson-loop/Creutz/marked-loop record restrictions with one debit ledger. | Structural only; not an area law, not a continuum construction by itself. |
| `HK-CYC-CLOSE` | Heat-kernel Wilson-loop source construction and continuum compatibility package. | Open/conditional unless its component estimates are proved without importing confinement. |
| `P16-LAW-IMPORT` | Paper-16 export of reflection positivity, covariance, gauge/readout compatibility, and loop-continuity data for the Wilson-loop law. | Imported structural/analytic package; not a confinement proof. |
| `AYM-CONF-CLOSE(m_*)` | Conditional area-law/confinement certificate strong enough to feed the mass-gap reduction. | Conditional until actual source constants pass. |
| `P19-CRES-DEB(c_R)` | Debited Creutz reserve lower bound after finite-battery, regulator, volume, and shape losses. | Open source estimate unless the debited liminf is proved positive. |
| `P19-KQ-SRC(W_R)` | Quotient loop-modulus/readout-control estimate relative to the moving Creutz denominator. | Open source estimate until evaluated on the same tower. |
| `R_H^opt<R_H^crit` | Heat-kernel leading-character coefficient error is below the AF-matched signal threshold. | Main Paper-20 coefficient source estimate. |
| `L_AFM^sharp<Sig_AFM` | Total decoration/transport loss is below the AF-matched direct-witness signal floor. | Main Paper-20 loss source estimate. |
| `P19-T13-CEWIN` | Character-expansion window for the leading nontrivial central coefficient and non-leading tail. | Reduced; leading sign/subunit/rate remain source estimates. |
| `P20-FROZEN-SEL` | One frozen AF trajectory, selector, character channel, windows, cutoffs, counterterm convention, and pushed-forward record law. | Structural selector; not a source inequality. |
| `P20-SEL2-TREE-RATE-GATE` | Same-record lower bound that the normalized `SEL2` block-plaquette sheet rate beats the rooted surface-polymer entropy: `q_rho gamma_rho>Theta_esc^tree` and `T_-^{SEL2}>Theta_T^tree`. | Parked open source obstruction after Papers 11--12: RG and Wilson-loop readout ledgers do not supply it. |
| `Paper-11 RG scaffold` | Conditional CYM-RG residual summability, AF locality-margin forms, perturbative trajectory tracking, and smeared Wilson-loop anchors. | Useful input ledger; not a block-plaquette coefficient-time source. |
| `Paper-12 loop-readout bridge` | Perimeter/cusp-renormalized and de-smeared Wilson-loop record control on admissible batteries. | Useful for loop-readout debits; not an area law, mass gap, confinement, or `SEL2` tree-rate source. |

For the Lorentz/locality/QFT reconstruction side, the public translations are:

| Internal phrase | Standard-language translation | Status boundary |
| --- | --- | --- |
| sampled Lorentz covariance | Equality or convergence of selected finite batteries under sampled boost data. | Not exact finite Lorentz covariance. |
| operational locality | No-signaling or boundary-flux locality for declared finite effect spaces. | Not Haag-Kastler AQFT unless the AQFT completion axioms are separately proved. |
| Schur-Hadamard gauge | Rephasing freedom of a chosen amplitude lift over fixed `Gamma`. | Not physical gauge freedom unless the lift class is unitary/circuit/physical-gauge controlled. |

## V3 Success Levels

### Level 1: restricted interacting relativistic ISP

V3 succeeds at Level 1 if it proves a projective interacting finite-to-continuum theorem for at least one nontrivial local interacting benchmark.

Minimum target:

```math
P\Gamma_{\mathrm{int}}^{\mathrm{fine}}
=
\Gamma_{\mathrm{int}}^{\mathrm{coarse}}P+o(1),
```

with controlled inverse propagation to

```math
PJ_R^{\mathrm{fine}}=J_R^{\mathrm{coarse}}P+o(1),
\quad\text{and}\quad
PE_{R,S}^{\mathrm{fine}}=E_{R,S}^{\mathrm{coarse}}P+o(1).
```

and a nonzero interacting exchange-curvature or locality theorem.

### Level 2: continuum QFT interface

V3 succeeds at Level 2 if it proves either:

1. a reconstruction theorem for a restricted known continuum QFT class from a
   declared projective ISP kernel/instrument/enrichment package; or
2. a no-go theorem showing exactly which additional data beyond `Gamma` are
   unavoidable.

This should include local observable/cylinder-effect structure, not only
transition matrices. It should also explicitly compare itself to the V2 Papers
6-9 ledger: if the theorem needs lift, phase, polarization, CAR, or instrument
data, it is an enriched reconstruction theorem, not Gamma-only reconstruction.

### Level 3: non-Abelian gauge benchmark

V3 succeeds at Level 3 if it constructs a finite and projective non-Abelian gauge-sector ISP benchmark with:

- finite non-Abelian link state spaces or controlled representation truncations;
- exact Gauss-sector decomposition;
- center-resolved locality over boundary representations;
- localized gauge-compatible comparison maps;
- first non-Abelian exchange-defect coefficient package;
- a defined path toward representation-cutoff/refinement limits.

### Level 4: full north-star success

Full success would combine Levels 1 through 3 into a single interacting non-Abelian continuum-directed ISP whose operational local nets reconstruct or match a known continuum QFT class.

This is a long-program target, not the baseline expectation for a first V3 cycle.

## V3 Paper 1: Minimal Enriched ISP Data For Relativistic QFT Reconstruction

Suggested title:

`Minimal Enriched ISP Data for Relativistic QFT Reconstruction`

Main question:

> What is the smallest Barandes-aligned ISP data package that can carry the
> phase, orientation, CAR/Clifford, instrument, and local-net information that
> bare endpoint `Gamma` provably cannot carry?

Main job:

- define the layers: endpoint `Gamma`, projective kernels, operational
  instruments/effects, Hilbert or GNS lifts, CAR/CCR data, Clifford/principal
  symbols, and metric coefficients;
- state a minimal-enrichment axiom package and prove that each added item is
  operationally or theorem-level forced by V2 Papers 6-10;
- incorporate the Paper 10 obstruction: full signed metric data cannot be
  reconstructed from the present Born-squared `Gamma` rule;
- prove a conservativity theorem: forgetting enrichment returns the V2
  stochastic kernel architecture without Markovizing unrecorded subprocesses;
- define what later V3 papers may import as hypotheses.

Pass condition:

- a clean enrichment ledger with a theorem-level minimality/no-go rationale,
  not an informal list of QFT structures pasted onto ISP.

Fail condition:

- QFT matching still requires undeclared phases, signs, fields, or local
  observables that are not carried by any ISP datum.

Why this matters:

Paper 10 makes this the first V3 gate. Without it, later QFT reconstruction
would silently smuggle in exactly the data that bare `Gamma` lacks.

Current status, 2026-05-17:

- Draft started in
  `physics/relativistic-isp-v3-paper1-minimal-enriched-isp-data-qft-reconstruction.md`.
- The hardened pass defines the formal enriched tuple
  `D_enr=(D_Gamma,W,I,E,H,F,N,S,C,A_adm)` and the forgetful map back to
  `D_Gamma`.
- It states the conservativity theorem: forgetting enrichment returns the
  original stochastic kernel architecture and creates no hidden Markov
  divisibility.
- It states the forced-enrichment/minimality theorem using V2 Paper 6
  phase blindness, V2 Papers 7-9 free-QFT enrichment, and V2 Paper 10 signed
  metric obstruction.
- It adds three concrete witnesses: Mach-Zehnder phase, free Dirac/CAR local
  net, and signed off-diagonal metric ambiguity.
- It adds an admissibility criterion for every non-Gamma layer.
- It exports a V3 import contract for every later paper.

## V3 Paper 2: Primitive Smooth-Lapse Hypersurface Kernels

Suggested title:

`Primitive Smooth-Lapse Hypersurface Kernels in Relativistic ISP`

Main question:

> Can the log-smeared finite-slab construction from V2 Paper 1 be replaced by
