> a primitive smooth-lapse kernel construction?

Main job:

- define weighted local Hamiltonian or local kernel deformations for smooth
  lapse profiles;
- prove positivity and column-stochasticity where primitive stochastic kernels
  are claimed;
- compare primitive smooth-lapse maps with log-smeared maps;
- prove the same free stochastic-curvature limit under a weaker or physically
  clearer `Delta(a)` scaling;
- identify exactly when smooth lapse profiles require signed algebraic
  comparison maps rather than positive primitive kernels.

Pass condition:

- a primitive finite-slab theorem whose leading limit agrees with V2 Paper 1.

Fail condition:

- the log-smeared construction is the only controllable smooth-lapse finite-slab
  object, or primitive smooth-lapse kernels lose the exchange-curvature limit.

Why this matters:

Full Lorentz-covariant interacting ISP should not rest forever on a log-smearing
regularization if a more physical primitive deformation exists.

Current status, 2026-05-17:

- Draft started in
  `physics/relativistic-isp-v3-paper2-primitive-smooth-lapse-hypersurface-kernels.md`.
- The first pass imports the V3 Paper 1 contract and keeps the baseline theorem
  Gamma-level, except where randomized protocols or Hilbert diagnostics are
  explicitly declared.
- Three candidates are audited: weighted-Hamiltonian Born-squared slabs,
  declared convex-mixture whole-process kernels, and Trotterized local
  stochastic protocols.
- The positive result is a primitive convex-mixture smooth-lapse kernel for
  bounded nonnegative lapse profiles. Its normalized exchange defect recovers
  the V2 free stochastic-curvature limit under the safe V2 thin-slab scaling.
- A positive-cone-to-signed-algebra theorem now proves that positive primitive
  lapse kernels determine the full signed bilinear hypersurface-deformation
  bracket by unique cone completion/tangent extension.
- The theorem has been hardened as a continuum coefficient theorem: it states
  the strong sampled topology, uses a common auxiliary intensity `eta` for
  finite positive test families, proves cone-generation/uniqueness explicitly,
  and does not claim a finite-regulator signed primitive kernel.
- The obstruction is also explicit: arbitrary signed real lapses are not
  primitive positive kernels in this construction, and naive weighted-Hamiltonian
  smoothing gives the nonlinear/signless coefficient `c_theta=theta(2-theta)`
  rather than a linear lapse coefficient.
- Current verdict: primitive smooth-lapse kernels work at the positive-cone
  leading-curvature level, while full signed smooth-lapse algebra is recovered
  as the algebraic tangent/comparison bracket generated by the positive cone,
  not as a primitive negative-probability operation.

## V3 Paper 3: Interacting Projective Kernel And Inverse-Control Theorem

Suggested title:

`Interacting Projective Kernel Dynamics and Comparison-Map Inverse Control`

Main question:

> Can local interacting finite dynamics preserve projective compatibility after
> Born-squared projection and algebraic inversion?

Main job:

- choose a controlled interacting benchmark class, such as finite-range lattice
  fermions, lattice scalar fields with cutoff, or an interacting Dirac chain;
- prove primitive-kernel refinement estimates;
- bound `Gamma_0^{-1}` in a regulator-stable regime;
- bound `J_R`, `J_R^{-1}`, and `E_{R,S}` under refinement;
- prove a quasilocality or controlled-tail theorem for interacting comparison
  maps;
- identify whether Lieb-Robinson-type bounds survive Born-squared projection
  and inversion.

Pass condition:

- a theorem transferring local interacting Hamiltonian assumptions into
  projective comparison-map and exchange-defect control.

Fail condition:

- inverses blow up or delocalize generically, making raw interacting comparison
  maps unusable for continuum relativistic dynamics.

Why this matters:

This is the first serious gate toward full Lorentz-covariant interacting ISP.

Current status, 2026-05-17:

- Draft started in
  `physics/relativistic-isp-v3-paper3-interacting-projective-kernel-inverse-control.md`.
- The draft imports V2 Paper 3's LC-log/local inverse calculus rather than
  relying on global inverse norms or a Lieb-Robinson shortcut.
- It defines the V3 interacting projective setup with primitive residuals
  `R_0`, `R_R` and the crucial reference-renormalized residuals
  `R_*(Gamma_0^b)^{-1}`.
- Hypothesis IC separates two burdens: LC-log inverse locality for `J_R` and
  `J_R^{-1}`, and projective residual estimates strong enough to survive the
  fine reference inverse.
- The transfer theorem proves
  `P J_R^b-J_R^a P = Rhat_R-J_R^a Rhat_0`, giving projective compatibility of
  comparison maps when renormalized residuals vanish.
- The inverse theorem propagates the estimate to `J_R^{-1}`, and the exchange
  theorem propagates it to `E_{R,S}` by a telescoping product/corridor norm
  estimate.
- A bounded interacting qudit/Dirac-chain surrogate benchmark has now been
  added. It uses declared projective fibers
  `X_b=X_a \times Y_ab` and marginal readouts `P_ab`, not Markov time-slicing.
  For tensor-sum whole-process lifts
  `H_*^b=H_*^a \otimes I + I \otimes K_*^{ab}`, the primitive residuals
  `R_0,R_R` and the reference-renormalized residuals vanish exactly.
- V2 Proposition 10 supplies uniform LC-log constants for that bounded
  finite-range/common-collar benchmark, so `J_R`, `J_R^{-1}`, and `E_{R,S}`
  are exactly projectively compatible and retain the exchange-corridor tail.
- The draft also states the real spatial Dirac-chain gate: for lattice
  refinements with block readouts, one must prove marked-KP activity mismatch
  bounds, called Hypothesis SR. This avoids global inverse estimates and keeps
  the proof whole-process/Barandes-aligned.
- Hypothesis SR has now been proved for a named dyadic occupation-block
  marginal in the thin-slab regime for hopping scale `1/a`. With
  `theta(a)=Delta(a)/a -> 0`, the activity mismatch satisfies
  `eta_0,eta_R = O(theta(a)^2 + Delta(a)^2 |g_a|^2)`, hence `J_R`,
  `J_R^{-1}`, and `E_{R,S}` are projectively controlled after block readout.
- The same section records the obstruction to an all-mode fixed nonzero
  `Delta/a` theorem for the naive dyadic marginal: unresolved high-frequency
  fine modes leave an `O((Delta/a)^2)` local block mismatch. A fixed-ratio
  theorem needs a declared low-momentum/smooth-sector readout or a
  Wilson/staggered/doubler-controlled regulator.
- The low-momentum route has now been added. It declares an accept/reject
  Fourier-sector instrument, defines the accepted readout
  `P_ab^low = Gamma(B_ab^low)` between shared low physical modes, proves
  low-sector stability for `Delta(a)/a -> lambda` under
  `a^2 Lambda(a)^3 -> 0`, `a Lambda(a)->0`, smooth collars, and
  `a|g_a|->0`, and proves fixed-ratio SR on the accepted smooth sector with
  error
  `O(a^2 Lambda(a)^3 + tau_N(a) + a|g_a| + |Delta(a)/a-lambda|)`.
- The SR estimates have now been pushed through Theorems 7.1, 8.1, and 9.1:
  both the thin-slab dyadic route and the fixed-ratio low-momentum route give
  explicit projective residual bounds for `J_R`, `J_R^{-1}`, and `E_{R,S}`
  with the same vanishing error scale.
- The all-mode regulator gap has been closed at the projective-kernel level by
  a detail-preserving staggered block readout. Instead of marginalizing
  `2n,2n+1` into one coarse site, it maps them to `(n,0)` and `(n,1)`,
  retaining the UV/detail label as an explicit record. For the transported
  staggered Hamiltonian this gives exact all-mode SR and exact transfer through
  `J_R`, `J_R^{-1}`, and `E_{R,S}` at fixed `Delta/a`, provided the
  dimensionless KP activity remains small.
- The Wilson/staggered continuum interpretation has also been added. A Wilson
  term gives the detail/doubler branch an `O(1/a)` mass gap, so it decouples
  from finite-energy tests; without a Wilson term, the retained detail branch
  is a declared staggered taste/species, so the continuum target is multi-taste
  unless an additional taste-removal structure is supplied.
- The detail-preserving and Wilson branches have now both been advanced. Paper
  3 proves a common-trunk obstruction theorem: any exact all-mode readout that
  identifies fine states with different outgoing coarse fluxes fails unless it
  retains the detail label, declares a reject/instrument record, or works in a
  vanishing-mismatch regime. On the Wilson branch, fixed finite-particle and
  fixed finite-energy sectors have no detail excitations for small cutoff, and
  physical/detail mixing is suppressed by the Wilson gap under
  `a||V_a||_{tested}->0`. On the staggered branch, the same retained detail
  label reconstructs a multi-taste finite-particle CAR target rather than a
  hidden single-species target.
- Paper 3 now also states the conditional QFT interface. On the Wilson branch,
  if smearing maps, polarizations, lattice propagators, and tested effective
  interactions converge, then finite local CAR polynomial expectations
  converge to the single-species Dirac target and the local-CAR net converges
  on the declared test class. On the staggered branch, the analogous
  representation data converge to a multi-taste CAR target. The operational
  bridge is explicit: raw `J_R`, `J_R^{-1}`, and `E_{R,S}` feed measurable QFT
  predictions only after compatible instrument/effect functionals are
  declared.
- Paper 3 has now made that interface concrete for the free one-dimensional
  Dirac-chain benchmark. It defines Wilson band-limited smearing maps,
  proves physical one-particle convergence with error
  `a Lambda(a)^2+a^2 Lambda(a)^3+tail`, proves Wilson polarization convergence
  for the massive branch, and proves Wilson propagator convergence on finite
  time/test-function windows. It also defines Wilson-admissible interactions
  and proves the Feshbach correction bound showing when detail modes do not
  alter tested continuum interactions. In parallel, it defines the staggered
  two-branch smearing map and proves smearing, polarization, and propagator
  convergence to the two-taste target. A formal V3 Paper 4 import contract now
  separates what later papers may use from what remains open.
- Current verdict: Paper 3 now has a positive exact interacting projective
  benchmark, a proved thin-slab spatial block theorem for `1/a` hopping, and a
  fixed-ratio low-momentum accepted-branch theorem carried all the way through
  comparison maps, inverses, and exchange defects. It also has a non-naive
  all-mode fixed-ratio regulator theorem when the UV/detail label is retained.
  The boundary is sharp: naive all-mode dyadic marginalization fails; declared
  low-sector refinement and detail-preserving all-mode refinement work in their
  stated scopes; Wilson gives the best single-species finite-energy route;
  staggered gives the honest multi-taste route; and the free QFT interface is
  now concrete for smooth finite test families. The next hard burdens are
  sharp deleted-bond collars, explaining why this enriched representation
  package is selected from the ISP ontology rather than merely declared,
  nonperturbative interacting vacuum/local-net convergence, full Lorentz
  covariance, and gauge/non-Abelian cutoff stability.

## V3 Paper 4: Detail-Sector Options And Interacting Stochastic Curvature

Suggested title:

`Detail-Sector Options and Interacting Stochastic Curvature in Relativistic ISP`

Draft:

`relativistic-isp-v3-paper4-two-branch-interacting-stochastic-curvature.md`

Main question:

> Does the exchange-defect curvature theorem survive a genuine interaction in
> both the Wilson single-species branch and the no-Wilson staggered
> multi-taste branch, and what are all Barandes-aligned ways of handling the
> retained detail sector?

Candidate targets:

1. Wilson branch: detail-preserving all-mode regulator plus Wilson gap plus a
   bounded local density-density interaction;
2. staggered branch: detail-preserving all-mode regulator without Wilson, with
   the retained detail sector interpreted as physical taste;
3. operational taste projection: a declared accept/reject instrument selecting
   one taste sector without silently erasing the reject sector;
4. dynamical taste-breaking: declared interactions that split, mix, or mass
   taste sectors;
5. branch comparison: identify exactly when Wilson, staggered, projection, and
   taste-breaking curvature predictions agree or differ.

Main job:

- define branchwise interacting coefficient curvature
  `C_b[N,M;g]=[K_b[N;g],K_b[M;g]]`;
- state and then prove under explicit ICURV hypotheses the expansion
  ```text
  free curvature + g mixed curvature + g^2 interaction curvature;
  ```
- derive the `Delta^2` Born-squared coefficient
  `Q(H)_{xy}=|H_{xy}|^2` and compute the first interaction coefficient
  `B_R=DQ_{H_R}(V_R)-DQ_{H_0}(V_0)`;
- prove the Wilson density-density benchmark is Wilson-admissible on fixed
  finite-particle finite-energy tests;
- prove diagonal density-density interactions have zero first mixed curvature
  at leading `Delta^2` coefficient scope;
- derive the delayed `Delta^4` comparison-map coefficient for diagonal
  phase-like interactions and show that their first linear exchange-curvature
  contribution appears at order `gDelta^6`;
- state the delayed theorem as a finite-cutoff normed coefficient result with
  explicit remainder control, and keep the continuum limit as a separate
  branch-specific estimate;
- isolate off-diagonal interactions as the interactions with immediate
  `Delta^2` mixed curvature and density-density interactions as delayed
  whole-process curvature;
- prove Wilson detail-sector curvature is suppressed by the Wilson gap;
- prove the staggered branch gives a two-taste interacting curvature theorem,
  not a hidden single-species theorem;
- prove operational projection gives conditional selected-taste curvature,
  not all-mode single-species curvature;
- prove dynamical taste-breaking creates physical curvature channels unless a
  declared heavy-taste gap or instrument removes them;
- prove an option-comparison theorem: agreement requires declared taste-blind
  or taste-projected instruments and taste-preserving interactions.

Pass condition:

- all detail-sector options are laid out in the same projective-kernel
  language, with honest branch-specific targets: Wilson single-species,
  no-Wilson multi-taste, operationally projected selected taste, and
  dynamically split/mixed/heavy taste.

Fail condition:

- the Wilson branch works only by silently erasing detail, or the staggered
  branch/projection/taste-breaking options are left unexamined; either failure
  would break the Barandes-aligned ontology.

Why this matters:

Free curvature is not enough. A relativistic physics theory needs interacting
curvature, and the Wilson route should not be allowed to obscure the
detail-preserving no-Wilson route or the other honest ways a retained detail
sector can be handled. Paper 4 therefore pushes both main dynamical branches
and lays out the projection/taste-breaking option space explicitly.

Current status:

- first pass created in
  `relativistic-isp-v3-paper4-two-branch-interacting-stochastic-curvature.md`;
- primitive coefficient derivation added: at `Delta^2`,
  `Gamma(e^{-iDelta H})=I+Delta^2 Q(H)+...` with
  `Q(H)_{xy}=|H_{xy}|^2`, so
  `B_R=DQ_{H_R^{(0)}}(V_R)-DQ_{H_0^{(0)}}(V_0)`;
- Wilson branch: density-density interaction shown Wilson-admissible on fixed
  finite-particle finite-energy tests, but because it is diagonal its first
  `Delta^2` interaction coefficient is zero; its first primitive signature is
  a derived delayed `Delta^4` comparison coefficient with finite-cutoff
  `O(Delta^5)` remainder control, producing a linear exchange-curvature
  channel at order `gDelta^6`; off-diagonal Wilson interactions have an
  immediate `Delta^2` coefficient `B_R` and a mixed-curvature theorem when the
  finite-stencil continuum limit is proved; a concrete bounded off-diagonal
  mass-channel modulation now has a proved smooth-core mixed-curvature limit;
  compactly supported density-density now has a proved smooth-core delayed
  `gDelta^6` limit; the Wilson branch is decoupling by a declared
  gap/Feshbach estimate, not silent erasure of the detail block;
- staggered branch: parity-blind density-density likewise has zero first
  `Delta^2` interaction coefficient but has delayed taste-preserving and
  possible taste-mixing `gDelta^6` channels; off-diagonal or alternating
  interactions split into immediate taste-preserving and taste-mixing
  mixed-curvature channels; the same concrete bounded off-diagonal
  mass-channel modulation and compactly supported density-density interaction
  now have proved smooth-core limits; because there is no Wilson gap, taste
  channels are physical unless oscillatory averaging or a recorded instrument
  removes them;
- branch-decision data: Wilson is the better single-species comparison branch
  for standard relativistic QFT tests; no-Wilson staggered is the more direct
  Barandes-aligned retained-record branch, but it targets multi-taste QFT
  unless extra declared structure removes or projects taste data.
- operational projection: selected-taste curvature is conditional on an
  accept outcome, with the reject sector retained as process data;
- dynamical taste-breaking: taste-splitting/mixing produces physical curvature
  channels unless a declared heavy-taste gap or instrument removes them;
- option comparison theorem: Wilson, staggered, projection, and taste-breaking
  agree only after declared taste-blind/taste-projected observables, selected
  states, and matching interaction matrix elements.

## V3 Paper 5: Wilson Single-Species QFT Benchmark

Suggested title:

`Wilson Single-Species QFT Benchmark for Relativistic ISP`

Draft:

`relativistic-isp-v3-paper5-wilson-standard-qft-benchmark.md`

Main question:

> Can the Wilson branch of relativistic ISP reproduce the tested local data of
> a standard single-species Dirac/CAR QFT, including the interacting curvature
> channels developed in V3 Paper 4?

Main job:

- fix the Wilson branch as the conservative standard-QFT comparison branch;
- import the Paper 3 Wilson smearing, polarization, propagator, detail-gap,
  and Wilson-admissible interaction package;
- import the Paper 4 off-diagonal `gDelta^4` and density-density delayed
  `gDelta^6` interacting curvature channels;
- upgrade the Paper 4 smooth-core limits to tested Wilson graph-domain
  quadratic-form limits;
- extend the off-diagonal benchmark from bounded mass-channel modulation to
  Peierls current/hopping perturbations, where the link phase cancels the
  apparent `1/a` hopping divergence on the physical band;
- define Wilson-compatible local operational instruments and effect systems;
- compare the resulting finite local statistics with the standard
  single-species Dirac/CAR QFT target;
- state exactly which data are reconstructed and which are imported as
  declared enrichment.

Pass condition:

- a positive tested benchmark:
  ```text
  declared Wilson ISP data
  -> single-species Dirac/CAR local tests
  -> controlled off-diagonal and delayed density-density curvature channels.
  ```

Fail condition:

- the Wilson branch can match free local QFT but cannot carry the interacting
  curvature channels into operational local tests.

Why this matters:

This is the conservative reconstruction benchmark. If it succeeds, ISP has a
controlled route to ordinary single-species relativistic QFT data once the
Wilson enrichment package is declared. If it fails, the program cannot use the
Wilson branch as its standard-QFT comparison baseline.

Current status:

- first theorem-level draft created in
  `relativistic-isp-v3-paper5-wilson-standard-qft-benchmark.md`;
- Wilson single-species tested-QFT benchmark theorem stated;
- Paper 4 smooth-core mass-channel, Peierls-current, and delayed
  density-density limits upgraded to tested Wilson graph-domain
  quadratic-form limits, with explicit graph norm and mapping order;
- Peierls current/hopping perturbation hardened with the exact Wilson link
  variation: although bare hopping scales as `1/a`, the link variation
  contributes a compensating factor `a`, and the Wilson-term variation is
  `O(a Lambda(a))` on the physical band;
- concrete Wilson-compatible instruments added for density, current,
  exchange-defect weak probes, and detector records;
- finite benchmark-equivalence theorem added: every finite Wilson test battery
  converges to the corresponding single-species Dirac/CAR QFT prediction;
- imported-data ledger added: smearing maps, CAR/Fock functor, polarization,
  Clifford data, Wilson term, finite-energy tests, and instruments remain
  declared enrichment, not Gamma-only reconstruction.
- Gamma-only appendix added: entrywise `Gamma=|U|^2` cannot determine complex
  phase orientation or the operational instrument/effect system.

## V3 Paper 6: No-Wilson Detail-Preserving Branch

Suggested title:

`No-Wilson Detail-Preserving Branch and Taste-Record Tests in Relativistic ISP`

Draft:

`relativistic-isp-v3-paper6-no-wilson-detail-preserving-new-physics-branch.md`

Main question:

> If ISP keeps all retained detail records instead of Wilson-decoupling them,
> does the no-Wilson branch become an ordinary multi-taste QFT, an empirically
> invisible regulator sector, or a possible new operational channel?

Main job:

- develop the no-Wilson branch as the Barandes-aligned retained-record route;
- treat the detail label as physical taste/species data unless a declared
  instrument or dynamics removes it;
- prove a two-taste QFT benchmark on finite test batteries;
- classify interactions into taste-preserving, taste-mixing, taste-splitting,
  and taste-blind channels;
- prove when the no-Wilson branch reduces to the Wilson single-species
  benchmark after declared taste-blindness/projection;
- prove a difference criterion: surviving taste-mixing curvature or
  taste-resolving instruments give finite test batteries that Wilson
  single-species QFT cannot match without importing an extra internal degree
  of freedom;
- formulate an EPR-like taste-record witness that is relativistically causal
  but absent from the Wilson single-species benchmark.

Pass condition:

- a rigorous no-Wilson multi-taste benchmark plus a clear operational criterion
  for when the extra taste sector is invisible, ordinary multi-species QFT, or
  a possible ISP-specific discovery channel.

Fail condition:

- the no-Wilson branch cannot be given a coherent operational meaning beyond
  a regulator artifact, or its proposed differences require silently erasing
  or importing data contrary to Barandes discipline.

Why this matters:

Paper 5 gives the conservative route to standard single-species QFT. Paper 6
is the place to ask whether ISP is more general than standard QFT in an
operationally meaningful way. Any "EPR moment" must happen here: retained
records produce measurable correlations or curvature channels that the
single-species benchmark lacks.

Current status:

- completed theorem-level draft created in
  `relativistic-isp-v3-paper6-no-wilson-detail-preserving-new-physics-branch.md`;
- no-Wilson multi-taste benchmark theorem stated;
- Wilson-reduction theorem stated: agreement with Paper 5 requires declared
  taste-blindness, projection with reject records, or vanishing taste-mixing
  coefficients;
- difference criterion stated for taste-resolving or taste-mixing curvature
  probes;
- microscopic taste-resolving instruments added via the two-site staggered
  block field: finite cutoff operators `T_a^i(f)` converge to continuum taste
  Pauli bilinears;
- taste-preparation control added: declared finite CAR source instruments can
  prepare one-taste states and the two-region taste singlet on finite test
  batteries;
- empirical regime theorem added: the no-Wilson branch is taste-inaccessible,
  ordinary multi-species QFT, selected-taste Wilson reduction with recorded
  rejects, or an ISP-retained-record discovery branch depending on the declared
  instruments and surviving taste-mixing coefficients;
- detector-hardware bridge added: finite block-local pointer arrays implement
  the spectral instruments of `T_a^\theta(f)` at cutoff, with `\tau_z` as
  site-imbalance readout and `\tau_x,\tau_y` requiring phase-coherent
  intra-block access;
- taste-resolving causality theorem added: spacelike separated taste detector
  instruments commute, give no-signaling marginals, and are detector-order
  foliation independent; full interacting foliation dependence is reduced to
  the exchange-collar estimate targeted by Paper 7;
- finite discriminator battery added: a taste-record CHSH test separates the
  no-Wilson branch from a Wilson single-species comparison by
  `2 sqrt(2) V+o(1)` in the ideal taste channel, with a classical-detector
  loophole threshold `V>1/sqrt2`;
- hardware protocol completion added: the pointer detector is tied to a
  two-mode analyzer pattern, where coherent local rotations plus number
  readout implement `t_a^\theta`; finite-battery statistics are stable under
  calibrated operator-norm hardware errors;
- finite-battery foliation theorem added: under Hypothesis EC, summable
  exchange-collar defects imply foliation-independent continuum limits for all
  Paper-6 taste batteries, including reject/no-click records;
- gauge compatibility added: gauge-covariant taste readout is obtained by
  inserting the local parallel transporter across the two block sites; the
  resulting taste effects preserve finite Gauss sectors;
- final taste-sector classification added: the no-Wilson branch is exactly one
  of taste-blind regulator sector, ordinary multi-taste QFT, selected-taste
  Wilson reduction with recorded rejects, or ISP-retained-record channel;
- EPR-like taste-record witness added: a two-region taste singlet gives the
  standard CHSH value `2 sqrt(2)` for taste-resolving instruments, while the
  Wilson single-species benchmark has no corresponding taste operators;
- status boundary stated: Paper 6 is internally complete as a finite-battery
  no-Wilson/taste branch, but its beyond-QFT reading remains conditional on a
  real physical system supplying the retained detail channel as an operational
  record.

## V3 Paper 7: Interacting Lorentz Covariance And Foliation Independence

Suggested title:

`Foliation Independence for Interacting Projective ISP Kernels`

Draft:

`relativistic-isp-v3-paper7-foliation-independence-interacting-projective-kernels.md`

Main question:

> Can interacting projective kernels satisfy a genuine hypersurface-path
> equivalence theorem?

Main job:

- define regulated hypersurface paths and endpoint kernels;
- prove path equivalence up to projective tangential corrections generated by
  exchange curvature;
- control local detector/instrument insertions along different foliations;
- identify the relation to Poincare covariance in flat background;
- prove a restricted Lorentz-covariant interacting ISP theorem, or isolate the
  obstruction.

Pass condition:

- a genuine foliation-independence theorem for at least one interacting
  projective benchmark.

Fail condition:

- exchange curvature cannot be integrated into a consistent projective
  path-equivalence law.

Why this matters:

This is the direct route from local interacting kernels to relativistic QFT
behavior. It should happen before the full QFT reconstruction theorem, because
the latter should not have to guess whether the foliation law exists.

Current status:

- theorem-level draft created in
  `relativistic-isp-v3-paper7-foliation-independence-interacting-projective-kernels.md`;
- regulated hypersurface protocols defined as declared endpoint comparison
  protocols, not hidden Markov time slicings;
- finite causal linear-extension lemma added: different causal-compatible
  hypersurface orders reduce to adjacent swaps of incomparable/spacelike collars;
- adjacent spacelike swap theorem proved: path-order probability differences
  are bounded by the corresponding exchange defect `E_{C,D}-I`;
- detector adjacent swaps are exact for locally commuting spacelike detector
  collars;
- path-summability theorem proved: summable exchange defects imply
  foliation-independent finite-battery continuum statistics;
- controlled exchange-collar condition CEC stated and shown to imply Paper-6
  Hypothesis EC;
- CEC verified for the smooth-collar low-sector branch, the Wilson finite-energy
  branch under Wilson-admissible conditions, and the no-Wilson taste branch when
  its dynamical collars satisfy the same bound;
- asymptotic finite-battery Lorentz covariance theorem stated: sampled
  Lorentz-related batteries agree in the continuum when representation data
  transform covariantly;
- obstruction theorem added: non-summable exchange defects are a precise failure
  mode for relativistic ISP on the tested class.

## V3 Paper 8: Continuum QFT Reconstruction Or Sharp No-Go

Suggested title:

`Continuum QFT Reconstruction and No-Go Theorems for Enriched Relativistic ISP`

Draft:

`relativistic-isp-v3-paper8-continuum-qft-reconstruction-no-go.md`

Main question:

> Are projective ISP kernel, instrument, and minimal-enrichment data sufficient
> to reconstruct known local QFT structures?

Main job:

- use V3 Paper 1's minimal data package as the allowed input;
- attempt reconstruction of a Hilbert representation, local algebras, field
  correlators, scattering data, or Wightman/Haag-Kastler-style structure;
- identify what is fixed by `Gamma`, what is fixed by instruments, and what
  requires phase/lift/CAR/Clifford data;
- use V2 Papers 6-10 as the baseline audit: Gamma-only no-go, free-QFT
  enrichment gates, sampled Lorentz completion, spacetime local-net matching,
  and Gamma-level metric obstruction;
- prove a reconstruction theorem for a restricted class, or a no-go theorem
  showing unavoidable missing data.

Pass condition:

- a nontrivial reconstruction theorem for a known free or controlled
  interacting QFT class, or a mathematically sharp no-go theorem.

Fail condition:

- no stable bridge from ISP kernels to local QFT observables or correlations
  can be defined without reintroducing standard QFT as primitive.

Why this matters:

This is the central test for whether ISP is a reconstruction program for QFT or
a useful stochastic representation layer below ordinary QFT.

Current status:

- theorem-level draft created;
- layer-typed reconstruction rule added: Gamma-only reconstruction,
  operational reconstruction, and enriched QFT matching are kept distinct;
- finite-battery local-net reconstruction definition added;
- positive enriched operational local-net reconstruction theorem proved;
- Wilson single-species finite-battery Dirac/CAR local-net matching theorem
  stated and proved on the declared test class;
- no-Wilson local-net classification theorem added: taste-blind quotient,
  multi-taste net, selected-taste Wilson reduction, or retained-record channel;
- Gamma-only no-go theorem proved for full relativistic QFT reconstruction;
- representation existence separated from reconstruction by corollary;
- final V3 QFT status theorem stated: ISP has a controlled enriched interface
  to restricted QFT finite-battery local-net data, but not a full interacting
  continuum QFT reconstruction from bare Gamma;
- export to Paper 9 fixed: the next target is finite non-Abelian gauge ISP,
  not continuum Yang-Mills.

## V3 Paper 9: Finite Non-Abelian Gauge ISP Benchmark

Suggested title:

`Finite Non-Abelian Gauge Sectors in Relativistic ISP`

Draft:

`relativistic-isp-v3-paper9-finite-nonabelian-gauge-sectors.md`

Main question:

> Can non-Abelian gauge structure be formulated at the finite `Gamma`, `J`, and
> `E` levels, with the necessary sector/enrichment data declared?

Main job:

- choose a conservative non-Abelian target: finite group gauge theory, `SU(2)`
  quantum-link truncation, or a Peter-Weyl representation cutoff;
- define matter-plus-link configuration spaces;
- define local gauge transformations and Gauss constraints;
- prove exact primitive-kernel block decomposition by gauge sectors;
- identify boundary representation centers for local regions;
- define gauge-compatible localized deformations and comparison maps;
- compute the first non-Abelian mixed exchange coefficient.

Pass condition:

- an exact finite non-Abelian ISP gauge benchmark with localized comparison maps
  and exchange defects.

Fail condition:

- non-Abelian constraints make finite stochastic kernel/comparison-map structure
  nonlocal or noninvertible beyond repair.

Why this matters:

This is the first realistic non-Abelian target. It should not try to be
continuum Yang-Mills yet.

Current status:

- theorem-level finite benchmark draft created with named target `S_3`;
- finite gauge ontology defined: matter variables on sites, gauge variables on
  links, local gauge transformations, and physical orbit space;
- one-plaquette model made explicit: gauge fixing gives
  `Omega_square^phys congruent S_3^4` with `6^4=1296` physical endpoints;
- gauge-invariant local records defined: plaquette class functions,
  matter-link class functions, and declared charged transport probes;
- Gauss/boundary-center labels defined for regions, with a proof that local
  gauge-invariant records only see the complement through the boundary center;
- finite gauge-action Gibbs weight constructed from plaquette and matter-link
  class functions;
- full-rank sectorwise lazy heat-bath reference kernel derived from that finite
  gauge action, with explicit sectorwise inverse;
- optional finite two-endpoint transfer reference added, with inverse bound
  `(1-2 epsilon)^(-1)` for `0<epsilon<1/2`;
- gauge-compatible deformations and comparison maps `J_R=Gamma_R Gamma_0^{-1}`
  defined sectorwise;
- charged instruments defined as positive finite stochastic record kernels
  plus typed charged readout maps;
- exact sectorwise decomposition theorem proved for kernels, comparison maps,
  and exchange defects;
- finite local nonfactorization corollary added: local gauge ISP factors only
  after conditioning on boundary centers;
- center-conditioned gluing theorem added:
  physical regional algebras glue as a direct sum over boundary-center labels,
  not as an unconditional tensor product;
- first mixed exchange coefficient computed as `C_{R,S}=[A_S,A_R]`;
- scalar class-function probes shown not to carry the non-Abelian
  representation-commutator component;
- scalar-probe no-faking theorem added: class functions satisfy `c(ab)=c(ba)`
  and cannot detect oriented matrix-ordering curvature;
- charged transport probes shown to produce an explicit nonzero `S_3`
  coefficient using the standard two-dimensional representation;
- one-plaquette `S_3` example added with measured charged-channel scalar
  coefficient `-\sqrt{3}`;
- separated-support onset result proved exactly for the finite local benchmark;
- Wilson/no-Wilson gauge-coupling fork clarified: Paper 9 is the finite gauge
  layer common to both branches, not a fermion-continuum theorem for either;
- finite Wilson-gauge and no-Wilson detail-preserving gauge blocks added, with
  gauge-covariance proofs;
- Paper-10 export contract theorem added, explicitly listing allowed imports
  and forbidden continuum claims;
- Paper-9 pass theorem stated: finite non-Abelian ISP yes, continuum
  Yang-Mills not yet.

## V3 Paper 10: Projective Non-Abelian Gauge Continuum Program

Suggested title:

`Projective Non-Abelian Gauge Kernels and Representation-Cutoff Limits`

Draft:

`relativistic-isp-v3-paper10-projective-nonabelian-gauge-continuum.md`

Main question:

> Can the finite non-Abelian benchmark survive representation-cutoff and lattice
> refinement?

Main job:

- define projective maps between representation cutoffs;
- preserve Gauss sectors and boundary representation centers under refinement;
- prove primitive-kernel compatibility or asymptotic compatibility;
- control reference-kernel inverses and comparison maps in fixed sectors;
- identify the continuum covariant derivative or field-strength target in
  exchange-defect data.

Pass condition:

- a controlled representation-cutoff/refinement theorem for a non-Abelian
  benchmark.

Fail condition:

- boundary representation centers, inverse control, or truncation errors cannot
  be made projectively compatible.

Why this matters:

This is the bridge from finite non-Abelian gauge ISP to continuum non-Abelian
gauge theory.

Current status:

- theorem-level projective-cutoff draft created;
- `SU(2)` Peter-Weyl finite-battery route chosen as the primary continuum-facing
  regulator;
- ontology clarified: Peter-Weyl cutoff is a finite declared
  observable/effect battery over a compact endpoint space, not a finite hidden
  state space;
- finite Gauss-invariant batteries defined by Haar gauge averaging;
- boundary representation centers defined by cut-link irreps and intertwiners;
- cutoff-stability theorem proved: Peter-Weyl projections commute with gauge
  averaging and preserve retained boundary-center labels;
- representation-cutoff and lattice-coarsening projective maps defined;
- Hypothesis PC stated for finite-battery projectivity under combined
  representation/lattice refinement;
- reference heat-bath kernel restricted to finite batteries defined, with
  explicit inverse and uniform bound;
- Hypothesis KCOMP stated for primitive kernel and reference-inverse
  compatibility;
- projective comparison-map transfer theorem proved under PC/KCOMP;
- exchange-defect compatibility corollary proved under uniform boundedness;
- smooth-background field-strength target theorem proved by BCH:
  charged plaquette transport yields `F_{mu nu}`;
- charged exchange-coefficient limit proved conditionally under
  `a^{-2}`-small residuals;
- finite-battery Yang-Mills target conditions defined through Wilson-loop test
  functionals, reflection positivity, gauge invariance, and OS-type continuity;
- heat-kernel lattice gauge measure added as the conservative Euclidean
  finite-lattice target, with gauge invariance and reflection positivity;
- YM-LIM stated as the honest continuum Yang-Mills scaling-window hypothesis;
- standard-facing finite Wilson gauge-matter target added: `SU(2)`
  heat-kernel gauge fields coupled to a typed Wilson-Dirac finite matter
  battery, with gauge-invariant source contractions, bilinears, and optional
  determinant records only when the determinant/sign prescription is declared;
- finite Wilson gauge-matter records proved gauge-compatible by finite
  conjugation covariance of the Wilson-Dirac block;
- exact two-dimensional heat-kernel plaquette blocking theorem proved:
  blocked plaquettes satisfy `K_t * K_s = K_{t+s}`;
- one-step 2D renormalization residual shown to vanish on scalar Wilson-loop
  batteries under heat-kernel time addition;
- higher-dimensional renormalization isolated as Hypothesis RG-D rather than
  hidden inside projectivity;
- RG-D shown to imply primitive kernel compatibility for bounded local
  finite-instrument tilts;
- exact finite-battery perfect blocking theorem added in arbitrary dimension:
  push forward the whole fine process to the declared coarse battery and the
  one-step residual is exactly zero;
- local-action higher-dimensional RG identified as the real gate: replacing
  the exact perfect block by a heat-kernel/Wilson/improved local ansatz costs
  the explicit finite-battery residual `delta_locRG`;
- concrete four-dimensional local-RG battery added: plaquette, rectangle,
  chair/parallelogram Wilson loops, charged plaquette curvature records,
  Wilson matter records, and finite products up to declared degree;
- local coarse ansatz family added: plaquette/character, rectangle,
  chair/parallelogram, clover-curvature, and Wilson-matter counterterm
  operators;
- response matrix and missing-direction error defined:
  `C_{i alpha}=Cov(F_i,A_alpha)` and `epsilon_perp` measures the part of the
  perfect-block displacement not spanned by the chosen local operators;
- response-rank criterion proved: full tested rank is equivalent to no
  non-null tested record combination being covariance-orthogonal to every
  ansatz operator; if the centered ansatz span contains the centered battery
  modulo null relations, rank holds;
- finite-battery local projection theorem proved: under tested response-rank
  and second-order bounds, a local parameter shift matches the perfect block
  up to perpendicular error plus a quadratic remainder;
- explicit `delta_locRG` bound proved with finite-battery norm constant,
  perpendicular error, quadratic response error, and declared tail error;
- local residual propagated into `KCOMP`, comparison-map residuals, and
  exchange-defect residuals;
- missing-direction diagnostics added for scalar Wilson loops, charged
  curvature records, Wilson matter source contractions, and no-Wilson
  taste/detail records;
- local ansatz completion rule added: add a symmetry-allowed local operator,
  record branch-specific data, declare a nonlocal perfect-block obstruction,
  or quotient a redundant battery direction; no silent fifth option;
- iterative finite-battery local RG algorithm added: compute perfect-block
  moments, compute response matrix, solve for the local parameter shift,
  measure residuals, complete the ansatz or record the obstruction, then
  iterate until tolerance or stable obstruction;
- scalar tiny-battery closure theorem added: matched plaquette/rectangle/chair
  loop terms close scalar loop records to first order when the scalar
  covariance matrix is nondegenerate after quotienting exact identities;
- charged curvature closure theorem added: scalar class-function terms fail
  on the traceless charged channel, while charged clover/source-sink terms
  close the finite charged battery under enlarged covariance rank;
- Wilson matter closure theorem added: pure gauge loops do not generally span
  Wilson-Dirac source contractions; Wilson-matter source/counterterm operators
  close the finite matter battery under enlarged covariance rank;
- first branch outcome table added: scalar gauge closes under rank; charged
  gauge requires framed instruments; Wilson matter requires matter operators;
  no-Wilson detail requires recorded taste/detail handling or becomes a
  measurable branch difference;
- Wilson/no-Wilson local-RG split added: Wilson succeeds on finite batteries
  when response rank and tail control hold; no-Wilson must include
  taste/detail operators or else the omitted signal appears as a measurable
  perpendicular response channel;
- Gamma-only gauge reconstruction no-go proved: scalar Gamma gauge data can
  recover conjugacy-class statistics but not framed charged holonomies or full
  non-Abelian connections;
- Wilson and no-Wilson branches kept typed through the same gauge projective
  layer;
- finite dynamical matter boundary added: determinant/reweighting prescriptions
  are admissible finite normalized functionals when declared and integrable
  and are positive states only under an explicitly nonnegative prescription;
  they do not yet prove continuum QCD, anomaly control, or OS reconstruction;
- Paper-10 pass theorem stated: projective non-Abelian finite-battery gauge
  cutoff control yes; full continuum Yang-Mills not yet.

## V3 Paper 11: Continuum Yang-Mills And Non-Abelian RG Closure

Suggested title:

`Finite-Battery Non-Abelian RG Closure Toward Continuum Yang-Mills`

Draft:

`relativistic-isp-v3-paper11-continuum-yang-mills-nonabelian-rg-closure.md`

Main question:

> Can the finite-battery local-RG closure machinery of Paper 10 be pushed into
> a genuine continuum Yang-Mills scaling window?

Main job:

- choose explicit increasing four-dimensional Wilson-loop and charged-curvature
  batteries;
- analyze whether the local ansatz completion algorithm closes under
  symmetry-allowed gauge operators as the batteries grow;
- prove or isolate the scaling behavior of `delta_locRG` along a running
  coupling path;
- connect finite-battery reflection positivity, gauge invariance, and
  Euclidean covariance to a Yang-Mills candidate functional;
- determine whether Wilson matter records can be included without destroying
  positivity, locality, or residual control;
- state the exact remaining gates for continuum Yang-Mills, QCD, mass gap, and
  OS/Wightman reconstruction.

Pass condition:

- a theorem or conditional theorem showing that a growing family of finite
  non-Abelian test batteries has local-action residuals
  `delta_locRG -> 0` under a declared scaling path, with reflection positivity
  and gauge covariance preserved on the tested class.

Fail condition:

- the local ansatz completion algorithm stabilizes at a nonlocal perfect-block
  obstruction, an unavoidable charged/taste retained-record residue, or a
  positivity/sign problem that prevents a Yang-Mills/QCD continuum target.

Why this matters:

Paper 10 proves that the finite problem is well-posed. Paper 11 is where the
hard continuum gauge question actually lives: whether finite-battery local
closure survives the growing-battery/scaling limit.

Initial Paper-11 tasks:

1. Define a nested sequence of four-dimensional finite batteries:
   scalar loops, charged curvature probes, Wilson matter probes, and optional
   no-Wilson detail probes.
2. Define a nested local operator basis:
   plaquette, rectangle, chair/parallelogram, clover, higher Wilson loops,
   gauge-fixing-free improvement terms, and Wilson matter counterterms.
3. Prove finite-step monotonicity or a counterexample for the completion
   algorithm: adding symmetry-allowed local terms should not increase the
   best finite-battery residual.
4. Estimate the scaling of `epsilon_perp`, `epsilon_tail`, and the quadratic
   response term for small lattice spacing.
5. Identify which residuals are merely truncation artifacts and which are
   genuine nonlocal perfect-block obstructions.
6. Separate pure Yang-Mills, valence Wilson matter, and dynamical Wilson matter
   targets.
7. State the precise theorem needed for OS reconstruction from the limiting
   finite-battery Schwinger/Wilson-loop functionals.
8. Keep the Barandes discipline: no hidden Markov divisibility, no Gamma-only
   charged reconstruction, and no untyped fermion/gauge enrichment.

Current status:

- Paper-11 draft created with the full 1-12 structure;
- Paper-10 import contract stated explicitly, including finite Peter-Weyl
  batteries, perfect blocking, local-action residuals, response-rank theorem,
  tiny-battery closure tests, and Gamma-only no-go;
- nested scalar, charged, Wilson matter, and no-Wilson detail-preserving
  finite batteries defined;
- nested local operator bases defined for pure gauge, Wilson matter, and
  no-Wilson detail branches;
- finite-step monotonicity theorem proved: enlarging the local ansatz cannot
  increase the best finite-battery residual;
- finite-battery closure/obstruction dichotomy proved from monotone residual
  convergence;
- sharp CYM-RG scaling-window hypothesis stated, replacing vague continuum
  Yang-Mills claims with a residual ledger:
  `delta_locRG + epsilon_tail + epsilon_proj + epsilon_OS + epsilon_Euc -> 0`;
- CYM-RG broadened into subsequential and strong versions: subsequential
  CYM-RG is enough for a subsequential Wilson-loop interface, while strong
  CYM-RG adds uniqueness of subsequential limits on the tested class;
- reflection positivity and gauge invariance separated: gauge invariance is
  preserved by gauge-invariant completions, while reflection positivity remains
  an explicit gate;
- diagonal compactness theorem proved for countable bounded Wilson-loop tests:
  every refinement sequence has a subsequence on which all tested Wilson-loop
  expectations converge;
- convergence is no longer an independent assumption for countable bounded
  Wilson-loop tests; the remaining gates are uniqueness, nontriviality,
  loop-topology continuity, and extension to unbounded charged/matter records;
- conditional Wilson-loop interface theorem broadened: subsequential CYM-RG
  gives a subsequential gauge-invariant, reflection-positive,
  Euclidean-covariant Wilson-loop functional; strong CYM-RG plus nontriviality
  and continuity upgrades it to the continuum-facing functional;
- residual-decay theorem added: if the perfect block log-density is uniformly
  approximated by the local ansatz log-density with tail `eta`, then the
  finite-battery residual is bounded by `exp(2 eta)-1`;
- exponential local expansion tails shown to imply exponential residual decay;
- strong-coupling local expansion program added: define a four-dimensional
  `SU(2)` heat-kernel strong-coupling regime, state SC-KP polymer smallness,
  and prove that SC-KP gives an exponentially decaying perfect-block local
  expansion tail;
- SC-KP import/verification strengthened: heat-kernel character smallness
  gives an explicit finite-block KP criterion for fixed block ratio, finite
  block depth, and finite battery; hence blocked four-dimensional `SU(2)`
  satisfies SC-KP at sufficiently large heat time;
- strong-coupling finite-battery interface theorem added: under uniform SC-KP
  plus vanishing projectivity/RP/Euclidean defects, scalar Wilson-loop
  batteries satisfy subsequential CYM-RG, with the five-gate theorem upgrading
  this to a continuum-facing interface only when uniqueness, nontriviality,
  and continuity also hold;
- asymptotic-freedom boundary sharpened: the same Haar-background character
  KP margin provably fails on the weak-coupling continuum trajectory, so
  continuum Yang-Mills requires a Balaban-style or equivalent multiscale AF
  locality-margin replacement with summable polymer tails;
- continuum-trajectory trichotomy added: literal SC-KP survival fails,
  renormalized survival means recentering into an AF locality margin, and the
  direct replacement route requires weak-coupling multiscale control plus the
  Paper-11 five gates;
- one-block AF locality theorem added: in finite volume and finite battery,
  explicit small-field, large-field, and counterterm bounds imply a computable
  one-block margin `eta_1B=A_0 Q_r exp(alpha)/(1-zeta_r)`, a KP-style
  incompatible-polymer bound, and a finite-battery residual tail
  `M_F N_F eta_1B exp(-mu R_r)`;
- gauge-fixed derivation of the one-block input added: the package `AF-GF(r)`
  with chart/Jacobian, Hessian coercivity, covariance localization, Taylor
  remainder, counterterm, large-field, and observable-derivative constants
  implies `AF-1B`;
- block axial-tree gauge now proves finite-volume `AF-GF(r)` with explicit
  constants: tree-cycle radius, Hessian eigenvalue, weighted inverse-Hessian
  covariance constant, local derivative suprema, Jacobian bounds, large-field
  entropy/Jacobian constants, and battery derivative bounds;
- multiscale iteration theorem added: uniform `AF-GF(r)` constants and
  `sum_r G_r Q_r^* exp(-mu R_r)<infinity` imply summable local-RG residuals;
  the central remaining gate is uniform covariance localization or an
  equivalent finite-range covariance decomposition for the massless gauge
  field, because finite-volume weighted inverse-Hessian constants need not be
  useful in the continuum limit;
- conditional multiscale summability theorem added: Theorem AF.14 gives
  strong-CYM-RG residual summability from uniform `AF-GF(r)`, uniform
  covariance localization or finite-range covariance decomposition,
  battery-growth control, local-radius summability, and summable
  positivity/covariance/projectivity defects; this is not yet an
  unconditional continuum Yang-Mills construction;
- uniform-constant program advanced: fixed-ratio block conditioning plus a
  uniform Dirichlet Poincare bound gives uniform geometry/chart/Jacobian/local
  derivative constants and finite-range conditional covariance; polynomial or
  logarithmic degradation is absorbed by a slowly growing local ansatz radius;
  the remaining gate is compatibility of this decomposition with the exact
  whole-process RG ledger, running local action, RP/covariance, and gauge
  reconstruction;
- compatibility package added: exact conditional disintegration preserves
  whole-process semantics, the Schur complement supplies the running local
  action ledger, residual root averaging reconstructs gauge-invariant scalar
  tests, RP/covariance defects are tracked as summable ledger terms, and an
  anchored Wilson-loop lower bound is preserved by the local-RG approximation;
  the anchor's existence remains a separate nontriviality input;
- perturbative trajectory and anchor layer added: the inverse-coupling ledger
  tracks the pure `SU(2)` one-loop Yang-Mills trajectory, irrelevant couplings
  contract, and a smeared Wilson-loop anchor exists in a controlled
  weak-coupling reference window when its Gaussian loop coefficient is
  positive and the perturbative remainder is dominated by the leading term;
  this closes the continuum-facing interface on the declared perturbative
  tested class, not a full nonperturbative continuum construction;
- uniqueness criterion added: summable scale-stability moduli imply full-path
  convergence and agreement of all subsequential Wilson-loop limits;
- nontriviality criterion added: an anchored Wilson-loop test separated from
  the trivial value survives to a nontrivial limit;
- continuity criterion added: a uniform loop-topology modulus passes to the
  limiting Wilson-loop functional;
- controlled charged-record theorem added: bounded, truncated, or
  moment-tight charged curvature records extend the compactness and residual
  arguments beyond scalar Wilson loops;
- controlled Wilson matter theorem added: infrared-regularized/invertible
  Wilson source contractions extend the interface, while dynamical determinant
  records require positivity or explicit sign/phase reweighting control;
- matter boundary separated into pure Yang-Mills, valence Wilson matter,
  dynamical Wilson matter, and no-Wilson detail-preserving targets;
- main conditional Paper-11 theorem updated: subsequential CYM-RG plus
  Paper-10 projective control yields a subsequential Wilson-loop interface and
  comparison-map/exchange-defect convergence; strong CYM-RG plus
  nontriviality/continuity yields the continuum-facing Yang-Mills functional;
- five-gate upgrade theorem added: residual decay, uniqueness, nontriviality,
  continuity, and typed charged/matter control yield a unique nontrivial
  continuum-facing Yang-Mills interface on the declared tested class;
- main obstruction theorem stated: stable residuals, positivity defects,
  nondecaying local tails, nonunique limits, triviality, discontinuity,
  uncontrolled charged/matter records, nonlocal required operators, or untyped
  charged/matter/detail records block the standard local Yang-Mills/QCD target
  on the declared battery;
- export to Paper 12 written with a precise list of allowed and forbidden
  unsmeared Wilson-loop claims, and with a four-program follow-up map:
  renormalized unsmeared loops, nonperturbative continuum Yang-Mills, mass
  gap, and confinement.

## V3 Paper 12: Renormalized Unsmeared Wilson-Loop Functionals

Suggested title:

`From Smeared Perturbative Wilson Loops To Renormalized Unsmeared Wilson-Loop Functionals`

Draft:

`relativistic-isp-v3-paper12-renormalized-unsmeared-wilson-loop-functionals.md`

Main question:

> Can the smeared perturbative Wilson-loop interface of Paper 11 be upgraded
> to renormalized unsmeared Wilson-loop functionals?

Main job:

- define admissible loop classes and the admissible loop metric `d_adm`;
- define calibration-based perimeter/cusp counterterms for unsmeared and
  counterterm-normalized smeared Wilson-loop records;
- prove product-boundedness by finite cumulant envelopes derived from
  Paper-11 connected-polymer control;
- prove product/cumulant smearing removal by a local subtraction theorem;
- prove loop-continuity on admissible strata;
- transfer nontriviality from small-smearing perturbative anchors;
- preserve reflection positivity and Euclidean covariance under
  symmetric-positive scalar counterterms with a counterterm-weighted defect
  ledger;
- export exactly what Paper 13 may use and may not use.

Pass condition:

- a positive finite-battery AF theorem: finite admissible loop batteries have
  nontrivial, product-bounded, smearing-independent, continuous,
  reflection-positive, Euclidean-covariant renormalized unsmeared Wilson-loop
  functionals.

Fail condition:

- perimeter/cusp calibration, cumulant product-boundedness, local subtraction,
  loop-continuity, nontriviality, or counterterm-weighted RP/covariance fails
  without adding undeclared data.

Why this matters:

Paper 11 reaches a smeared perturbative interface. Paper 12 attacks the
nearest nonperturbative-looking observable boundary: unsmeared Wilson loops.
Its honest output is finite-battery and perturbative-AF, not full
nonperturbative Yang-Mills, mass gap, or confinement.

## V3 Paper 13: Nonperturbative Continuum Yang-Mills Functional

Suggested title:

`Nonperturbative Continuum Yang-Mills From ISP RG: Tightness, Uniqueness, And Loop Algebra`

Draft:

`relativistic-isp-v3-paper13-nonperturbative-continuum-yang-mills-functional.md`

Main question:

> Can the perturbative tested-class interface be upgraded to a genuine
> nonperturbative continuum Yang-Mills functional?

Main job:

- build a nested dense admissible loop algebra from the Paper-12 finite
  batteries;
- prove projective consistency of the finite-battery functionals under
  inclusion, refinement, and loop approximation;
- extend by continuity from countable dense admissible loops to the declared
  admissible completion;
- preserve reflection positivity and Euclidean covariance through the
  extension without hiding nonlocal perfect-block data;
- prove whole-process regulator and gauge-chart independence by certified
  common-refinement, chart-transition, and elementary-move defect ledgers;
- test whether the construction remains perturbative-AF or becomes genuinely
  nonperturbative;
- prove a positive-margin nonperturbative nontriviality anchor, for example
  from Creutz/running-coupling/constructive Wilson-loop bounds plus a complete
  finite-volume/refinement/chart/counterterm error ledger, or state precisely
  why the Paper-12 perturbative anchor is the boundary.
- for the primary Creutz route, execute the seven-gate anchor program:
  choose scalar closed Wilson-loop records; define the finite four-rectangle
  Creutz battery; prove or import a nonperturbative finite margin, with a
  strong-coupling character/polymer estimate as the first concrete criterion;
  prove the renormalized strong-block criterion `RSB(s_0,\rho,L)` for the
  exact whole-process pushforward if claiming the margin on the actual
  continuum trajectory, preferably by an exact RG entry certificate: cutoff
  convergence on the Creutz battery, a dominant minimal-sheet term, uniform
  KP control of sheet decorations, and a summable nonminimal-sheet tail;
  Paper 13 now fixes the concrete finite-volume `SU(N)` target and proves
  that such a surface-polymer entry estimate implies the exact RG entry
  certificate and hence RSB; it also proves that a checkable strong-block
  character domain implies the surface-polymer entry estimate, and that an
  actual-continuum strong-block entry package implies the strong-block
  character domain; the actual-entry package is now split into six gates
  `BC`, `CE`, `RPF`, `KP_dec`, `SUB`, and `WP`, with block convergence reduced
  to subsequential block-limit uniqueness; Paper 13 further gives a
  determining-identity route to that uniqueness, Haar-projection tests for the
  character coefficients, a connected-cumulant KP criterion for residual
  polymers, a mass-gap/area-law bridge, and an explicit decision table;
  transport the margin through finite-volume, RG, loop-approximation, chart,
  regulator, and counterterm losses; prove scale-resolved positive-margin
  survival by a summable AF-compatible transport profile; express the actual
  transport constants through the Paper-11 AF residual constants
  `Q_r^*`, `G_r`, `R_r`, ledger defects, and loop-observable Lipschitz
  constants; close regulator/chart independence on that battery; upgrade the
  main theorem from perturbative-AF to nonperturbative if the margin remains
  positive; export to Paper 14 only after this decision.

Barandes alignment:

- the dense loop algebra is an operational record algebra, not a fundamental
  field algebra;
- extension is a whole-process consistency theorem, not composition of
  partial kernels;
- renormalization remains a declared record transformation;
- Hilbert-space/local-net language is representation output only after
  positivity, covariance, and continuity have been proved.

Pass condition:

- a nontrivial reflection-positive Euclidean-covariant Wilson-loop functional
  on a declared dense loop algebra, independent of regulator and gauge-chart
  choices, with a genuine nonperturbative anchor certificate; concretely, a
  renormalized/block-scale Creutz battery margin whose scale-resolved
  continuum transport loss, computed from the Paper-11 constants, is strictly
  smaller than the finite nonperturbative lower bound, with the block-scale
  sheet expansion derived from `RSB(s_0,\rho,L)`; Paper 13 proves that the
  exact RG entry certificate implies RSB, and that strong-block character
  entry implies the needed surface-polymer estimate, so the remaining
  nonperturbative pass gate is proving the finite identity, coefficient,
  connected-cumulant, subcriticality, and whole-process certificate estimates
  with enough positive transport reserve.

Fail condition:

- only perturbative/smeared/finite-battery functionals survive, or the
  regulator/chart/anchor ledgers do not close with positive margin; in
  particular, a microscopic Creutz signal that shrinks faster than the
  continuum transport losses is not a nonperturbative Paper-13 success, and
  neither is a block-scale margin whose Paper-11 transport constants consume
  the full reserve, nor a formal sheet expansion not proved for the exact
  whole-process pushforward on the actual continuum trajectory. Perturbative
  asymptotic freedom alone is not enough: it supplies transport constants
  after an anchor exists, but it does not by itself prove the exact
  minimal-sheet/surface-KP entry certificate or actual entry into the
  strong-block character domain. Paper 13 now makes this sharper: the missing
  first arrow is actual continuum `SU(N)` Yang-Mills satisfying the six
  `ACSB(s_0,\rho,L)` gates: uniqueness of the finite block limit, positive
  character coefficient window, KP-small residuals, surface subcriticality,
  and whole-process regulator/chart integrity.

## V3 Paper 14: Finite-Block Entry For Actual Yang-Mills

Suggested title:

`Finite-Block Entry Gates For Actual Continuum SU(N) Yang-Mills`

Draft:

`relativistic-isp-v3-paper14-finite-block-yang-mills-entry-gates.md`

Main question:

> Does actual four-dimensional continuum `SU(N)` Yang-Mills enter the
> finite-block record domain required by Paper 13?

Main job:

- prove or reduce the block-limit uniqueness gate `BLU(s_0,L)` by a
  determining finite-block identity ledger;
- make the Schwinger-Dyson, loop-equation, reflection-positivity, and
  covariance identities finite, record-level, and whole-process rather than
  Markovian;
- choose the Creutz-character battery and its countable determining
  completion;
- prove a BLU closing sequence, preferably through a triangular
  moment-closure theorem; if triangular closure fails, enlarge the declared
  battery by the forced records rather than hiding them in a microscopic
  field ontology;
- the first nontrivial Creutz-character battery has now been tested and does
  not close exactly: exterior one-staple deformation records are forced; the
  next BLU test must therefore use the one-staple enlarged battery and decide
  whether the forced-record tower is local and summable;
- the one-staple enlarged battery has also been tested and does not close
  exactly: two-staple, corner, rectangle-extension, transverse-sheet, and
  local action-density records are forced; the current positive result is a
  full forced-tower theorem: finite-stage compactness, all-depth
  locality/branching, and the implication
  `FTS(s_0,L) + LTD(s_0,L) => BLU(s_0,L)`;
- canonical forced-record weights have now been defined, and `FTS` is reduced
  to one of three explicit decay inputs: KP forced-polymer decay,
  collar-factorizing exponential clustering, or area-law forced-detour decay
  with exponent margin over the tower branching rate;
- limiting tower determinacy is reduced to `LID`, a loop-identity determinacy
  certificate: recursive moment determination, kernel removal by
  reflection-positivity/covariance, positivity of the moment functional, and
  separation by the countable tower algebra;
- `LID` is further reduced to shell-by-shell loop-identity invertibility
  `SSI`: shell matrices `M_k`, physical kernel quotients, controlled right
  inverses, nonlinear Lipschitz gaps, summable inverse-tail amplification,
  and positivity/separation of the recursive moment functional;
- prove the central character extraction gate `CE(s_0,\rho,L)` by explicit
  Haar-projected coefficient windows for the block plaquette marginal;
- prove the finite-character actual-RG certificate `cRGCE(s_0,\rho,L)`, which
  puts the actual block plaquette marginal in a positive-reserve central
  character neighborhood for the declared coefficient and tail records;
- prove the whole-process certificate gate `WP(s_0,L)` under regulator,
  chart, counterterm, and finite-volume transport;
- prove a concrete standard-chain rate certificate for `WP`, including
  identity, projection, coefficient, tail, chart, counterterm, volume,
  covariance, and reflection-positivity defects;
- final Paper-14 closure theorem added:
  forced-collar decay plus `SSI`/positivity/separation plus `cRGCE` plus
  admissible `WP` rates imply `FBE`, hence the Paper-13 gates `BC`, `CE`,
  and `WP`;
- identify exactly which pieces are imported constructive-Yang-Mills input
  and which are ISP record-theoretic consequences.

Barandes alignment:

- the objects are finite batteries of gauge-invariant records and their
  pushed-forward laws, not hidden microscopic fields;
- the identities determine a whole finite-block law, not a divisible
  subprocess;
- gauge fixing and chart choices are scaffolding for certificates only;
- Hilbert-space mass-gap language is postponed until the record functional is
  constructed.

Pass condition:

- a forced-collar decay estimate proving `FTS`, a loop-identity determinacy
  certificate proved via `SSI` and positivity/separation, a finite-character
  `cRGCE` certificate, and an admissible `WP` rate certificate hold for the
  declared finite-block batteries, giving explicit error reserves that can be
  exported to Paper 15.

Fail condition:

- compactness gives subsequential limits, but the identities do not determine
  a unique finite-block law; triangular closure produces unresolved kernel
  directions that cannot be repaired by forced records; the leading character
  coefficient has no positive actual-RG window; or the certificate depends on
  regulator/chart choices.

## V3 Paper 15: Connected-Polymer KP And Surface Subcriticality

Suggested title:

`Connected-Polymer KP, Surface Subcriticality, And Creutz Margins`

Draft:

`relativistic-isp-v3-paper15-connected-polymer-kp-creutz-margin.md`

Main question:

> Given the finite-block entry gates of Paper 14, can the residual law be
> controlled strongly enough to enter the Paper-13 `ACSB/RSB` domain?

Main job:

- prove the residual factorization gate `RPF(s_0,L)` for the exact
  finite-block pushforward;
- repair `RCE` as a coefficient-normalized generator/activity envelope,
  not an impossible volume-exponential bound for all bounded macroscopic
  observables;
- define the AF residual-cumulant certificate `AFRCE`: Paper-11 local-RG
  summability, Paper-12 renormalized connected-polymer localization, Paper-14
  block projection, product-reference locality, and positive raw margin after
  generator/tree losses;
- prove `AFRCE => RCE`, and hence reduce the first Paper-15 gate to named
  constructive Yang-Mills ledgers;
- make the first gate numerical: define `Delta_blk`, `h_an`, `A_AF`,
  `mu_AF`, `lambda_gen`, `lambda_tree`, `C_KP`, and `eta_res`;
- prove the raw-margin certificate
  `min(mu_RG/c_blk,mu_0,mu_12)>lambda_gen+lambda_tree`;
- prove the explicit KP test
  `C_cum A_AF exp(-delta_KP)/(1-exp(-delta_KP))<1`, with
  `delta_KP=mu_AF-m-h_an`;
- prove explicit decoration smallness:
  `eta_ch^{bd}=C_ch Tail_CE`, `eta_dec^{bd}=eta_res^{bd}+eta_ch^{bd}<1`;
- convert `eta_dec^{bd}` into surface and Creutz losses
  `D_*`, `xi_*`, `xi'_*`, and `Delta_dec^{bd}`;
- prove the explicit surface reserve
  `M_SUB^{bd}=(E_surf^*D_*)^{-1}-u_+>0`;
- prove the explicit Creutz reserve
  `M_15^{bd}=u_-^{N_0}(1-u_+^{Q_sigma})-Delta_dec^{bd}-T_loss^{bd}>0`;
- package the full numerical certificate `nCPSC` so Paper 16 imports one
  finite tuple rather than scattered inequalities;
- prove the final numerical closure theorem:
  Paper-14 `FBE` plus positive `nCPSC` gives all six Paper-13 `ACSB` gates,
  opens the declared `RSB` route, and exports `X_15`;
- prove the connected-cumulant KP gate `KP_dec(s_0,\rho,L)` with explicit
  constants and surface-entropy losses;
- prove the surface subcriticality gate `SUB(s_0,\rho,L)`;
- define the connected-polymer surface certificate `CPSC`: Paper-14 `FBE`,
  residual cumulant envelope `RCE`, residual KP certificate `RKP`, combined
  decoration smallness, positive `SUB` reserve, positive Creutz reserve, and
  whole-process compatibility;
- prove that `CPSC` gives `RPF + KP_dec + SUB` and hence, together with
  Paper 14, all six Paper-13 `ACSB` gates;
- transport a positive renormalized Creutz margin through the Paper-11 and
  Paper-12 ledgers without consuming the reserve;
- separate a genuine block-scale area-law input from a finite-regulator
  strong-coupling artifact.

Barandes alignment:

- residuals are connected correlations of declared records, not virtual
  particles or off-record fields;
- the polymer expansion is a norm-controlled statement about one
  whole-process pushforward measure;
- confinement language remains operational until the continuum functional and
  representation layer are built.

Pass condition:

- the connected-polymer surface certificate `CPSC` holds, with `RCE` either
  proved directly or obtained from `AFRCE`; hence `RPF`, `KP_dec`, and `SUB`
  hold with enough positive Creutz-margin reserve to trigger the Paper-13
  exact-entry route to `RSB(s_0,\rho,L)`. For the first gate this means the
  numerical tuple `Y_15^{(1)}=(A_AF,mu_AF,h_an,C_cum,C_KP,eta_res)` has
  `eta_res<1`. For the full Paper-15 gate this means `nCPSC` is positive:
  `AFRCE(A_AF,mu_AF,r_*)`, `eta_res^{bd}<1`, `eta_dec^{bd}<1`,
  `M_SUB^{bd}>0`, and `M_15^{bd}>0`. The final export is `X_15`.

Fail condition:

- the residual has uncontrolled nonlocal tails, surface entropy beats the
  leading sheet coefficient, the positive margin exists only before
  continuum transport, or one accidentally demands the too-strong naive
  sup-norm `RCE` instead of the coefficient-normalized activity envelope
  needed by KP. Numerically, the sharp failures are raw-margin failure,
  KP-entropy failure, character-tail failure, surface-entropy failure,
  Creutz-margin failure, or whole-process compatibility failure.

## V3 Paper 16: Nonperturbative Continuum Yang-Mills Closure

Suggested title:

`Nonperturbative Continuum Yang-Mills Closure From ISP Record Gates`

Draft:

`relativistic-isp-v3-paper16-nonperturbative-yang-mills-closure.md`

Main question:

> Do the Paper-13 reduction and the Paper-14/15 entry estimates assemble into
> a nontrivial reflection-positive Euclidean-covariant continuum Yang-Mills
> Wilson-loop functional?

Main job:

- assemble `BLU`, `CE`, `RPF`, `KP_dec`, `SUB`, and `WP` into
  `ACSB(s_0,\rho,L)`;
- import the Paper-15 export package `X_15` and distinguish positive
  finite-battery closure from continuum closure;
- define the continuum Yang-Mills closure certificate `CYC`: positive
  `X_15` tower, summable projectivity, volume exhaustion, regulator/chart
  independence, reflection positivity, Euclidean covariance, loop
  continuity, nontriviality anchor, and whole-process compatibility;
- define `CYM_WL`, the continuum-facing pure `SU(N)` Wilson-loop functional;
- invoke the Paper-13 implication chain
  `ACSB -> SB -> surface-polymer entry -> exact RG entry -> RSB`;
- construct the continuum Wilson-loop functional on the declared loop
  completion;
- preserve reflection positivity, Euclidean covariance, regulator/chart
  independence, and nontriviality through the final extension;
- classify the actual `nCPSC` rows as verified, conditional, or obstructed;
- define the actual-trajectory closure certificate `AYM-CLOSE`, starting
  from finite cutoff pushed-forward `SU(N)` record laws and adding the
  precise continuum clauses: `FBE`, `AFRCE`, KP margin, character-tail
  margin, surface reserve, Creutz reserve, projectivity, regulator/chart
  independence, RP/covariance transport, loop continuity, nontriviality
  anchor, and whole-process compatibility;
- split `AYM-CLOSE` into the named workbench subcertificates `AYM-LAW`,
  `AYM-FBE`, `AYM-AFRCE`, `AYM-KP`, `AYM-TAIL`, `AYM-SURF`, `AYM-CREUTZ`,
  `AYM-PROJ`, `AYM-REG`, `AYM-RP-COV`, `AYM-LC`, `AYM-NT`, and `AYM-WP`;
- choose the heat-kernel lattice trajectory `HK-AYM` as the primary
  regulator path, while treating Wilson action as a later regulator/chart
  comparison problem;
- reduce the first analytic bottleneck to the local-cluster estimate
  `HK-LCB`, proving `HK-AYM + HK-LCB => AYM-AFRCE`;
- push `HK-LCB` one level deeper by defining the three constructive
  subgates `HK-SF-GCD`, `HK-LFS`, and `HK-CTS`, and prove
  `HK-SF-GCD + HK-LFS + HK-CTS => HK-LCB => AYM-AFRCE`;
- reduce the large-field gate further by proving
  `HK-BFE + HK-LF-DOM + sigma_lf>h_poly => HK-LFS`, where
  `sigma_lf = c_B delta^2/t_L - log(C_B M_L)`;
- reduce `HK-BFE` to the finite-dimensional heat-kernel denominator margin
  `m_B(delta)=c_H delta^2-a_D>0`, proving
  `compact heat-kernel lower bound + finite block geometry + m_B(delta)>0
  => HK-BFE`;
- test that generic margin by deriving the threshold
  `delta^2>P_b^{loc}a_-/c_H`; when it is too crude, replace it with the
  sharper collar-adapted route
  `q_loc(e_col+L_B alpha^2)<a_ad<c_H => HK-CAD + m_B^sharp(delta)>0
  => HK-BFE`, with `m_B^sharp(delta)=(c_H-a_ad)delta^2`;
- reduce `HK-LF-DOM` to a finite-battery coefficient representation
  `HK-LF-REP-SRC`, proving
  `HK-LF-REP-SRC => HK-LF-REP => HK-LF-DOM` with
  `M_L=N_lab J_blk R_blk E_blk`;
- assemble the large-field branch as one certificate
  `HK-LF-SRC => HK-LF-CLOSE => HK-LFS`, where the sharp entropy margin is
  `sigma_lf^sharp=(c_H-a_ad)delta^2/t_L
  -log(C_ad P_b C_H N_lab J_blk R_blk E_blk)>h_poly`, and once
  `c_H>a_ad` and `HK-LF-REP-SRC` hold, this margin is forced by choosing
  `t_L` sufficiently small;
- reduce counterterm stability to a local counterterm ledger by proving
  `HK-CT-CLOSE => HK-CTS`;
- reduce the small-field gate to a block-conditioned covariance and
  tree-activity certificate by proving `HK-SF-CLOSE => HK-SF-GCD`;
- sharpen the small-field tree activity: Paper 16 now defines
  `HK-SF-SRC` and proves
  `theta_sf <= e C_v C_G C_E g_*^{2p}`. It now also defines the finite
  Yang-Mills vertex ledger `HK-SF-YM2`, with labels
  `{4,33,J2,gf2,cov2,rec2,norm2}`, and proves that it gives `p=1` and
  `C_v=C_v^{YM2}`. Paper 11's block-conditioned covariance supplies finite
  `C_G,mu_G,C_E` on the fixed-ratio branch, so the intended route is
  `theta_sf <= e C_v^{YM2} C_G C_E g_*^2<1` on a sufficiently fine AF tail,
  provided `HK-SF-YM2` is verified on the same pushed-forward record law.
  Paper 19 verifies this common-record import for the frozen `SEL_0`
  one-block battery via `CRL-SF_0`, neutral odd cancellation, time-tangent
  absorption, and finite pushed-forward projection constants;
- derive the KP threshold
  `eta_res^{bd}(m)=C_KP A_res exp(-(mu_res-h_KP-m)r_*)/
  (1-exp(-(mu_res-h_KP-m)))<1`, making clear that a size-resolved envelope is
  needed;
- sharpen `HK-KP-TEST(m)` to a scalar decision: with
  `D_0=mu_res-h_KP` and `B_res=C_KP A_res`, some `m>=0` passes iff
  `B_res exp(-D_0 r_*)/(1-exp(-D_0))<1`; any required positive weight
  `m_req` must lie below the explicit `m_max`, and increasing the effective
  range requires a genuine local-absorption certificate for all smaller
  residual polymers;
- assemble those analytic pieces into one certificate
  `HK-AN-SRC => HK-AN-CLOSE => AYM-AFRCE + AYM-KP`, which becomes the clean
  analytic import for the remaining Paper-15 numerical gates. The ordered
  source route is:
  `HK-SF-SRC` with `theta_sf<1`, then `HK-LF-CLOSE` with
  `sigma_lf^sharp>h_poly`, then `HK-CT-CLOSE`, then common residual
  constants, and finally the scalar KP test
  `B_res exp(-(D_0-m)r_res)/(1-exp(-(D_0-m)))<1`. The first execution step
  is now closed on batteries with a verified common-record `HK-SF-YM2`
  import; Paper 19 supplies that verification for frozen `SEL_0`. The next
  analytic target is `HK-LF-SRC`: prove the good-collar minimizer inequality
  and the finite large-field representation ledger, then choose `t_L` to
  force `sigma_lf^sharp>h_poly`;
- start the character-tail branch using growing Casimir batteries
  `Rep_{R_i}` and the heat-kernel/Weyl tail estimate
  `Tail_ch(t_i,R_i)<=C_W t_i^{-nu_W} exp(-(a_ch/2)t_i R_i)`;
- prove the finite-battery cutoff theorem with
  `R_i >= (2/(a_ch t_i))(nu_W log(1/t_i)+log(C_W/epsilon_ch))`;
- assemble decoration smallness as
  `HK-DEC-CLOSE => AYM-TAIL`, with
  `eta_dec^{bd}=eta_res^{bd}(m)+C_dec epsilon_ch<1`;
- package surface reserve as `HK-SURF-CLOSE => AYM-SURF`, with
  `M_SUB^{bd}=kappa_sheet-h_surf-L_dec eta_dec^{bd}-R_surf>0`;
- package transported Creutz reserve as `HK-CREUTZ-CLOSE => AYM-CREUTZ`, with
  `M_15^{bd}=M_SUB^{bd}-L_bat-L_reg-L_vol-L_shape>0`;
- assemble the full Paper-15 numerical certificate as
  `HK-NCPSC-CLOSE => verified positive nCPSC`;
- lift the finite-battery positive certificate to the Paper-15 export tower
  by proving `HK-X15-CLOSE => positive X_15 tower`, where `HK-X15-CLOSE`
  means Paper-14 `FBE` and `HK-NCPSC-CLOSE` hold on one common
  whole-process heat-kernel tower;
- reduce continuum projectivity to summable finite-battery marginal defects
  by proving `HK-PROJ-CLOSE => AYM-PROJ`;
- make projectivity concrete by defining the readout scheme in which
  restriction is coordinate deletion on declared records, then prove
  `concrete readout scheme + HK-PROJ-DRIFT + HK-XDRIFT
  => HK-PROJ-CLOSE`, so the remaining projectivity burden is exactly the
  cross-scale finite-battery drift and `X_15` constant drift;
- derive those drifts from the actual heat-kernel RG ledger by proving
  `HK-RG-PROJ-LEDGER => HK-PROJ-DRIFT` and
  `HK-RG-XLEDGER => HK-XDRIFT`; the remaining projectivity burden is now the
  verification of summable one-shell law drifts and margin-preserving
  one-shell `X_15` constant drifts on the actual trajectory;
- reduce regulator, gauge-chart, and blocking independence to summable
  finite-record comparison defects by proving `HK-REG-CLOSE => AYM-REG`;
- make regulator/chart independence concrete by defining finite record maps
  from each declared comparison description into the heat-kernel primary
  readout chart, then prove
  `concrete comparison scheme + HK-RG-REG-LEDGER + HK-RG-REGX-LEDGER
  => HK-REG-CLOSE`; this is the operational place where Wilson/heat-kernel
  universality, gauge-chart independence, blocking independence, and
  counterterm-scheme independence must be verified;
