## V3 Paper 33: Same-Law Bootstrap Of Live Scalars

Path:
`physics/relativistic-isp-v3-paper33-same-law-bootstrap-of-live-scalars.md`

Status:

- Paper 33 is the first law-space bootstrap pass after the Paper-32 scalar
  endpoint.  It does not add a hidden dynamics.  It forms the finite convex
  set of same-record laws compatible with the printed affine identities,
  gauge/selector/recoupling constraints, heat-kernel data, Ward identities,
  pointwise envelopes, and positive moment matrices.
- It defines `P33-LAWBOOT-SCAL(B_rem)` as a finite dual upper-certificate
  route for \(m,t\), and `P33-LAWBOOT-FLOOR(M_*)` as the sign-coherent lower
  floor route for \(m,t,\lambda_+,\lambda_-\).
- It proves certificate soundness: a dual positivity identity over licensed
  constraints bounds every admissible same-law record distribution.
- It executes the minimal two-channel bootstrap and proves that the scalar
  ray \(B=cI_2\) remains feasible under the current constraints.  Along this
  ray
  \(m=c(h_0+h_A)\) and \(t=ca_N(h_0-h_A)\).
- Therefore the minimal bootstrap cannot prove useful scalar smallness below
  the crude envelope, cannot prove a positive
  `P32-SCAL-STRUCTSRC-GRAM`, and cannot prove a sign-coherent floor because
  both signs of \(c\) remain feasible.
- The active next theorem is now forced: add a same-law constraint that cuts
  off or orients the scalar ray.  The ranked candidates are
  `P32-SCAL-RESDEFECT(delta)`, structural coupling plus Gram, a non-gauge
  Ward/Stein identity, a reflection-positive upper moment inequality
  involving \(R\Sigma\), `P32-RN-BLKDER(L)` if the joint route is
  prioritized, or a sign-coherent scalar floor.
- Its residual-score pass defines the score-augmented bootstrap and the
  score-energy source `P33-SCAL-SCOREENERGY(I_m,I_t)`.  It proves this source
  implies `P32-SCAL-RESDEFECT(delta_score)` with
  \(\delta_{score}=A_m(M_\beta)\sqrt{I_m}+A_t(M_\beta)\sqrt{I_t}\).  It also
  proves Ward identities alone do not close: without score-energy control,
  two-point score rays can realize arbitrary score pairings.  The current
  corpus does not print the needed score-energy bounds.
- Its \(L^2\) score investigation decomposes the new score into residual,
  Jacobian, selector, and normalizer components.  It proves component
  \(L^2\), pointwise, Sobolev/analytic, or curvature/self-energy packages
  would each source `P33-SCAL-SCOREENERGY`.  The most promising positive
  target is `P33-SCAL-SCORE-CURV(K_m,L_m)` and
  `P33-SCAL-SCORE-CURV(K_t,L_t)`, but it requires expected second
  derivatives of the actual residual/selector score; the current corpus does
  not print them.
- Its score-curvature pass expands that target into four exact same-law
  component gates: `P33-RES-HESS`, `P33-JAC-HESS`, `P33-SEL-CURV`, and
  `P33-NORM-HESS`, plus licensed-score energy.  These imply score energy
  with the printed quadratic constant.  The audit shows that normalization
  does not remove the normalizer variance, selector curvature is harmless
  only under local constancy or a boundary-flux bound, and more finite labels
  do not help unless they produce one of those component curvature estimates.

Executed work packages:

1. **Define the same-law bootstrap space.** Treat the printed finite
   constraints as a convex set of admissible record laws, with no Markov or
   off-law comparison measure: completed.
2. **Print primal/dual certificate soundness.** Prove that finite positive
   moment certificates bound live scalar expectations, and that oriented
   dual certificates source lower floors: completed.
3. **Instantiate the minimal two-channel scalar bootstrap.** Use the
   Paper-32 variables \(\beta_{00},\beta_{0A},\beta_{A0},\beta_{AA}\) and
   the affine formulas for \(m,t,\lambda_\pm\): completed.
4. **Test the scalar ray.** Prove that deterministic laws with
   \(B=cI_2\) satisfy positivity, gauge-scalar compatibility, and all
   printed two-channel affine identities: completed.
5. **Close the minimal bootstrap at current-corpus level.** Prove that the
   current constraints do not bound \(m,t\), do not force Gram positivity,
   and do not orient a scalar floor.  Record the active next constraints:
   completed.
6. **Attack the residual-score active constraint.** Add score variables
   \(S_m,S_t\), define `P33-SCAL-SCOREENERGY(I_m,I_t)`, prove the
   Cauchy-Schwarz transfer to `P32-SCAL-RESDEFECT(delta_score)`, prove that
   Ward identities without score-energy control leave arbitrary two-point
   score rays, and audit the score-energy theorem as unsourced by the current
   corpus: completed.
7. **Investigate the \(L^2\) score estimate.** Decompose the new scalar score
   into residual, Jacobian, selector, and normalizer pieces; prove component
   \(L^2\) bounds imply score energy; prove pointwise, Sobolev, and
   curvature/self-energy sufficient routes; show Poincare/log-Sobolev has the
   wrong direction without a separate Dirichlet or curvature bound; and audit
   all score-energy sourcing routes as unsourced by the current corpus:
   completed.
8. **Attack score-curvature directly.** Expand
   `P33-SCAL-SCORE-CURV` into residual Hessian, Jacobian Hessian, selector
   curvature, and normalizer Hessian gates; prove the component-curvature
   implication to `P33-SCAL-SCOREENERGY`; prove normalization only gives
   centering and not variance control; and record selector local constancy
   plus residual/Jacobian/normalizer Hessian control as the cleanest
   remaining positive subroute: completed.

## V3 Paper 34: Reflection-Positive Moment Bootstrap

Path:
`physics/relativistic-isp-v3-paper34-reflection-positive-moment-bootstrap.md`

Status:

- Paper 34 attacks the reflection-positive moment/SOS candidate left by
  Paper 33.  It stays inside the same adaptive pushed-forward record law:
  RP matrices have entries \(\mathbf E[(\Theta A_a)A_b]\) for finite record
  functions \(A_a\).
- It proves finite RP/SOS certificate soundness for upper bounds and
  sign-coherent floors.  This is Barandes-aligned because it introduces no
  hidden Markov transfer, no off-law Euclidean path measure, and no new
  ontology for Peter-Weyl or operator variables.
- The all-degree scalar-ray test is decisive.  For every allowed scalar
  \(c\), the deterministic law \(B=cI_2\) extends to every passive finite
  RP worksheet.  Ordinary moment matrices and RP moment matrices are
  rank-one positive semidefinite outer products.
- Therefore passive RP/SOS constraints cannot prove a useful bound on
  \(m,t\), cannot orient \(\lambda_\pm\), and cannot force a positive Gram
  determinant.
- The only remaining RP routes are non-passive same-law value inputs:
  `P34-RP-UPMOM`, `P34-RP-ODD`, `P34-RP-SCHUR`,
  `P34-RP-STRUCTCOUPLE`, or `P34-RP-FLOOR-WIT`.  None is printed by the
  current corpus.

Executed work packages:

1. **Define the finite RP record algebra.** Include the live block
   \(B=R\Sigma\), \(m,t,\lambda_\pm\), heat-bad projectors, channel
   projectors, retained Peter-Weyl modes, and selector-stable functions:
   completed.
2. **Print RP/SOS certificate soundness.** Prove upper and floor
   certificates over ordinary and RP moment cones: completed.
3. **Execute the scalar-ray test.** Prove deterministic scalar-ray laws
   extend to all passive finite RP worksheets and make every RP matrix
   rank-one positive: completed.
4. **Close passive RP/SOS at current-corpus level.** Prove no passive finite
   RP refinement cuts the scalar ray or orients a floor: completed.
5. **Audit non-passive RP routes.** Prove upper-moment, oddness, Schur,
   structural-coupling, and floor routes are valid if sourced, but each
   requires new same-law value information not printed by the corpus:
   completed.

## V3 Paper 35: Scalar-Ray Detector Theorem

Path:
`physics/relativistic-isp-v3-paper35-scalar-ray-detector-theorem.md`

Status:

- Paper 35 turns the obstruction \(B=cI_2\) into a detector test.  For any
  proposed constraint package \({\mathcal C}\), define its scalar-ray trace:
  the set of \(c\)'s for which the deterministic scalar-ray law extends to a
  same-law model satisfying \({\mathcal C}\).
- It proves the universal ray-blindness criterion: any passive
  deterministic-character compatible package leaves every
  \(c\in[-M_\beta,M_\beta]\) alive.
- It classifies the current ray-blind classes: passive finite labels,
  ordinary moment positivity, passive RP/SOS positivity, gauge covariance,
  recoupling, heat-diagonal data, selector relabeling, and source
  reparametrization without bounds.
- It proves the complete detector dichotomy for the current scalar branch.
  A useful theorem must be an upper amplitude/value bound, a non-gauge
  Ward/Stein linear equation, structural coupling plus Gram, a non-passive
  reflection theorem, an RN block derivative/residual Jacobian rank theorem,
  or a sign-coherent floor.
- It ranks the next work: first attack
  `P35-NONGAUGE-WS-RAYCUT(A,epsilon)`; if the Ward/Stein range misses the
  scalar direction, extract the corresponding dual floor candidate.

Executed work packages:

1. **Define scalar-ray traces.** Classify constraint packages as ray-blind,
   ray-cutting, ray-killing, or ray-orienting: completed.
2. **Prove passive ray-blindness.** Show deterministic scalar-ray laws pass
   all passive deterministic-character constraints: completed.
3. **Audit current ray-blind structures.** Gauge/recoupling, moments, passive
   RP, heat diagonal, selector relabeling, and source reparametrization are
   all ray-blind: completed.
4. **Print ray-cutting mechanisms.** Isolate upper amplitude, Ward/Stein,
   structural coupling, non-passive RP, RN derivative, and floor mechanisms:
   completed.
5. **Close the detector theorem.** Prove every current scalar Branch-A route
   is either ray-blind or one of the detector mechanisms; recommend
   non-gauge Ward/Stein ray-cut as the next constructive target: completed.

## V3 Paper 36: Non-Gauge Ward-Stein Ray-Cut Or Dual Floor

Path:
`physics/relativistic-isp-v3-paper36-nongauge-ward-stein-raycut.md`

Status:

- Paper 36 attacks the Rank-1 detector recommended by Paper 35:
  `P35-NONGAUGE-WS-RAYCUT(A,epsilon)`.
- It proves the formal block-entry ray-cut algebra.  In the envelope
  coordinates
  \(\beta=(\beta_{00},\beta_{0A},\beta_{A0},\beta_{AA})\), the linear forms
  \(m=\ell_m\cdot\beta\) and \(t=\ell_t\cdot\beta\) are exact
  Ward-Stein derivatives of quadratic tests.
- It prints the scalar-ray coefficients:
  \(A_m=h_0+h_A\) and \(A_t=a_N(h_0-h_A)\).  Thus the formal scalar rank
  obstruction is gone.
- It proves that the formal coefficient is not yet an actual same-law
  theorem.  The positive route requires actual scalar-field admissibility,
  actual nonzero ray coefficient in the active quotient, and a closing
  residual/selector score-defect bound:
  `P36-ACT-SCALFIELD-ADM + P36-ACT-RAYCOEFF(A_0) +
  P36-WS-SCOREDEF(epsilon)`.
- It audits and discards pure gauge/Haar, selector-only, endpoint-additive,
  normalizer-only, and heat-only directions as ray-blind for this detector.
- It proves the dual fork: if the actual Ward-Stein range misses the scalar
  direction, finite separation supplies only a dual candidate.  A Branch-A
  falsification still requires the sign-coherent value theorem
  `P36-WS-DUALSIGN(M_*)`.

Executed work packages:

1. **Define the ray-cut target.** Formalize scalar-ray-sensitive
   Ward-Stein pairs and the closing range: completed.
2. **Prove the one-line ray-cut lemma.** A same-law equation
   \(Ac=\epsilon\) with \(|A|\ge A_0\) bounds \(|c|\le\epsilon/A_0\):
   completed.
3. **Print formal coefficients.** Compute the exact block-entry derivatives
   and scalar-ray coefficients for \(m,t\): completed.
4. **Audit actualization.** Show that formal block derivatives become useful
   only after actual scalar-field admissibility and score-defect control:
   completed.
5. **Audit blind subroutes and dual fork.** Discard gauge, selector, endpoint,
   normalizer, and heat-only routes; isolate `P36-WS-DUALSIGN(M_*)` as the
   negative close: completed.

## V3 Paper 37: Actual Scalar-Field Admissibility Or Kernel Floor

Path:
`physics/relativistic-isp-v3-paper37-actual-scalar-field-admissibility-or-kernel-floor.md`

Status:

- Paper 37 executes the exact five-step plan left by Paper 36 before any
  score-defect attack should be attempted.
- It defines the actual scalar map only after a pointwise same-law lift:
  \(s_{act}(\theta)=(m_{\Gamma_1}^{pt}(\theta),
  t_{\Gamma_1}^{pt}(\theta))\).
- It prints the actual Jacobian target
  \(G_{act}^{scal}=D_\theta s_{act}\), and proves that actual scalar-field
  admissibility is equivalent to
  `P37-SCAL-POINTLIFT + P37-SCAL-JACRANK(sigma) +
  P37-SCAL-SCOREENV(C_S)`.
- It audits the possible right-inverse constructions.  Atom-value lift and
  group-coordinate lift are not sourced by the current corpus; free scalar
  coordinates are not same-law; source response is valid but it is the
  separate source-rank/curvature route, not an actual configuration right
  inverse.
- It proves the conditional positive close: if the lift/rank/score-envelope
  package holds, the lifted fields \(Y_m,Y_t\) exist and Paper 36 reduces to
  the residual score-defect theorem.
- It proves the negative fork: rank failure gives only a finite separator
  candidate.  Falsifying Branch A still requires
  `P37-SCAL-KERFLOOR(M_*)`.
- It then attacks the source-response/structural pivot inside the same
  paper.  The positive structural route is
  `P37-STRUCTSRC-COUPLE + P37-STRUCTSRC-GRAM + P37-STRUCTSRC-CURV`;
  the negative route is `P37-STRUCTSRC-RIGIDFLOOR`.
- It proves that clean heat/channel sources do not couple to the actual
  residual/signed product \(R\Sigma\), so they are ray-blind for this route.
  The current corpus does not source the structural coupling, Gram,
  curvature, or rigidity/floor inputs.

Executed work packages:

1. **Define the actual scalar map.** Introduce the actual chart and
   pointwise lift `P37-SCAL-POINTLIFT`: completed.
2. **Print the Jacobian target.** Define
   \(G_{act}^{scal}=D_\theta(m^{pt},t^{pt})\) and the rank gate:
   completed.
3. **Try the right inverse.** Audit atom-value, group-coordinate, free
   coordinate, and source-response constructions: completed.
4. **If rank passes.** Define \(Y_m,Y_t\) and prove the reduction to the
   Paper-36 score-defect theorem: completed.
5. **If rank fails.** Define the kernel separator and prove that a
   sign-coherent kernel floor is still required: completed.
6. **Define structural source-response.** Add the two-knob structural source
   and coupling gate `P37-STRUCTSRC-COUPLE`: completed.
7. **Compute the structural rank object.** Define the Gram and curvature
   gates `P37-STRUCTSRC-GRAM` and `P37-STRUCTSRC-CURV`: completed.
8. **Discard clean heat shortcuts.** Prove clean heat/channel sources do not
   reach the actual residual/signed product \(R\Sigma\): completed.
9. **Close the structural fork.** Prove the positive conditional route and
   the rigidity/floor alternative, while auditing both as unsourced by the
   current corpus: completed.

## Decision Tree

1. If V3 Paper 1 fails, QFT matching cannot be claimed as reconstruction; ISP
   remains a stochastic representation layer whose extra QFT data are external.
2. If V3 Paper 2 fails, finite-slab smooth-lapse dynamics remains
   regulator-artificial; keep log-smearing as a benchmark only.
3. If V3 Paper 3 fails, full interacting relativistic ISP likely fails at the
   raw comparison-map level.
4. If V3 Paper 4 fails, stochastic curvature may be a free-theory phenomenon
   rather than an interacting law.
5. If V3 Paper 5 fails, the Wilson branch cannot serve as the conservative
   single-species standard-QFT benchmark, even with declared enrichment.
6. If V3 Paper 6 fails, the no-Wilson retained-record branch cannot support a
   coherent multi-taste or possible discovery-channel interpretation.
7. If V3 Paper 7 fails, Lorentz-covariant interacting ISP remains unproved even
   if fixed-foliation interacting benchmarks work.
8. V3 Paper 8 gives a mixed result: enriched finite-battery QFT local-net
   matching succeeds on the declared classes, while Gamma-only and full
   interacting continuum QFT reconstruction remain no-go/open targets.
9. If V3 Paper 9 fails, non-Abelian gauge theory is not yet compatible with
   finite ISP kernel architecture.
10. If V3 Paper 10 fails, non-Abelian ISP may remain finite-cutoff only.
11. If V3 Paper 11 fails, the program may still have finite non-Abelian gauge
    benchmarks, but it has not crossed the local-action continuum Yang-Mills
    gate.
12. If V3 Paper 12 fails, the program has not crossed from smeared
    perturbative Wilson-loop anchors to renormalized unsmeared Wilson-loop
    functionals.
13. If V3 Paper 13 fails, the program has not constructed a nonperturbative
    continuum Yang-Mills functional.
14. If V3 Paper 14 fails, actual continuum `SU(N)` Yang-Mills has not been
    shown to enter the finite-block record domain required by Paper 13.
15. If V3 Paper 15 fails, the program has not proved the connected-polymer,
    surface-subcriticality, and positive-margin gates needed for `RSB`.
16. If V3 Paper 16 fails, the nonperturbative continuum Yang-Mills functional
    remains conditional even if the reduction is precise.
17. If V3 Paper 17 fails, the program has not proved a mass gap.
18. If V3 Paper 18 fails, the program has not proved confinement and has not
    supplied the dynamical `G_j-2PT-KP + MG-UNIF` inputs needed to turn Paper
    17's conditional mass-gap theorem into a complete 4D gauge-theory
    example.
19. If V3 Paper 19 fails, the program has not supplied the actual source
    constants needed by Paper 18's conditional confinement closure. The
    architecture may still be correct, but actual `4D SU(N)` confinement and
    the resulting mass gap remain unproved.
20. If V3 Paper 20 fails, the program has not supplied the actual
    heat-kernel coefficient and loss estimates needed to turn Paper 19's
    conditional direct-witness closure into an unconditional confinement
    theorem on the selected tower. The current Paper-20 endpoint is sharper:
    the selected `SEL2` route is blocked at `P20-SEL2-TREE-RATE-GATE`.
21. If V3 Paper 21 fails, the strict reduced `SEL2` direct-witness route has
    not supplied a tree-rate source strong enough to beat rooted
    surface-polymer growth. This falsifies that route or leaves it conditional;
    it does not falsify every possible confinement strategy.
22. V3 Paper 22 now closes the strict `SEL2` finite-table continuation and
    settles the post-\(F_4\) branch ledger. Branch A is reduced to fixed or
    adaptive source gates; Branch B and Branch C are parked behind new theorem
    packages. Until one surviving source package passes, actual `4D SU(N)`
    confinement and the resulting mass gap remain unproved.
23. V3 Paper 23 is the adaptive Branch-A source campaign. If it fails, the
    large-\(N\), high-\(\alpha\), same-record route has not supplied the
    prefactor/source package needed to close Paper 22's adaptive theorem. This
    falsifies adaptive Branch A, not the Branch-B or Branch-C alternatives.
24. V3 Paper 24 is the full-object RPF dual-certificate campaign. It now
    proves that, in the nontrivial live RPF case, the closed Paper-23 scalar
    body \({\mathcal M}_{56}\) is too large for a closing universal
    full-object certificate. The program must add new actual-law scalar
    information or return to tail sourcing, bridge damping, upstream screened
    conditional influence, or the parked Branch-B/Branch-C routes.
25. V3 Paper 25 is the Branch-A actual-law source and truth-status audit. It
    proves the exact closure implications for direct Dobrushin rows, screened
    shell influence, Peter-Weyl step contraction, Peter-Weyl tail/projection
    control, and bridge damping on the adaptive `SEL2` law. It also proves
    that the current Papers 20--24 supply none of those five sources, do not
    prove the lower-floor theorem needed to falsify adaptive Branch A, and do
    not decide the actual truth value of any of the five options. The active
    obstruction is now genuinely new actual-law numerical, screening,
    spectral, tail, or bridge information.
26. V3 Paper 26 is the actual-law finite-template data extraction,
    atom-value source, primitive residual-source, RN-ratio, and RN-MIXAMP
    campaign.  It proves that a populated finite worksheet would decide all
    five Paper-25 Branch-A gates, imports the Paper-23 formal residual atom
    identity, unwinds the primitive residual density identity, isolates the
    weaker mixed-ratio bypass, identifies the minimal RN ratio with the true
    mixed `CleanRPF`/bridge amplitude table, exhausts structural zeroes, and
    proves `P26-ACTLAW-DATA-GAP`, `P26-ACTATOM-DATA-GAP`,
    `P26-RPF-RESID-SOURCE-GAP`, `P26-SEL2-RN-RATIO-GAP`,
    `P26-SEL2-RN-RATIO-ATTEMPT-GAP`, and
    `P26-RN-MIXAMP-VALUE-GAP`: the current Papers 20--25 do not populate the
    required conditional weights, primitive residual density values, mixed RN
    ratios, actual residual atom values or oscillation bounds, Peter-Weyl
    tails, or bridge amplitudes cofinally, and do not prove the lower floor
    needed to falsify adaptive Branch A. The active obstruction is now the
    RN-MIXAMP trichotomy: smallness, lower floor, or leave adaptive Branch A.
27. V3 Paper 27 executes that RN-MIXAMP trichotomy as far as the current
    corpus permits. It proves that Papers 20--26 do not give a closing
    signed cancellation theorem, a conditional spectral contraction plus
    tail, direct RN-MIXAMP row smallness, or the lower floor
    \(\overline\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}\ge M_*\). Adaptive Branch A remains
    undecided, but the next Branch-A move must be a genuinely new same-law
    value theorem, not another finite-label refinement. Otherwise the
    program should leave adaptive Branch A and return to Branch B/C.
28. V3 Paper 28 executes the most promising Paper-27 continuation,
    spectral contraction plus tail. It proves that the actual same-law
    RN-MIXAMP conditional transfer operator exists at finite cutoff, but
    Papers 20--27 do not supply a strict low-mode spectral gap, finite-band
    support, Peter-Weyl decay, a cofinal tail table, or the combined
    inequality
    \(\Theta^{act}[L]+\kappa^{act}[L]<\theta_{\mathrm{crit}}\). The spectral
    route remains a possible future positive route only if new same-law
    low-mode values and tail values are sourced.
29. V3 Paper 29 executes the low-mode value-extraction attempt and attacks
    the primitive residual value theorem. It proves that the minimal
    fundamental/dual/adjoint low-mode block is the first useful target, but
    also that Paper-26 RN-MIXAMP four-point ratios do not determine its
    transition matrix. Spectral closure now requires actual conditional
    entries, a primitive residual density source, or a same-law Doeblin floor
    plus tail. Paper 29 then defines `P29-PRIMRES-VAL` and proves that the
    current corpus supplies neither direct density values, nor residual
    coefficient row identity, nor same-law polymer values. Part II proves the
    literal atom identity `P29-PRIMRES-ATOM-ID`, shows that clean crossing
    rows alone do not determine conditional kernels, exports
    `P29-PRIMRES-DEFECT-EXPORTED`, and records
    `P29-PRIMRES-ROWID-FULL-GAP`. Part III reduces the remaining positive
    route to defect polymer values or a defect Dobrushin certificate, and the
    opposite falsification route to a defect lower floor; both are unsourced
    by the current corpus. Part IV proves the defect Dobrushin implication
    and closes the current-corpus audit at `P29-PRIMRES-DEFECT-DOB-GAP` and
    `P29-PRIMRES-DEFECT-DOBWIT-GAP`. The most economical Branch-A
    continuation is therefore a genuinely new defect influence/value table, a
    signed/bridge theorem, or the lower-floor theorem.
    The paper-level spectral value-extraction attempt is closed under
    `P29-SPECTRAL-VALUE-EXTRACTION-CLOSED`; more finite labels alone cannot
    alter this verdict.
30. V3 Paper 30 executes the signed/bridge theorem option left by Paper 29.
    It proves that direct signed bridge values, a narrowed-body signed dual
    certificate, bridge damping plus tail, or full-object signed range
    control would close adaptive Branch A under the Paper-23 scalar gates,
    while a lower floor \(\overline\Lambda_{13}^{RPF}\ge M_*\) would falsify
    it after route failure.  It then proves that Papers 20--29 supply none of
    these sources in a closing or falsifying range and that more finite labels
    do not determine the signed bridge values.  Paper 30 also executes the
    first analytic unblock attempt: parent-law pushforward domination,
    log-oscillation pushforward domination, and exact finite DLR localization
    are proved, reducing bridge damping to the strict heat-kernel/tree-gauge
    exponent
    \({1\over2}C_{min}^{br}\tau_{br}^{cof}-\chi_{tilt}^{cof}>g_{br}\),
    plus the common tail budget.  It then freezes the four-account bridge
    worksheet and proves that positive bridge time slope, residual tilt
    control, a Casimir floor, and a sharp bridge entropy table would source
    the bridge route.  The final in-paper screening campaign sharpens this
    further: because the AF-area heat-time window is bounded, the exact
    fixed-\(N\) bridge theorem is the window partition-sum source
    `P30-MIXED-RN-WINDOW(D)` plus the common tail.  Paper 30 proves this
    source would close the route, and proves that Papers 20--29 do not supply
    either the needed time-window bridge partition estimate or the residual
    mixed RN tilt estimate.  It then executes the signed-involution push:
    admissible bridge involutions and HK-symmetric cancellation would reduce
    the signed route to a residual orbit defect, but current recorded
    symmetries do not bound that defect and do not prove the lower-floor
    pivot.  The final Paper-30 pass sharpens the residual-defect value theorem
    into the exact mixed cross-ratio source
    `P30-BRIDGE-INV-XRATIO(C,Omega,kappa)`, closing when
    \(2C+\Omega^2/4<M_{\mathrm{sgn}}(\kappa)\), and proves the three
    same-law routes that would source it: maximal-defect KP,
    involution-defect Dobrushin/activity, or projected low-mode plus tail.
    It also defines the opposite sign-coherent lower-floor witness.  The
    subsequent prove/falsify pass shows all three positive source routes are
    falsified as current-corpus derivations, though not globally falsified as
    future actual-law theorems.  The active obstruction is now a concrete
    same-law value computation.  Paper 30 keeps this inside Branch A by
    defining three actual-law anchors -- `P30-BRANCHA-KP-ANCHOR`,
    `P30-BRANCHA-DOB-ANCHOR`, and `P30-BRANCHA-LOWTAIL-ANCHOR` -- each of
    which defeats the relevant residual-tail countercompletion and closes
    when its numerical margin holds.  Paper 30 then audits those values and
    proves they are neither proven nor falsified by the current corpus; only
    their decidability from the current corpus is falsified.  Paper 30 then
    finds the first actual same-law quantitative extractor: finite-DLR
    range/log-ratio data.  This gives a Dobrushin row envelope, a Möbius
    activity envelope, and exact projected low-mode/tail quantities, but the
    crude range form does not close because small-time heat-kernel range
    diverges, the Dobrushin \(\tanh\)-bound saturates, and range does not
    imply coefficient decay.  The active Branch-A task is therefore to
    sharpen this extractor.  The radical search pass proves the available
    finite identities/implications for score/covariance response, connected
    Möbius/cumulant cancellation, heat-flow Peter-Weyl smoothing plus
    residual tail, Ward/signed bridge cancellation, transport contraction,
    and the lower-floor exit, but all remain unsourced as closing theorems by
    the current corpus.  The active targets are now
    `P30-CONN-MOBIUS`, `P30-SCORE-COV-ROW`,
    `P30-HK-RESID-PWTAIL`, `P30-WARD-BRIDGE`, or
    `P30-RADICAL-FLOOR`.  The path-integral push then rewrites the same
    finite parent DLR law as a Peter-Weyl/spin-foam representation-history
    sum, proves flux selection for projected bridge coefficients, and
    reduces the low-mode/tail route to `P30-SPINFOAM-TAIL(r_L)` plus
    high-charge area, residual insertion decay, signed/intertwiner
    cancellation, and denominator control.  It then sharpens this into
    `P30-NONABELIAN-SWITCHING(delta,u)`, whose primitive subgates are
    residual quasi-invariance, switch neutrality, switch-area/unpaired-sector
    control, and insertion of the resulting \(\delta,u\) into the signed
    high-charge tail bound.  The minimal-corridor audit shows termwise
    neutrality is not generic and replaces it with the finite block theorem
    `P30-BLOCK-SWITCH(theta,u)`; otherwise return to Paper-29 defect
    value/influence or exit adaptive Branch A.

## What Not To Claim In V3

Do not claim full continuum QFT from finite kernel examples.

Do not claim non-Abelian Yang-Mills from a finite group or finite representation cutoff alone.

Do not claim Lorentz covariance from projective compatibility alone; foliation/path equivalence is a separate theorem.

Do not claim exact Lorentz covariance at finite lattice spacing from the V2
Route-B boost theorem. V2 Paper 9 proves sampled regulator convergence, not an
exact finite-regulator Poincare symmetry.

Do not identify raw comparison maps with observables.

Do not hide inverse-control assumptions.

Do not treat enriched free-QFT matching as Gamma-only reconstruction.

Do not treat the V2 Paper 10 metric-data gate as stress-energy, dynamical
geometry, or gravity.

Do not claim full signed metric reconstruction from bare Born-squared `Gamma`;
V2 Paper 10 gives an all-order sign-ambiguity obstruction for the present rule.

Do not treat Clifford/principal-symbol recovery of metric data as Gamma-level
recovery. It is enriched-representation recovery.

Do not move to gravity until QFT and non-Abelian gauge status are clear.

## Recommended Immediate Work

The best immediate V3-starting paper is not non-Abelian gauge theory yet. It is:

`Minimal Enriched ISP Data for Relativistic QFT Reconstruction`

Reason: V2 Papers 6-10 prove, in different ways, that `Gamma` alone does not
carry enough data for QFT, metric orientation, or local observables. V3 must
state exactly what extra data are admitted before it tries to reconstruct
relativistic QFT.

The second immediate paper should be:

`Primitive Smooth-Lapse Hypersurface Kernels in Relativistic ISP`

Reason: it replaces the log-smeared V2 finite-slab theorem with a more physical
finite-slab construction. That upgrade is needed before claiming serious
interacting Lorentz covariance. V2 Paper 9 already handles the free sampled
Lorentz benchmark; V3 should now improve the primitive deformation mechanism
that interactions will need.

The third immediate paper should be:

`Interacting Projective Kernel Dynamics and Comparison-Map Inverse Control`

Reason: all three north-star goals need inverse control and projective error propagation.

Non-Abelian gauge theory should begin after these first gates, unless the goal
is explicitly a fixed finite benchmark paper.

The first V3 paper should carry the V2 enrichment ledger in its introduction:

```text
Gamma-level data, operational instruments, Hilbert/CAR lifts, and metric
coefficients are distinct layers.
```

That single ledger prevents V3 from backsliding into the two mistakes V2 worked
hard to isolate: Markovizing unrecorded subprocesses and treating QFT
representational data as if it were already present in bare endpoint kernels.

## Bottom Line

V3 should push hard toward the three goals, but with sharp staging:

```text
minimal enriched ISP data
-> primitive smooth-lapse kernels
-> interacting projective inverse control
-> interacting stochastic curvature
-> projective operational local nets
-> interacting Lorentz covariance / foliation independence
-> enriched QFT reconstruction or no-go
-> finite non-Abelian gauge benchmark
-> projective non-Abelian cutoff/refinement limits
-> continuum Yang-Mills RG closure
-> renormalized unsmeared Wilson loops
-> nonperturbative continuum Yang-Mills
-> finite-block actual-Yang-Mills entry gates
-> connected-polymer KP and surface subcriticality
-> nonperturbative continuum Yang-Mills closure
-> mass gap gates
-> confinement gates
-> actual source constants and heat-kernel coefficient ledgers
-> SEL2 tree-rate/source finite-table audit
-> continuum Yang-Mills confinement continuation: common inverse/admissibility,
   comparison source rows, licensed pass graph, and finite-depth reduced-tail
   closure on the strict row-complete envelope branch
-> post-Work-III tree-rate worksheet: TREE-TIME selector-time trichotomy and
   ESC-MASS cofinal escape-ceiling/near-maximal anti-concentration source
-> Paper-22 branch ledger: F4 escape falsification, Branch-A source reduction,
   Branch-B surface theorem audit, Branch-C signed/selector audit
-> Paper-23 adaptive Branch-A source campaign:
   XIPLOG + AREA + RP/Cov margin + RPF margin on the same high-alpha large-N law
-> Paper-24 full-object RPF dual certificate campaign:
   closed-body witness verdict for the full normalized minimal-edge signed range
-> Paper-25 Branch-A actual-law source and truth-status audit:
   Dobrushin/screening/step/tail/bridge positive closure theorems and
   current-corpus undecidability verdict for the adaptive `SEL2` law
-> Paper-26 actual-law finite-template data extraction, atom-value source,
   primitive residual-source ledger, and RN-ratio bypass:
   finite worksheet theorem, formal atom/value-population split, residual
   density identity, and `P26-ACTLAW-DATA-GAP` + `P26-ACTATOM-DATA-GAP` +
   `P26-RPF-RESID-SOURCE-GAP` + `P26-SEL2-RN-RATIO-GAP` +
   `P26-SEL2-RN-RATIO-ATTEMPT-GAP` for the adaptive `SEL2` law; exported
   RN-MIXAMP trichotomy and `P26-RN-MIXAMP-VALUE-GAP`
-> Paper-27 actual-law RN-MIXAMP smallness or lower-floor campaign:
   frozen weighted mixed RN row; signed cancellation gap; conditional
   spectral contraction gap; direct RN-MIXAMP smallness gap; lower-floor gap;
   exported requirement for a genuinely new same-law value theorem or exit
   from adaptive Branch A
-> Paper-28 RN-MIXAMP spectral contraction plus tail campaign:
   actual same-law conditional transfer operator; finite low-mode block;
   Markov/oscillation non-expansion bound; same-law Peter-Weyl tail audit; combined
   spectral-tail margin gap
-> Paper-29 RN-MIXAMP low-mode value extraction:
   minimal fundamental/dual/adjoint battery; literal low-mode entry formula
   from \(H_{RPF}^{N,j}\); RN-ratio non-recovery theorem; low-entry, low-gap,
   Doeblin, spectral-value, direct primitive residual, row-identity, and
   polymer-value gaps; primitive atom identity; full-row identity gap;
   exported defect-polymer target; defect-polymer and defect-floor gaps;
   defect Dobrushin and defect-witness gaps; paper-level closure
   `P29-SPECTRAL-VALUE-EXTRACTION-CLOSED`; pivot to signed/bridge amplitude
   control unless a new defect influence/value theorem is found
-> Paper-30 actual-law signed/bridge amplitude or floor campaign:
   actual signed true-bridge Hamiltonian; signed range and one-line width;
   Paper-23 signed scalar gate; direct signed-value gap; narrowed-body dual
   gap; bridge-damping-plus-tail gap; full no-tail signed range gap;
   lower-floor gap; label no-go; current-corpus closure of the signed/bridge
   channel; parent-law pushforward domination; exact finite DLR localization;
   log-oscillation pushforward domination; tree-gauge heat-kernel bridge
   exponent test
   \(m_{HK}^{eff}={1\over2}C_{min}^{br}\tau_{br}^{cof}
   -\chi_{tilt}^{cof}>g_{br}\); heat-kernel bridge/sign gaps; sharp
   residual-defect cross-ratio source `P30-BRIDGE-INV-XRATIO`; maximal
   involution-defect KP, Dobrushin/activity, low-mode-plus-tail, and
   sign-coherent witness routes; current-corpus residual-defect source gaps;
   three positive residual-defect source routes falsified as current-corpus
   derivations but not globally falsified as actual-law theorems; Branch-A
   overcoming anchors `KP-ANCHOR`, `DOB-ANCHOR`, and `LOWTAIL-ANCHOR`;
   anchor values audited as not proven, not falsified, and not decidable from
   the current corpus; first same-law quantitative extractor via finite-DLR
   range/log-ratio envelopes, with Dobrushin row, Möbius activity, and
   projected coefficient-tail quantities; crude range extractor does not
   close without cancellation, small boundary log-ratio rows, or Peter-Weyl
   coefficient decay; radical same-law search pass reduces the next live
   theorems to `P30-CONN-MOBIUS`, `P30-SCORE-COV-ROW`,
   `P30-HK-RESID-PWTAIL`, `P30-WARD-BRIDGE`, or `P30-RADICAL-FLOOR`;
   path-integral/spin-foam push gives exact same-law representation
   histories, flux selection, and the new concrete tail target
   `P30-SPINFOAM-TAIL(r_L)`; nonabelian switching push gives the sharper
   structural target `P30-NONABELIAN-SWITCHING(delta,u)` with residual
   quasi-invariance, switch neutrality, switch area, and unpaired-sector
   debits; minimal-corridor audit replaces termwise neutrality by the block
   target `P30-BLOCK-SWITCH(theta,u)`; universal two-channel block table
   reduces the next subgate to `P30-BLOCK-EVEN-SMALL(theta)`; full-block
   heat-bad audit reduces the live branch to the actual same-law matrix
   \(P_{bad}^{HK}(DR\Sigma+U^*DR\Sigma U)\); source-response reframing turns
   its trace-norm debit into a supremum of first derivatives of same-law
   source pressures
-> Paper-31 same-law source-response calculus:
   derivative dictionary for values, covariances, mixed influence rows,

   and source-slope floor witnesses; exports the calculus back to Paper-30

   bridge residual tilt, and tail obstructions; closes the source-response

   confinement
-> Paper-32 heat-bad source neutrality, curvature, or floor:
   attacks the narrowest primitive input after Paper 31; proves the
   switch-pressure reduction \(V_Q=V_Q^{odd}+V_Q^{even}\), exact pressure
   evenness for switch-odd sources, the even-defect neutrality bound, and the
   debit \(\epsilon+\chi a/2\) from even defect plus curvature; audits
   universal curvature, same-law Poincare/log-Sobolev, Ward-Stein,
   Peter-Weyl low/tail regularity, direct response, and sign-coherent floor;
   second pass replaces exact switch law by switch quasi-invariance and the
   optimized debit \(\epsilon+\sqrt{\omega\chi}\), prints the exact
   signed/residual/heat product decomposition, and isolates
   `P32-HKBAD-SWQI`, `P32-HKBAD-PRODTHIN`, and `P32-HKBAD-EVENRESP` as the
   next primitive same-law inputs; third pass reduces `SWQI` to the exact
   finite DLR switch-Hamiltonian oscillation \(\Omega_{SW}^{DLR}\), compares
   product thinness with the nondegenerate heat-bad product term, and prints
   the response-only and product-floor alternatives; fourth pass proves that
   heat-bad `SWQI` needs counter-tilt rather than residual neutrality, splits
   product thinness by heat-mismatch null sectors, and isolates the

   anti-heat residual atom equation and isolates the compatibility theorem

   \(d_{prod}^{N,j}(\omega)\le\tau\), with product visibility plus sign

   `P32-HKBAD-QDIST-UP` and `P32-HKBAD-QDIST-DUAL-FLOOR`; eighth pass proves
   that the structural rowprint is sourced and reduces the remaining positive
   theorem to `P32-HKBAD-QRESP`, a source-response theorem for only the finite
   polar tests used by the certificate search; ninth pass attacks `QRESP`
   and reduces it to polar switch-oddness plus curvature, a polar Ward route,
   or a polar floor witness; tenth pass explores all three polar routes and
   proves their exact implication/floor criteria while recording that none is
   sourced by the current corpus; eleventh pass instantiates the smallest
   nontrivial singlet-adjoint block and proves that all three routes reduce
   to the actual \(2\times2\) same-law product
   \(B_{\Gamma_1}^{N,j}=R_{\Gamma_1}^{N,j}\Sigma_{\Gamma_1}^{N,j}\), via

   \(m,t\) through
   \(\Pi_+^{U_N}(D_{\Gamma_1}^{HK}B_{\Gamma_1}^{N,j})=(mI_2+tU_N)/2\) and
   proves that ordinary gauge/Haar Ward identities alone do not source them;
   thirteenth pass defines the two-scalar source pressure, proves the
   centering-involution implication, rules out crossing, gauge/Haar, and
   selector relabeling as current-corpus centerings, and prints the exact
   floor candidates \(m,t,\lambda_+,\lambda_-\); fourteenth pass attacks
   same-law Peter-Weyl regularity/tail, proves Sobolev and analytic
   sufficient criteria, isolates residual multiplier tameness as the transfer
   theorem needed to use clean heat damping, and proves that heat-kernel
   smoothness alone does not control actual residual tails; fifteenth pass
   proves the six-gate transfer theorem and audits Sobolev regularity,
   multiplier tameness, normalizer lower bounds, projection commutator
   decay, residual-score regularity, and high-mode floor as valid but
   unsourced primitive inputs; sixteenth pass defines local
   source-Dobrushin rows for the live observable family, proves the
   conditional Neumann response bound, proves the linear-plus-curvature
   upgrade, audits finite-DLR log-ratio envelopes, and prints the floor
   alternative as the exact remaining fork; seventeenth pass attacks mixed
   RN-MIXAMP Ward/curvature by printing the finite same-law Ward identity,
   proving conditional closures from Ward span plus Ward-score defect or
   Ward base plus residual-tilt curvature, identifying the curvature as a
   connected third source cumulant, and printing the mixed Ward floor route;
   eighteenth pass attacks connected source-cumulant decay, proves that
   defect source-KP would source the defect-polymer theorem and primitive
   residual values, records projection exports to RN-MIXAMP/Dobrushin/
   Peter-Weyl routes, audits moment-cumulant, clean-KP, and defect-Dobrushin

   records the post-menu attack plan, defines the joint Ward/Stein live
   quotient and range distance, proves range-plus-defect closure and dual
   separation, and executes the first subtest by discarding pure gauge/Haar
   Ward range for the scalar live classes; twentieth pass defines the
   residual/selector coordinate map and Jacobian, proves selector-only
   directions have zero live Jacobian, proves residual range plus residual
   score-defect would close the joint route, and audits rank, defect, and dual
   floor as unsourced; twenty-first pass executes the five-step residual-range
   worksheet, proves scalar rank is two in the block-entry envelope, defines
   `P32-RN-BLKDER(L)`, and reduces scalar closure to
   `P32-SCAL-RESDEFECT(delta)`; twenty-second pass attacks
   `P32-RN-BLKDER(L)` and proves it requires the sharper finite fork
   `P32-BLKFIELD-ADM + P32-RN-BETA-FACTOR`, or else
   `P32-RN-KERSEP` sending the problem back to the full residual Jacobian;
   twenty-third pass reduces scalar admissibility from four block directions
   to the two scalar directions \(m,t\), defining `P32-SCALFIELD-ADM` and its
   two possible sources `P32-SCAL-CONFJAC` or `P32-SCAL-SRCMAT`;
   twenty-fourth pass closes `P32-SCAL-CONFJAC` at current-corpus level and
   reduces the remaining scalar source route to `P32-SCAL-SRC-RANK` plus
   `P32-SCAL-SRC-CURV`; twenty-fifth pass reduces scalar source rank to the
   explicit determinant gate `P32-SCAL-SRC-DET(A,B;Delta,M_C)` or the
   negative gate `P32-SCAL-SRC-RANK-GAP` plus scalar floor; twenty-sixth
   pass reframes scalar rank by structural source tomography and reduces the
   compact positive target to
   `P32-SCAL-STRUCTSRC-COUPLE + P32-SCAL-STRUCTSRC-GRAM`, with
   rigidity/floor as the negative exit;
   closes the current-corpus heat-bad source campaign by showing that the
   missing input is `MINPOL-MTABLE`, a new non-gauge Ward/centering theorem
   for \(m,t\), a floor witness for \(m,t,\lambda_+,\lambda_-\), or actual
   Peter-Weyl regularity/multiplier/normalizer/commutator/score/floor input,
   local source-Dobrushin response/curvature/DLR/floor input, or mixed
   RN-MIXAMP Ward-span/Ward-defect/tilt-curvature/floor input, or connected
   source-KP/projection/floor input, or joint residual/selector
   Ward/Stein-range/score-defect/dual-floor input, not further bookkeeping;
   Paper 33 then turns the endpoint into a same-law bootstrap and proves
   that ordinary positivity plus the existing constraints still allow the
   scalar ray \(B=cI_2\), so the next active theorem must cut or orient that
   ray by residual-score, structural-coupling/Gram, non-gauge Ward/Stein,

   component package `P33-RES-HESS + P33-JAC-HESS + P33-SEL-CURV +

-> Paper-34 reflection-positive moment bootstrap:
   finite RP/SOS certificates are sound and same-law, but passive RP

-> Paper-35 scalar-ray detector theorem:
   any proposed Branch-A constraint is tested by its trace on \(B=cI_2\);
   passive deterministic-character constraints are ray-blind, covering

   formal block-entry Ward-Stein certificates for \(m,t\) exist and have
   scalar-ray coefficients \(A_m=h_0+h_A\), \(A_t=a_N(h_0-h_A)\); the route
   closes only after actual scalar-field admissibility, an actual nonzero
   ray coefficient, and residual/selector score-defect control in the same
   adaptive record law; pure gauge/Haar, selector-only, endpoint-additive,

   gives only a dual candidate unless `P36-WS-DUALSIGN(M_*)` supplies the

-> Paper-37 actual scalar-field admissibility or kernel floor:
   the actual scalar map must be a pointwise same-law lift
   \(s_{act}=(m_{\Gamma_1}^{pt},t_{\Gamma_1}^{pt})\), with Jacobian
   \(G_{act}^{scal}=D_\theta s_{act}\); admissibility is exactly
   `P37-SCAL-POINTLIFT + P37-SCAL-JACRANK + P37-SCAL-SCOREENV`;
   current corpus does not source atom-value or group-coordinate lifts,
   free scalar coordinates are forbidden, and the actual-coordinate route
   either reduces Paper 36 to score defect or needs `P37-SCAL-KERFLOOR(M_*)`;
   the same paper then executes the structural source-response pivot:
   `P37-STRUCTSRC-COUPLE + P37-STRUCTSRC-GRAM + P37-STRUCTSRC-CURV` is the
   positive source route, `P37-STRUCTSRC-RIGIDFLOOR` is the negative exit,
   clean heat/channel sources are ray-blind, and none of these primitive
   structural value inputs is sourced by the current corpus
-> later synthesis: QFT reconstruction, representation layer, or obstruction
```

If V3 succeeds strongly, relativistic ISP will no longer be merely a finite benchmark framework. It will have a controlled interacting projective dynamics, a serious interface with continuum QFT, and a finite-to-projective non-Abelian gauge program. That still may not equal full continuum QFT or full Yang-Mills, but it would be the strongest credible route toward them.
